{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"Skoda axes Citigo city car","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/skoda-axes-citigo-city-car","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/skoda-axes-citigo-city-car\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/1-skoda-citigo-e-iv-2020-uk-fd-hero-front_1_0.jpg?itok=6YT-E9a3\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"Skoda Citigo-e IV\" title=\"Skoda Citigo-e IV\" /></a>\n<blockquote class=\"image-field-caption\">\n  The new Citigo-e iV (pictured above) has already sold out in the UK\n</blockquote> The Citigo, in both combustion-engined and electric variants, is no more and will not be replaced \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>The <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/skoda/citigo-2012-2019\">Skoda Citigo</a> is officially no more, as the Czech maker&nbsp;focuses its efforts on larger models and electrification.</p> \n <p>The future of the city car, which is a sibling of the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/up\">Volkswagen Up</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/seat/mii-2012-2019\">Seat Mii</a>, has long been in question, but <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/skoda\">Skoda</a> sales and marketing boss Alain Favey has now confirmed it will not return.</p> \n <p>He said: “Citigo is gone - as far as Europe is concerned we are sold out. There will not be a replacement of the Citigo and we have no intention to have a car of this size in the future.”</p> \n <p>The combustion-engined Citigo went <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-skoda-citigo-e-iv-cost-%C2%A316955-uk\">off sale in late 2019 in the UK</a>, but the model continued with the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/skoda/citigo-e-iv\">electric Citigo-e iV</a>. The zero-emissions model went on sale in early spring, and the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/skoda-citigo-e-iv-withdrawn-sale-due-high-demand\">UK’s 400-unit allocation quickly sold out</a>. Customer deliveries will be complete by the end of this year, said a Skoda UK spokesman.</p> \n <p>A new, small electric car, which could potentially succeed&nbsp;the Citigo, is not currently on the table, said Favey. “If one day there is a version of the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/audi-lead-volkswagen-group-rd-efforts\">Volkswagen Group’s</a> [electric] MEB platform which allows smaller cars to be produced [than now], we would have a Skoda version, but I don’t know about such plans. But as far as the Citigo is concerned, the game is over.”</p> \n <p>Skoda this week revealed its <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/skoda-enyaq-iv-revealed-first-bespoke-ev-316-mile-range\">first stand-alone EV, the Enyaq</a>, built on VW’s MEB platform. Favey said that this model, alongside the existing Superb plug-in hybrid and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/next-skoda-octavia-vrs-go-hybrid\">upcoming Octavia plug-in hybrid</a>, would allow the brand to capitalise on the growing demand for electrified models.</p> \n <p>However, smaller Skoda models&nbsp;will not receive electrified versions for the foreseeable future, as the costly technology would make such cars unattainable for customers, Favey said.</p> \n <p>Talking about the possibility of plug-in hybrid options, he commented: “It’s disputable if it’s a good idea to have a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/skoda/scala\">Scala</a> PHEV. It’s a technology which is still extremely expensive - you need to find a customer base which has the buying power to afford that technology, or we have to lose money which is not an option for us.”</p> \n <p>Favey also said&nbsp;that there were no solid plans for Skoda’s next EV following the Enyaq, and&nbsp;that Skoda was closely watching EV demand. He added that the flexibility of VW’s MEB platform meant that development times of future EVs&nbsp;could be much quicker than traditional combustion-engined cars.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/skoda-citigo-e-iv-withdrawn-sale-due-high-demand\">Skoda Citigo-e iV withdrawn from sale due to high demand</a></strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/skoda-enyaq-iv-revealed-first-bespoke-ev-316-mile-range\">Skoda Enyaq iV revealed as first bespoke EV with 316-mile range</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/used-cars/nearly-new-buying-guide-skoda-karoq\">Nearly new buying guide: Skoda +0000","feedId":13379,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"2f9cb468126d158797217fd134aa16f2","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/1-skoda-citigo-e-iv-2020-uk-fd-hero-front_1_0.jpg?itok=6YT-E9a3":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn6@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-50-47-305_20738251c301ced3.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295843550},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 Indianapolis","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/opinion/motorsport/racing-lines-alonso-down-not-done-indianapolis","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/opinion/motorsport/racing-lines-alonso-down-not-done-indianapolis\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/20-alonso-indy-500.jpg?itok=LMeuLJTS\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"Alonso Indy 500\" title=\"Alonso Indy 500\" /></a>\n<blockquote class=\"image-field-caption\">\n  Alonso qualified on the ninth row and limped home 21st\n</blockquote> F1 legend again fell flat at the Indy 500 – but he’s far from ready to call it a day \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>The Indianapolis 500 is like a Beach Boys surfing song: so infectious and exuberant that you can’t help tapping along and more American than Tom Hanks eating apple pie on the 4th of July.</p> \n <p>Like just about everything in this screwed-up year, the 2020 edition carried a misfire, running to empty grandstands in August rather than before a quarter of a million people on its usual Memorial Day slot at the end of May. But even so, it’s the Indy 500, baby! Takuma Sato still poured the traditional quart of milk over his head with abandon, as the only Japanese driver to have won the famous race added a second victory to his historic first from 2017.</p> \n <p>Fernando Alonso rolled in a lowly and clutchless 21st, having qualified only 26th of 33. The two-time Formula 1 champion’s quest to complete motorsport’s unofficial triple crown of glory – the Monaco Grand Prix, the 24 Hours of Le Mans and the Indy 500 – remains unfulfilled. It was better than last year, when he didn’t even qualify, but it was no great surprise, given that his Arrow <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/how-mclaren-making-comeback-f1\">McLaren SP </a>had a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/chevrolet\">Chevrolet</a> engine when a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/honda\">Honda</a> was the thing to have.</p> \n <p>That’s what powered him on his unforgettable debut in 2017, when he was among the leading pack in the closing stages only for it to blow. Since then, Honda has vetoed Alonso due to the uncharitable things he had to say about its hybrid engines when they were powering his uncompetitive F1 <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mclaren\">McLarens</a> a few years ago. It’s another bridge burned in a career that has been great but could have been much more so.</p> \n <p><strong>Old-school star power</strong></p> \n <p>Alonso will return to F1 in 2021 – in the year that he turns 40 – for a third spell with <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/renault\">Renault</a>. This was the best seat that he could land when <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mercedes-benz\">Mercedes</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/aston-martin-and-red-bull-plan-more-incredible-products-under-new-deal\">Red Bull</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/ferrari\">Ferrari</a> (for whom he drove between 2010 and 2014) remained resolute in keeping the door shut to him. How he fares will likely revolve around what Renault can give him, rather than his age, but we will see.</p> \n <p>What he will certainly bring is that old star power, the kind that has made him loved at Indy. Alonso is old-school in that respect, as is his attitude to racing. Frozen out of competitive F1 drives with no one to blame but himself, he has chosen a refreshing path to light up the World Endurance Championship and Le Mans (which he has won twice), the Daytona 24 Hours (conquered in 2019) and even the Dakar Rally this year, on which he belied his lack of off-road experience to earn respect, if not stage wins.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/19-alonso-indy-500.jpg?itok=guvwQuYe\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Will he return to Indy for another crack at the quest? Not in the next two years, if all goes to plan at Renault. But AJ Foyt and Mario Andretti raced at the 500 well into their 50s, and while modern aerodynamics make racing more demanding now than it used to be, Alonso is made from the same stuff. He will go back. One day.</p> \n <p><strong>Bittersweet for Williams</strong></p> \n <p>I can’t help having mixed feelings about <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motorsport/exclusive-williams-f1-team-outlines-bold-recovery-plan\">Williams</a> succeeding in its quest to find a new owner. The priority was to save the beleaguered F1 team, and the deal with American private investment firm Dorilton Capital certainly hits that spot. But for Frank Williams not to own an F1 team, as he has since 1969, just feels off. As with Tyrrell in the late 1990s, such a move was inevitable; Williams hasn’t been a good F1 team for a long time. And, unlike with Tyrrell, this deal at least guarantees the Williams name will stay on the grid. But for how long?</p> \n <p>Changing an F1 team’s name isn’t easy, due to the binding financial contracts they all sign to be a part of grand prix racing. Williams, like the rest of the grid, has just signed up to a new so-called Concorde Agreement to ensure its continued presence in F1, and it’s no coincidence that the Dorilton deal followed quickly in its wake. It also means the Williams family will have been able to negotiate top price.</p> \n <p>But now the team is out of their hands, all bets are off about its future shape and guise. How long will these investors want to own an F1 team? Could it be sold again, to a Lawrence Stroll type or even a car manufacturer? Do they really give a damn about motor racing? All we know for sure is that from now on, even if the name above the garage doors remains familiar, it’s not Williams as we’ve known it.</p> \n <p><strong>Colin Turkington shows his class</strong></p> \n <p>Three meetings in four weeks, nine races and six winners for five makes of car. The breathless <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motorsport/btcc-announces-new-27-race-calendar-begin-august\">British Touring Car Championship (BTCC)</a> is as frenetic as ever – and by the time you read this, another weekend of action will have passed at Knockhill. But after Oulton Park, who sat atop the points standings? <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motorsport/autocar-awards-2020-colin-turkington-wins-motorsport-hero\">Colin Turkington,</a> of course. Who else?</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/18-colin-turkington.jpg?itok=AHUZE8pO\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The Northern Irishman is chasing a record fifth title in his Team <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/3-series\">BMW 3 Series</a> and has already won twice this season. But as much as he enjoys winning races, he knows that victories aren’t always the priority. In a series that throws in reverse grids and weight penalties for success, the only way to become champion is to pick your way through a season and keep your points tally consistently ticking over. Turkington didn’t win any races at Oulton, but he still left with an increased lead.</p> \n <p>That’s why he’s a four-time champion. Turkington knows better than anyone that nothing is guaranteed, that luck might play a part, just as it did in his favour last year. But he’s still the BTCC’s most rounded contender. If anyone is going to beat him to the 2020 crown, they’ll need to be at their very best.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motorsport/official-fernando-alonso-return-f1-renault-2021\">Official: Fernando Alonso to return to F1 with Renault in 2021</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"Iconic Volvo P1800 reborn as 414bhp continuation special","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/iconic-volvo-p1800-reborn-414bhp-continuation-special","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/iconic-volvo-p1800-reborn-414bhp-continuation-special\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/p1800cyan_5.jpg?itok=zy_reumF\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"Volvo P1800 Cyan\" title=\"Volvo P1800 Cyan\" /></a> Cyan Racing gives 1960s coupé race-bred turbo engine, lightweight chassis and hardcore suspension \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>Geely’s motorsport arm,&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/lynkco-03-cyan-concept-fastest-four-door-nurburgring\">Cyan Racing,&nbsp;</a>has unveiled the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/fine-balance-meeting-car-technicians-blending-old-skills-new\">Volvo P1800</a> Cyan as a modernised, uprated take on its sibling brand's iconic 1960s sports coupé.</p> \n <p>The continuation car was designed as a road-legal version of an imagined Cyan Racing track car from the 1960s, and as such goes without modern driving aids such as stability control, anti-lock brakes or brake boosting.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>It has, however, been comprehensively re-engineered to offer significantly enhanced performance, dynamics and drivability. The original car’s naturally aspirated four-cylinder engine, for example, has been swapped out for the turbocharged 2.0-litre unit used in Cyan Racing’s 2017 <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volvo/s60\">Volvo S60</a> TC1 racer, which revs to 7700rpm and gives the P1800 a substantially increased 414bhp&nbsp;and 336lb ft.</p> \n <p>To preserve some of the original car’s driving experience, the engine has been tuned to offer linear power and torque delivery, which Cyan claims are “the characteristics of a normally aspirated engine”, while still giving increased performance and precision.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/p1800cyan_12.jpg?itok=dYicKeMA\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>A range of engines were considered for use in the P1800 Cyan, including Volvo’s revered Red Block&nbsp;and five-cylinder turbo motors, but Cyan chose the newer VEA&nbsp;motor because it's familiar from the team's motorsport efforts.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The engine&nbsp;is mated to a bespoke five-speed gearbox from race engineering firm Holinger, which is said to give the same “mechanical feeling” as the original unit while offering more precise changes and durability. Power is still sent to the rear wheels, but the P1800’s live axle has made way for a bespoke independent rear suspension set-up that, like the front end, is fully adjustable.</p> \n <p>A limited-slip differential with torque-biasing functionality has also been fitted, with a gearing set-up that combines capable circuit performance with \"civilised\"&nbsp;on-road behaviour.</p> \n <p>To accommodate the enhancements, the P1800’s greenhouse has been repositioned, its track widened and its body reinforced with high-strength steel.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Its underpinnings have also been overhauled with a focus on engagement and lightness. The hydraulic suspension at each end comprises aluminium uprights, double wishbones and two-way adjustable dampers, while carbonfibre chassis reinforcements add stiffness with minimal weight penalty.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/p1800cyan_10.jpg?itok=f9awRkAe\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Overall, the continuation car tips the scales at just 990kg –&nbsp;around 150kg less than the&nbsp;original P1800.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The P1800 Cyan sits atop a set of 18in forged rims wrapped in Pirelli P Zero performance tyres, which cover a set of sizeable steel brake discs and four-piston callipers.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Cyan benchmarked its new creation against the 2010&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volvo/c30/first-drives/volvo-c30-polestar-concept\">Volvo C30 Polestar Performance Protoype</a>, its first road-going car. Head of engineering Mattias Evensson said Cyan wanted to “reconnect” with its first road car, as well as “carry over some of the driving feeling and performance availability”.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Cyan CEO Christian Dahl said: “Our company was founded in 1996 to race Volvo cars in Sweden, and the Volvo P1800 Cyan is closing the circle for us.&nbsp;“We claimed our first world title with Volvo in 2017 and have since then won two further world titles with two other manufacturers. The first world title was a milestone for us, and we felt it was a good time to reconnect with the past and to those before us racing Volvos. The first Volvo P1800 Cyan carries our blue and yellow racing colours to mark our heritage.”</p> \n <p>The P1800 Cyan will be marketed independently by Cyan, with production set to be extremely limited. Prices start at $500,000 (£379,000).&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Cyan Racing, which previously operated as Volvo’s Polestar performance division, has won the World Touring Car Championship for the past&nbsp;three years in a row, most recently in 2019 with the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/lynkco-03-cyan-concept-fastest-four-door-nurburgring\">Lynk&amp;Co 03</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n four-door at Nurburgring​</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volvo/c30/first-drives/volvo-c30-polestar-concept\"><strong>Volvo C30 Polestar concept it","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/opinion/new-cars/steve-cropley-if-post-opulence-ill-take-it","description":"<a alt=\"Rolls Royce Ghost camo\" title=\"Rolls Royce Ghost camo\" /></a> Our man enjoys a socially distanced visit to Rolls Royce HQ this week, and says hello to a new long-term test car \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>One of the few upsides of the pandemic is that when you visit a car firm’s headquarters, you’re now usually part of a small group.</p> \n <p>At <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/rolls-royce\">Rolls-Royce</a> in Goodwood for the unveiling of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-rolls-royce-ghost-acoustic-tuning-boost-luxury-feel\">the new Ghost</a>, the group comprised one person – me – which made the walk-around, the assembly plant visit and the prototype ride especially enjoyable. My hosts were designer Henry Cloke and project chief Jon Simms, who added evidence to my previous recent impressions that Rolls-Royce is nowadays populated by young people, not the venerable set you might once have expected.</p> \n <p>There’s plenty to tell about this all-encompassing Ghost project, but I was especially fascinated by the way the acoustics team has “tuned” every important Ghost component so that all of the natural resonances add up to a sound the occupants hear as an unobtrusive, unified whisper. We proved the matter on the move, too. The<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/rolls-royce/phantom\"> latest Phantom</a> is still a shade quieter than the Ghost, they say, but there’s now very little in it. If this is ‘post-opulence’, I’ll take it.</p> \n <p><strong>Saturday</strong></p> \n <p>On the way home from Rolls-Royce, I collected my new long-termer, a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/2-series-gran-coupe/first-drives/bmw-2-series-gran-coupe-m235i-2020-uk-review\">BMW M235i Gran Coupé xDrive</a>, complete with a 302bhp 2.0-litre turbo engine, an eight-speed paddle-shift gearbox, a slippery diff and front drive most of the time.</p> \n <p>In our initial review, this car wasn’t given an excessively good time for its styling (I don’t mind it), its somewhat aggressive ride quality (true, but I like strong body control) and especially its lack of six in-line cylinders and rear drive. It has a British-built transverse four that drives the rear wheels only in times of extreme slippage.</p> \n <p>On the evidence of 100 miles, I completely agree with our bottom-line description of this hot four-door 2 Series: effective. And although I’m not a naturally quick driver, I’m enjoying having a car with 4.9sec 0-62mph potential that naturally does its best when pressing on a bit. Everyone needs a bit of this in their lives.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/bmw_2_series_gran_coupe_m235i.jpg?itok=U4v-hXzY\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p><strong>Sunday</strong></p> \n <p>I was messing about at my local airfield when a bloke I hadn’t seen for years pitched up in <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/slideshow/mg-celebrating-birthday-british-legend\">a fit-looking, rubber-bumpered MG B</a>. We had a cheery, socially distanced chat, during which he explained that the car had been bought via eBay by his wife. He had spent so long dithering on the laptop that, in exasperation, she reached over his shoulder and clicked ‘buy’.</p> \n <p>We borrowed some disinfectant from the aero club to spruce the car and I had a little drive on one of the taxiways, confirming what we both already knew: that a 1970s B feels somewhat baggy next to <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mazda/mx-5\">my Mazda MX-5</a> but is still a surprisingly worthy machine.</p> \n <p>I was really surprised how good the bumpers looked; they’re proper period pieces now. So many have been converted to chrome front ends that a bounce-back B now looks special. Who’d have thought it, back when we all despaired over the antics of British Leyland’s tin-eared bosses?</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/mg_b_gt.jpg?itok=I7epWVIh\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p><strong>Monday</strong></p> \n <p>Thinking of buying a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/porsche\">Porsche</a> or a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mclaren\">McLaren</a>? Friends in the trade suggest that you watch the market for three-year-old cars closely from now on, as PCP deals end on cars that might normally have been bought by their owners post-lease and they come onto the market. The choice is already pretty good, they say, and it will only get better.</p> \n <p><strong>Tuesday</strong></p> \n <p>I’m off work this week, which means it’s time for a busman’s holiday. The Steering Committee and I have so missed the Festival of Speed and Revival events that have come to play such a large parts in all our lives that we’ve booked a short stay at the Goodwood Hotel, just to wander about and reminisce. It’s our first trip since the last Revival, almost exactly 12 months ago. It seems longer.</p> \n <p><strong>And another thing...</strong></p> \n <p>I’m amused to hear that new <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/aston-martin\">Aston Martin</a> chief Tobias Moers, to whom I wrote an open letter suggesting a number of earlyaction priorities, has been sent a published copy by colleagues he left behind at Daimler. It’s interesting to know they’re watching…</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dear_tobias.jpg?itok=lEPeJ4m-\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-rolls-royce-ghost-gain-bespoke-illuminated-fascia\">New Rolls-Royce Ghost to gain bespoke illuminated fascia</a></strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/2-series-gran-coupe/first-drives/bmw-2-series-gran-coupe-m235i-2020-uk-review\">BMW 2 Series Gran Coupe M235i 2020 UK review</a></strong></p> \n +0000","feedId":13379,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"3ae4fc24673e6a2ee3671dfb0771fba4","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/rolls_royce_ghost.jpg?itok=o4qtbpOS":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn15@2020_6/2020/09/05/08-50-48-524_08d5e5d46f323d66.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/bmw_2_series_gran_coupe_m235i.jpg?itok=U4v-hXzY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn83@2020_6/2020/09/05/08-50-46-619_dffaab2280fa52a0.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/mg_b_gt.jpg?itok=I7epWVIh":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn39@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-50-45-294_3a1ae67a6d56f226.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dear_tobias.jpg?itok=lEPeJ4m-":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn13@2020_4/2020/09/05/08-50-43-811_6f0c66e46c489326.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295843551},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"New Peugeot 308 due in 2022 with radical design overhaul","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-peugeot-308-due-2022-radical-design-overhaul","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-peugeot-308-due-2022-radical-design-overhaul\"><img height=\"125\" alt=\"2022 Peugeot 308 prototype - hero front\" title=\"2022 Peugeot 308 prototype - hero front\" /></a>\n<blockquote class=\"image-field-caption\">\n  New style-led 308 will take its design cues from recent Peugeots\n</blockquote> Hatchback range set to be topped by PSE-badged hot hatch with plug-in hybrid power and four-wheel drive \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>The next generation of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/peugeot\">Peugeot</a> models will start with the new <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/308-gti-2015-2017\">308</a> in 2022,&nbsp;and an early indication of what to expect has come in the form of a camouflaged prototype.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>As expected, the next-generation 308's styling appears to mark a radical departure from that of the current car, to bring it into line with the new 208, 2008 and 508, plus the facelifted 3008 and 5008.</p> \n <p>Heavy camouflage means it's unclear at this stage how exactly that will be achieved, but it looks like the 308 will swap its protruding lower bumper for a rounded front end that incorporates Peugeot's new frameless grille and narrow headlights, while the brand's vertical&nbsp;daytime running lights are likely to feature in some form.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The roofline also appears to curve more steeply towards the rear, which makes the hatchback appear longer and lower, while details including new wing mirrors, a subtle rear spoiler&nbsp;and a sharkfin-style aerial will round off the transformation.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><span>Peugeot boss Jean-Philippe Imparato has previously hinted that the 308 will&nbsp;build on the bold look of all other recent Peugeots:&nbsp;“We put the design first,” he said when describing why the brand's&nbsp;comeback has been so successful. “On top of all the investment choices, I protected the design. Then the brand image recovers.”</span></p> \n <p>When it was launched in 2014, the current 308 kick-started the transformation of the entire Peugeot range with a more confident design approach. The successful, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/3008\">more daringly styled 3008</a> followed, along with the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/5008\">5008</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/208\">208</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/2008\">2008</a>.</p> \n <p>The next 308 is set to play that role again by laying the groundwork for a new era of Peugeots when it goes on sale in 2022, most likely after a public debut towards the end of 2021.</p> \n <p>It will be built on an updated version of the EMP2 platform that underpins more than a dozen<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/psa-group-and-fiat-chrysler-confirm-merger-plans\"> PSA Group</a> models and was originally introduced on today’s 308.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>PSA’s strategy so far has been for EMP2 models to be offered with plug-in hybrid technology and for smaller CMP models to come with dedicated electric versions, both offered alongside existing petrol and diesel variants.</p> \n <p>The 308 is set to get a plug-in hybrid drivetrain, mixing a 1.6-litre petrol engine with an electric motor to drive the front wheels in a mainstream variant. However, it’s a proposed second plug-in hybrid model that will interest enthusiasts.</p> \n <p>This model,&nbsp;developed by the brand’s new PSE performance arm, would gain an additional electric motor on the rear axle – a set-up already used on the 3008 PHEV – to give the 308 four-wheel drive and create a new 300bhp-plus hot hatch version that would also receive a host of sporty chassis and styling upgrades to challenge the likes of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/golf-r\">the Volkswagen Golf R</a>.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/3-peugeot-308_pse-render-2020-static-side.jpg?itok=sANfzNAt\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The PSE&nbsp;badge is set to appear first on a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/new-peugeot-508-pse-make-production-ready-debut\">range-topping performance version of the 508</a>. Should the 508 PSE be a success, Imparato told Autocar the PSE formula could be applied “on the 3008 and other cars”, a comment that alludes to the desire to extend it to the 308.</p> \n <p>Success won't be judged on sales, either, but instead on the reputation and acclaim the PSE models receive. To that end, the PSE project is as much about “transforming electric cars” and the perception of them, because Imparato sees “a big opportunity for a line-up of sporty cars” in this mould.</p> \n <p>The GTi badge won't&nbsp;be used on the 308 or any other Peugeots apart from the 208. Even then, it might be limited to the UK only and be based on the electric version as part of the company’s plans to switch PSE's involvement in its models to electrified powertrains only.</p> \n <p>The next 308 range will again include five-door hatchback and estate versions, with still no return for the likes of the 308 CC coupé-convertible seen in previous generations, due to the lack of profitability with such cars. “I love these cars but today there are three other topics first,” said Imparato, naming 5G connectivity and autonomous vehicle development alongside electrified models.</p> \n <p>However, a crossover version of the 308 is a strong possibility for Peugeot. It has noted the success of the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/gla-2014-2020\">Mercedes-Benz GLA</a>, effectively a raised version of the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/a-class\">A-Class hatchback</a>. In addition, fellow PSA brand <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/ds\">DS</a> is planning both hatchback and crossover versions of its own new A-Class/GLA rival, which is due later this year with a shared body-in-white. There’s enough of a gap between the 308 and larger 3008 SUV to make such a car a reality.</p> \n <p>Updated petrol and diesel engines will continue to be offered alongside the plug-in hybrids. Peugeot is still committed to diesel and is even offering it in its new 208 and 2008 models at a time when many rivals are abandoning the fuel at this end of the market.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"642\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/2-peugeot-2008-static-side.jpg?itok=2BXfCXZK\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>An electric version of the 308 may be on the cards too, as Imparato hinted late last year in an interview with Automotive News Europe: “It [the 308] will be a plug-in hybrid first but could perhaps later have a full-electric drivetrain. Our compact and mid-size cars will have plug-in hybrid drivetrains, because it’s a smoother way to switch from internal combustion to electric.”</p> \n <p>Inside, the style-led formula will continue with an updated version of Peugeot’s i-Cockpit design, adapted from that of the newer 3008 and 508.</p> \n <p>Peugeot will be hoping for much greater sales success for the 308 in the UK, though, where it has struggled. “This car was Car of the Year in 2014 and has been a huge sales success in Europe,” said Imparato. “It’s not as strong in the UK, where it deserves more than a 2.5% market share.”</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/new-peugeot-508-pse-make-production-ready-debut\"><strong>New Peugeot 508 PSE makes production-ready debut</strong></a></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/peugeot-gti-sub-brand-will-live-hot-208-likely\">Peugeot GTi sub-brand will live on, hot 208 likely</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/2008/first-drives/peugeot-2008-12-puretech-130-gt-line-2020-uk-review\">Peugeot 2008 1.2 Puretech 130 GT Line 2020 UK review</a></strong></p> \n <p><span class=\"wysiwyg-embed\"></span></p> \n <iframe allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" Bond. And this time… I’m sorry, are those your initials embroidered onto the headrests?</p> \n <p>And so we welcome another <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/aston-martin\">Aston Martin</a> special edition, a product of the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/aston-martin-launch-q-commission-service-bespoke-models\">company’s bespoke Q division </a>– a wryly amusing department name. Yet strangely, I find myself similarly untickled by the arrival of a limited number of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/aston-martin-007-edition-models-celebrate-new-james-bond-film\">007 Edition Vantages and DBS Superleggeras</a>.</p> \n <p>These 100 <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/aston-martin/vantage\">Vantages</a> and 25 <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/aston-martin/dbs-superleggera\">DBS Superleggeras</a> will have 007 embroidery, hazard stripes to mimic rocket booster warning labels and missile-launch-button-themed shift paddles. Owners can even have a 007 badge on the boot lip – overt signals to suggest they’re sufficiently deceptive and intriguing that they would claim they’re in an off-site meeting while secretly playing golf.</p> \n <p>I’m not sure the whole ‘Bond thing’ needs to be shouted about quite this loudly. We all know the world’s least secret secret agent drives an Aston Martin, like we know he drinks vodka martinis. And in the same way that, outside of a fancy dress party, no normal grown adult can order a vodka martini without feeling like an impossible wazzock, I’m not convinced any ordinary person can order a 007-specified Aston without at least some nagging similar pangs.</p> \n <p>But my worry isn’t for those who do buy a 007 Edition Vantage or DBS. Aston only has to find 125 of them, and doubtless they will get the gentle, affectionate ribbing that they deserve from their spouses and friends for choosing the man-child equivalent of an Action Man lunchbox.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/2-aston-martin-james-bond-editions_0.jpg?itok=lAQfyFM9\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>No, I worry instead for those who would like to buy a sports car in an arena where it’s already hard enough to pick one that doesn’t make the owner look insufferable by association and think this is one association they would rather avoid.</p> \n <p>There are many reasons why people spend more than a hundred grand on a Range Rover or a Porsche 911, and they’re not all related to those cars’ tangible qualities. Sometimes it’s because they say not too much about their owners.</p> \n <p>It’s nice to buy a car that suggests you’re quite cool with who you are, rather than a car that says you would rather be someone else. Particularly if the message you’re sending is that, yes, you’re a quite normal company managing director, but should your spouse be brutally murdered by mobsters, you will, before the day is over, be getting your leg over with one of your account managers in an adequately prestigious hotel from which you collect reward points. Jane, hold my calls.</p> \n <p>It’s not like Aston doesn’t do progressive things elsewhere. It’s more committed to an expansive racing programme than most of its peers, and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/aston-martin-valkyrie-specs-details-pricing\">the Valkyrie hypercar </a>is a brilliantly bold project. A back-of-mind link with a dysfunctional film character alongside those is no bad thing in itself. But when that becomes the fixation it seems to be, I wonder if the sentence “Darling, I’ve been thinking I might buy an Aston Martin” raises an eyebrow that says “Really?” more often than we realise.</p> \n <p>My understanding is that MI6 actually prefers its agents to be rather forgettable. I wonder if it wouldn’t do this association any harm in trying to be more of the same.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/aston-martin-007-edition-models-celebrate-new-james-bond-film\">Aston Martin 007 Edition models celebrate new James Bond film</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/dear-tobias-how-new-ceo-can-fix-aston-martin\">Dear Tobias: How the new CEO can fix Aston Martin</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/aston-martin/dbx/first-drives/aston-martin-dbx-2020-uk-review\">Aston Martin DBX 2020 UK review</a></strong></p> \n <p><iframe allow=\"accelerometer; Paul McCartney. John Lennon. Vincent van Gogh. Pablo Picasso. Richie McCaw. Michael Schumacher.</p> \n <p>Chances are you’ll instantly recognise each and every one of those names. I’d wager that it’s also likely you’ll have a rough understanding of the common thread that ties them all together, too. Undoubtedly, they’re all legends in their respective fields – imposing names attached to outstanding individuals who have cast exceptionally long shadows over the worlds of music, art and sport. These are figureheads with whom all promising newcomers will inevitably be compared in some capacity as they rise through the ranks of their chosen profession.</p> \n <p>Now, I reckon that if you do a small amount of mental contortionism, you could probably add <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/audi/a3-sportback\">the Audi A3</a> to that list. You see, in the car world, it’s the model that arguably kick-started an entire genre: that of the premium family hatchback.</p> \n <p>Over its first three generations, the little A3 went on to do pretty great things for the brand from Ingolstadt. Not only did it tally up some 600,000 sales in the UK alone but also, over the course of its 24-year existence, it established itself as the benchmark that all contenders needed to reach if they were to be taken at all seriously.</p> \n <p>Solid refinement and a dynamic character that was stereotypically <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/audi\">Audi</a> in its stability and security were crucial contributors to the A3’s success over those years. But arguably more than anything else, it was the hugely successful way it showcased how a relatively small, reasonably affordable family hatchback could offer the sorts of outstanding levels of material and design appeal that had previously only appeared in cars of a larger footprint sold at a higher price point.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"616\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/29-audi-a3.jpg?itok=N9ny0Gt8\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Indeed, the shadow cast by its success was a long one. Now, with all of the apparent slickness of a Usain Bolt baton handover, a new, fourth-generation model has arrived to maintain its predecessor’s place at the top of the table. At least, that’s the plan. It sits on an updated version of the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/volkswagen-group-invest-further-electrification-expansion\">Volkswagen Group’s </a>ubiquitous MQB platform, sporting a handsome but conservatively evolved new look, multi-link rear suspension and a heavily revised interior.</p> \n <p>A mild hybrid, a couple of plug-in hybrids and decidedly more raucous <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/audi/s3\">S3</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/audi/rs3\">RS3</a> performance models are due to pitch up at some point in the near future, but for now, Audi offers the A3 with a choice of a 148bhp 2.0-litre four-cylinder diesel engine or the 148bhp 1.5-litre turbocharged four-pot petrol tested here. On the surface, at least, it seems the A3 is in a prime position to continue the success of its predecessors.</p> \n <p>Only it’s never that simple, is it? Not when the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/a-class\">Mercedes-Benz A-Class</a> is arguably at its most accomplished level yet, in its sleek fourth generation, or when <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/bmw\">BMW’s</a> new front-driven <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/1-series\">1 Series</a> has solved so many of the packaging problems that the old rear-driven architecture historically created yet retained a healthy level of dynamic prowess in the process.</p> \n <p>With this in mind, we’ve collected together a 161bhp A200 AMG Line Premium (£32,905) and a 138bhp 118i M Sport (£27,805) to see just how well they stack up against our 148bhp A3 35 TFSI S Line (£28,205).</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"599\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/24-audi-a3.jpg?itok=vrDAtAMF\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Rather unfortunately for Audi, it doesn’t take very long at all for you to realise that, in terms of the interior design appeal and apparent build quality for which the A3 has always been so highly regarded, this new model has dropped the ball a bit.</p> \n <p>The view from its admittedly comfortable and appreciatively adjustable driving position just isn’t as impressive as it once was. Sure, the Virtual Cockpit and 10.1in touchscreen infotainment system (standard even on entry-level A3s) inject a healthy dose of technical appeal into the cabin, but from a materials point of view, it seems that a fairly conspicuous level of cheapening has occurred as well.</p> \n <p>Whereas the A3’s dashboard was once an example of clean, effective minimalism and solidity, there are now vast swathes of shiny plastics that sound hollow to the touch and, along with some more hard and scratchy plastics on the doors, contribute to an overall look that comes across as a step backwards – which is a real shame, even if it might not be a deal-breaker in the mind of Joe Public.</p> \n <p>Nevertheless, of the three cars here, it’s the A3 that feels the most spacious, offering up more comfortable amounts of second-row head and leg room than either the BMW or the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mercedes-benz\">Mercedes</a>.</p> \n <p>Speaking of which, the 1 Series and the A-Class seem to take opposing approaches to the field of interior design and, superficially at least, it’s the A-Class that packs the biggest punch in terms of wow factor. Its stepped dashboard, turbine-style air vents, choice materials and crisp twin digital displays all inject a healthy amount of perceived quality into its cabin. But dig a little deeper and it too begins to slide; a few pokes and prods are all it takes to reveal the odd creak or groan as surfaces flex beneath your fingers. And despite its comparatively large footprint (it’s the longest car here), its second row feels notably tighter than the other cars’.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/16-audi-a3.jpg?itok=30qPm7JU\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Conversely, the 1 Series looks relatively plain from behind its typically thick-rimmed M Sport steering wheel, yet it promotes a level of sturdiness and tactile appeal that’s lacking in the Audi and the Mercedes. By shifting onto Munich’s UKL2 architecture, the 1 Series now has far more space to offer as well – no bad thing when you remember how cramped the old rear-driven models felt. The pay-off is that while the 1 Series comes up a bit short on visual pizazz, it’s also the car that’s the nicest to spend time in.</p> \n <p>Round one goes to BMW, then, but an attractive and practical interior is only one discipline in which a successful premium hatchback needs to succeed. On-road performance and refinement are of even greater importance, and it’s here where the three cars most noticeably begin to differ in approach.</p> \n <p>For outright comfort and bump isolation, it’s the A-Class that gets the nod. Its comfort-orientated suspension lends itself very well indeed to motorway driving, but its notably pliant, softly sprung set-up does act as a double-edged sword. On fast B-roads and with heightened levels of vertical and lateral forces working against it, the car begins to feel loose and comparatively lacking in outright composure, even if it nonetheless grips well and has a likeably weighted and accurate steering rack.</p> \n <p>It’s easily the quickest of our trio, with strong mid-range acceleration, but a comparative lack of refinement under load (particularly at higher engine speeds) and an automatic gearbox that can be a bit twitchy and overly willing to kick down under partial throttle inputs are downers.</p> \n <p>By comparison, the 1 Series, on its stiffened and lowered M Sport suspension, feels far more tied down and controlled than the A-Class yet doesn’t give up huge ground when it comes to outright comfort. Sure, it doesn’t yield quite as readily as the A200, and there’s more road roar generated by its 225-section front tyres, but there’s an appealing sophistication to the way its springs and dampers iron out compressions and control weight transfer laterally through quick corners.</p> \n <p>The only trouble is that while its steering feels appealingly sporty in its gearing and it turns in to corners with a heightened level of initial keenness, it suffers from a bit of a shortage of front-end bite. That said, slip is manageable enough and might have been a product of the 35deg C heat on the day of our test. I certainly don’t remember the 1 Series behaving like that when we tested it last year.</p> \n <p>Even so, it served to sap a degree of confidence and left an impression that the BMW isn’t quite the standout driver’s choice the propeller roundel on its nose suggests it should be. Its three-pot motor is also a touch rough at idle and very low crank speeds, although spin it up and it showcases impressive refinement, if not outstanding punch or exceptionally slick gearbox dexterity. It’s fine in both regards but nothing more.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"599\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/25-mercedes-a-class.jpg?itok=B9pclTVg\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>And the A3? Well, Audi may have pulled money away from interior development, but it doesn’t seem like it has cut many corners as far as the A3’s on-road manners are concerned. Tauter than the A-Class in its vertical and lateral body control yet with a level of pliancy that makes it comfortable enough on poorer surfaces and around town, the A3 strikes an appealing dynamic middle ground between its two compatriots.</p> \n <p>Front grip is strong and it takes a pleasingly neutral stance through fast corners, serving to bolster a level of confidence that’s already heightened by its intuitive steering set-up. Add lock and the rack weights up superbly, and while its responses aren’t as quick or as eager just off centre as those of the BMW, it’s accurate nonetheless.</p> \n <p>Add a commendable level of poke, a slick (if slightly relaxed) manual ’box and a level of engine refinement that stands clear of the others’ and the A3 paints itself as an eminently likeable, if slightly bland, premium hatchback.</p> \n <p>Depending on your priorities, you really could argue why any of these cars should stand atop the podium. But for the way in which it blends practicality, dynamic sophistication and superior refinement, victory has to go to the A3. It’s a narrow victory, though, and the temptation to knock it off its perch because of its downgraded interior was very real. Had the 1 Series generated a bit more grip, it would have snatched the win.</p> \n <p>So, the A3 remains on top. But the shadow it casts is shorter than ever.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/audi-r8-and-tt-face-axe-maker-reviews-line\">Audi R8 and TT face axe as maker reviews line-up</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/facelifted-audi-q5-gains-mild-hybrid-tech-and-new-infotainment\">Facelifted Audi Q5 gains mild-hybrid tech and new infotainment</a></strong></p> \n height=\"125\" alt=\"2020 Toyota GR Yaris - hero front\" title=\"2020 Toyota GR Yaris - hero front\" /></a> UK deliveries of rally-derived, four-wheel-drive performance car are set to begin in autumn \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>The 257bhp&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-2020-toyota-gr-yaris-prototype\">Toyota GR Yaris</a>, the second model in the GR sports car range, has entered production at a new, bespoke facility in Japan ahead of its October launch.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The first production example left the new GR&nbsp;line last week, following the implementation of a new vehicle assembly&nbsp;system that comprises a series of individual cells connected by driverless vehicles. Toyota says this method is more suitable than the conventional conveyor belt system used elsewhere&nbsp;because it allows for greater accuracy in constructing&nbsp;rigid sports car shells and chassis.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The GR Yaris was recently made available to pre-order from £29,995 ahead of its market launch.</p> \n <p>Interested buyers are invited to choose between the standard variant - which comes equipped with 18in alloy wheels wrapped in Dunlop Sport Maxx tyres, as well as&nbsp;dual-exit exhaust pipes, a leather steering wheel, keyless entry and active noise control as standard - or the hardcore Circuit Pack variant. This latter&nbsp;bumps the price up to £33,495 and adds a pair of limited-slip differentials, red brake calipers, sticky Michelin Pilot sports tyres and tuned suspension in the name of enhanced dynamics.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Both models are painted white as standard, but&nbsp;red, black and silver finishes are available as optional extras. Deliveries are set to get underway in November.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/toyotagryaris1_0.jpg?itok=yJ5JYNJK\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The new hot hatch,&nbsp;<span>which&nbsp;</span><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-2020-toyota-gr-yaris-prototype\">Autocar has driven&nbsp;in camouflagued prototype form</a><span>,&nbsp;</span>has been developed by Gazoo Racing in Japan as a homologation special&nbsp;to aid development of the next-generation Yaris WRC. Tommi Mäkinen Racing, which runs Toyota’s World Rally Championship&nbsp;programme, had significant input into the model.</p> \n <p>The GR Yaris&nbsp;joins the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/supra\">GR Supra</a> in Toyota's growing performance line-up. At the car's launch, Gazoo Racing boss&nbsp;Shigeki Tomoyama said: “While the new GR Supra is a sports car developed through track racing, the GR Yaris has been devised through our participation in rallies – something that many of our fans have been waiting for.”</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-2020-toyota-gr-yaris-prototype\"><strong>First drive: Toyota GR Yaris hot hatch prototype tested</strong></a></p> \n <p>The GR Yaris is built&nbsp;on a special four-wheel-drive version of Toyota’s TNGA architecture, with the front end of the GA-B small car platform – as used on the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-2020-toyota-yaris-revealed-ground-redesign\">new Yaris</a> – and the rear from the GA-C of the larger Corolla.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Compared with the regular Yaris, the new machine has an entirely different body, with a lower roof, three doors instead of five&nbsp;and significantly reworked bodywork to aid aerodynamics.</p> \n <p>The GR Yaris is 3995mm long and 1805mm wide, with a wheelbase of 2558mm. The front track is 1530mm and&nbsp;the rear track is 1560mm.</p> \n <p>The bodywork makes extensive use of carbonfibre polymer and aluminium to reduce weight. It also includes a substantially wider rear track than the regular Yaris, along with new double-wishbone rear suspension. Kerb weight is 1280kg.</p> \n <p>Only limited technical information was available when <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-2020-toyota-gr-yaris-prototype\">Autocar drove the GR Yaris</a>, but Toyota later confirmed that the&nbsp;<span>turbocharged&nbsp;</span>1.6-litre three-cylinder engine will produce a maximum of 257bhp and 265lb ft.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/toyotagryaris6.jpg?itok=CejAumfd\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The engine is mated to a six-speed Intelligent Manual Transmission (IMT) gearbox, with permanent four-wheel drive delivered by&nbsp;Toyota’s new GR-Four system. This uses a multi-plate clutch and can vary power to all four wheels, with three preset levels of torque distribution, including a wholly rear-biased one. The GR Yaris features 356mm grooved front disc brakes that&nbsp;utilise four-pot calipers.</p> \n <p>Pre-orders have already opened for the hot hatch in Japan, where it's being being offered&nbsp;<span>initially</span>&nbsp;in limited-run RZ First Edition and RZ High Performance First Edition&nbsp;guises. Both models feature bodywork styling tweaks and elements, along with other design features.</p> \n <p>The GR Yaris will be produced on a dedicated Gazoo Racing line at Toyota’s production facility in Motomachi, Japan, that uses a large number of manual processes.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-2020-toyota-gr-yaris-prototype\"><strong>First drive: Toyota GR-Yaris hot hatch prototype tested</strong></a></p> \n <p><a 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"Lotus Evija: 2000bhp hypercar stars at Concours of href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/lotus-evija-2000bhp-hypercar-stars-concours-elegance\"><img alt=\"2020 Lotus Evija at Concours of Elegance - side\" title=\"2020 Lotus Evija at Concours of Elegance - side\" /></a>\n<blockquote class=\"image-field-caption\">\n  Evija will kickstart a new era of design and performance at Hethel\n</blockquote> World's most powerful production car is sold out for 2020, but deliveries have been pushed back to next year \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>The new <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/lotus\">Lotus</a> Evija has been shown&nbsp;at London's Concours of Elegance, as the company gears up to begin customer deliveries in 2021.</p> \n <p>The hypercar's second public appearance - following a debut at last week's London Concours - comes following the company's announcement that <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/exclusive-lotus-evija-launch-pushed-back-until-mid-2021\">deliveries have been pushed back five month</a>s as a result of the pandemic. As exclusively reported by Autocar, lockdowns, travel restrictions and quarantine rules hampered the firm's ability to continue the model's testing programme, which will&nbsp;recommence as restrictions ease.</p> \n <p>More recently, Lotus <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/lotus-ends-evija-development-contract-williams-advanced-engineering\">ended its technical development partnership with Williams Advanced Engineering</a>, which had seen the two forms collaborate on the Evija, citing \"delivery problems\". Hethel added that \"the end result will be a better product\" as a result.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Claimed to be the most powerful production car in the world, the 1973bhp electric hypercar&nbsp;is sold out for its initial 2020 production run.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>A video&nbsp;of&nbsp;the newly&nbsp;designed configurator show how the ordering experience begins for buyers. Autocar had a chance to <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/virtually-perfect-next-level-lotus-evija-configurator\">play with the high-tech configurator, and meet the team behind it</a>, earlier this year.</p> \n <p><span class=\"wysiwyg-embed\"></span></p> \n <iframe allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/f162vo_M_ok\" width=\"560\"></iframe>\n <p></p> \n <p>&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The Evija&nbsp;is being built in at a refurbished facility at Lotus's&nbsp;<span>headquarters</span>&nbsp;in Hethel, Norfolk, called Factory 3. Work on the facility, which is a former Lotus Engineering building that was once home to the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/opinion/anything-goes/dont-read-just-another-journo-glorious-vauxhall-lotus-carlton\">Vauxhall Lotus Carlton</a>,&nbsp;is now near completion.&nbsp;Each of the 130 Evijas will be hand-built there.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Lotus has told Autocar that all of the Evijas due to be built this year have already been sold, although it hasn't given an exact figure.</p> \n <p>“With our new factory ready, we are ahead of the pack in the emerging EV hypercar segment and 100% ready for some healthy competition,\" said Lotus boss Phil Popham, an indirect reference to the likes of the Pininfarina Battista that have so far remained quiet on sales.</p> \n <p>Dynamic testing of the car got underway earlier this year at Lotus's&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/lotus-reveals-plans-overhauled-hethel-hq\">Hethel </a>test track, which sits adjacent to the Evija production facility.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Gavan Kershaw, director of vehicle attributes at Lotus, said: “Physical prototype testing at speed is a landmark moment for the Evija and hugely exciting for everyone involved. Our aim is to make sure it’s a true Lotus in every sense, with exceptional performance that’s going to set new standards in the hypercar sector.”&nbsp;</p> \n <p>While most track testing will be done at Hethel, Lotus claims it will use other demanding European circuits, too. \"Over the coming months several prototypes will cover many thousands of miles and hundreds of hours of driving assessment, including on public roads\" the maker said in a release.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>An output of 1973bhp is promised for the Evija, which is more than the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/pininfarina-battista-1900bhp-ev-shows-restyled-front-end\">1888bhp Battista</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/£15m-rimac-ctwo-hypercar-almost-sold-out-three-weeks\">Rimac C_Two</a>&nbsp;and the 1479bhp petrol-powered&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bugatti/chiron\">Bugatti Chiron</a> currently in production.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Each of the 130 due to be built will be priced at £2.04 million. “Target specifications” include four-wheel drive, 1254lb ft and torque vectoring, giving it a 0-62mph time of less than three seconds, a 0-186mph time of less than nine seconds and a top speed of 200mph-plus. A production slot can be reserved with a refundable £250,000 deposit.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"506\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/evija_configurator_7.jpg?itok=JAiLS3PN\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The Evija, pronounced ‘E-vi-ya’, will be Lotus’s first new-model launch <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/lotus-suv-use-volvo-underpinnings-and-have-class-leading-handling\">under Geely ownership</a>, and is the maker’s first all-new model for more than a decade. It will&nbsp;act “as a ‘halo’ for the rest of the Lotus range” both now and for “new Lotus performance cars to come”.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The car pictured here in a studio is for show, but Lotus’s design director, Russell Carr, told Autocar that “this is how it’ll be on the road. This is very much the production car. All the surfaces are made to production level.”&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The Evija, which is codenamed Type 130, is low and broad, at 4.59m long, 2.0m wide and 1.12m high. According to Lotus, it “marks the beginning of a contemporary new Lotus design language”.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dsc_5468.jpg?itok=lGL8GAeO\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>“We wanted from the start to do something that was pure, simple, but have a sense of luxury and elegance about it,” said Carr. “On the outside, we started by thinking ‘what are the existing factors from the Lotus DNA that we want to keep?’, and really important for us were the strong haunches you see on the car. It’s very important when you’re sitting inside that you can see the corners of the vehicle – it helps you place the car on the track. It’s also just a very emotional thing to see the bodywork; rearwards as well.”&nbsp;</p> \n <p>“We have the cabin sat low within those fenders, which are really important to us because the car’s all about dynamics,” said Carr, “and if the cabin sits low and the fenders are pronounced, you have the impression that the car’s got a low centre of gravity.”&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Around the overall design simplicity come some advanced aerodynamics (see Carr Q&amp;A, below), which direct air flow over, under and through the car, creating a complex body shape with vast scoops running through the rear three-quarters, and exiting at the back.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dsc_5451-edit.jpg?itok=BaBb094f\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The design is permitted by the adoption of electric drive. “That certainly gives us a lot more freedom, yes,” said Carr. “You’ve obviously got battery packs that can be placed in certain places, and it’s certainly different from a traditional combustion engine, and we’ve tried to exploit that as much as possible.”&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Lotus hasn’t yet revealed how many electric motors the car will have or where they’ll be positioned, but its partnership with Williams Advanced Engineering – which is, among other things, the supplier of batteries to the Formula E grid – will be key to the Evija’s performance.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Lotus said the Evija will have a 70kWh battery, capable of being charged at up to 350kW, enabling an 18-minute charge with a WLTP range of around 250 miles. The charge port is at the rear of the car.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Construction is from carbonfibre, both for the chassis and the body. Light weight is core to all Lotus models and the Evija weighs several hundred kilos less than the Battista and C_Two are reported to be, although they have more battery capacity. Even so, at 1680kg, the Evija is likely to become the heaviest Lotus ever. Despite this, Lotus boldly claims it will “set a new standard for Lotus driving performance” and be “the most dynamically accomplished road car in the history of Lotus”.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Inside, the carbonfibre construction remains visible in what’s a relatively spacious cockpit. “The start point is a floating beam, this open instrument panel you can place your hand right through,” said Carr. “The inspiration for that came from classic racing cars, from the 1950s and ’60s, in which you can see the structure. In those days it would have been tubular, but on this it’s carbonfibre.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dsc_5469-edit.jpg?itok=6CG5Jiok\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>“We wanted to use carbonfibre, and once we got into that we started looking at wishbones on racing cars. We looked at modern racing bicycles as well, and that informed some of the sections and forms that go in there. And that’s really become a very distinctive part of this interior. If you love modern racing bikes or componentry on racing cars, you’ll recognise that.”&nbsp;</p> \n <p>“It’s a nice shape to use as well, with the wing profile, and adds a strong aeronautical flavour on the whole car. It’s very distinctive,” Carr added. “There’s a certain luxury to space and in such cars you can feel very claustrophobic. This feels open.”&nbsp;</p> \n <p>That’s in stark contrast to another upcoming hypercar, the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/aston-martin-valkyrie-specs-details-pricing\">Aston Martin Valkyrie</a>, with the implication that the two British hypercars will be quite different, in ethos as well as propulsion.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>“We wanted, if this doesn’t sound ridiculous, a really usable hypercar,” said Carr. “The Evija is very much a road car. But obviously the performance credentials of this car mean that it can be driven on the track.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dsc_5165-edit.jpg?itok=ATMLUl2i\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>“Certainly from our side the work we’ve done on the aerodynamics means that it’s going to be an extremely quick car, generating a huge amount of downforce, which means it can be driven at high speeds. It’s going to be a stable car wherever it’s driven.”</p> \n <p><strong>Q&amp;A with Russell Carr, design director, Lotus Cars</strong></p> \n <p><strong>Tell us about the way air moves around this car.&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p>“Something very Lotus which we’ve taken to another level is the aerodynamics. <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/lotus-70-highs-and-lows\">It’s always been part of our history and motorsport</a>: in the ’60s we were among the first teams putting wings on cars, we had ground effects in the ’70s and streamlining way back in the ’50s. With this car, the philosophy was that we wanted to harness the airflow over the body of the car, but also through the body of the car. We’re not the first people to do it, but we wanted to do it in a very sculptural manner that would give a different aesthetic to the car.”&nbsp;</p> \n <p><strong>What does that mean for aesthetics?&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p>“When you look at the car from the outside you see familiar volume, we hope a very beautiful-looking car. It’s important that it’s beautiful in the first place. But as you walk around it you start to see openings that go through the car, which allow the air to pass through. As I say, that gives it a different aesthetic, draws the eye through the car and over the car, and gives it a great sense of movement.”</p> \n <p><strong>Read more</strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/used-cars/james-ruppert-nows-time-buy-lotus\"><strong>James Ruppert: Now's the time to buy a Lotus</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/lotus-elan-frame-boxster-rival-revival-plan\"><strong>Lotus Elan in frame as Boxster rival in revival plan</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/lotus-70-highs-and-lows\"><strong>Lotus at 70: the highs and lows​</strong></a></p> \n <p><span class=\"wysiwyg-embed\"></span></p> \n <iframe
