+0000","feedId":13379,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"bb2f24884384ef46fe491a89b81f5e52","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/40-lotus-evija.jpg?itok=y7OiAu8k":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn10@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-50-45-111_ae622d72bcdd5a83.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/evija_configurator_7.jpg?itok=JAiLS3PN":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn35@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-51-33-991_57b0ce48f2697e19.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dsc_5468.jpg?itok=lGL8GAeO":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn73@2020_1/2020/09/05/08-50-43-679_c3774b5599d869f3.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dsc_5451-edit.jpg?itok=BaBb094f":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn91@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-50-46-303_704a205783918e80.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dsc_5469-edit.jpg?itok=6CG5Jiok":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn29@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-50-43-895_c25b6c2ada37e920.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/dsc_5165-edit.jpg?itok=ATMLUl2i":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn55@2020_4/2020/09/05/08-50-47-831_4291b5339382861e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295843550},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"New electric cars 2020: What’s coming and when?","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-electric-cars-2020-2021","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-electric-cars-2020-2021\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/new_electric_cars_2019_0.jpg?itok=F7zdjITp\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"New electric cars 2020\" title=\"New electric cars 2020\" /></a> Every debut and new model due to arrive over the next twelve months, all in one place \n<div> \n <p>Keeping track of every new car and knowing when they’re due to go on sale can be tough, especially if you’re only interested in <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/best-cars/top-10-best-electric-cars\">EVs</a>.</p> \n <p>There are so many due to arrive over the course of the next twelve months, in spite of the ongoing global health emergency,&nbsp;so it’s worth learning how long you’ll be waiting for the one you want to go on sale. 2019 saw new entrants to the category from the likes of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/audi\">Audi</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mercedes-benz\">Mercedes</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mg-motor\">MG</a>, with major launches from well-known electric pioneers such as&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/tesla\">Tesla</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/nissan\">Nissan</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/renault\">Renault</a>&nbsp;all following soon after.</p> \n <p>The final few months of 2020 and early 2021 look&nbsp;to be even more stacked, as manufacturers work hard to meet increasingly tough emissions rules with the introduction of more all-electric models.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/new-car-release-dates\">New Cars 2020: what's coming this year and when?​</a></strong></p> \n <p>Here is our comprehensive list of what EVs are coming when in the car industry.</p> \n <h2>September</h2> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-la-motor-show/audi-e-tron-sportback-electric-coupe-suv-priced-%C2%A379900\">Audi E-tron Sportback</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-audi-e-tron-s-and-e-tron-s-sportback-arrive-hot-electric-suvs\">E-tron S</a></h3> \n <p>The coupe-styled version of Audi's first dedicated EV arrives in the UK this month, carrying a price premium over the regular E-tron as well as several mechanical upgrades that promise a slightly improved electric range over the SUV.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>It will be joined by a pair of Audi's first electric performance models. The E-tron S duo use three electric motors, becoming one of the first production cars to do so, producing 496bhp.</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-mg-5-electric-estate-headed-uk-214-mile-range\">MG 5</a></h3> \n <p>The UK's first affordable electric estate car will make its official debut shortly, sitting alongside the ZS EV crossover in MG's growing range of zero-emissions models. The MG 5 is understood to be a reengineered version of the China-only&nbsp;Roewe Ei5, and should deliver 214 miles of range from a&nbsp;52.5kWh battery pack.</p> \n <p>Cost will be the 5's strongest selling point, with the estate expected to arrive at a similar price to the ZS EV - undercutting many smaller electric models from European and Japanese rivals.</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/id-3/first-drives/volkswagen-id-3-2020-review\">Volkswagen ID 3</a></h3> \n <p>Designed and built as a pure electric car, the ID hatchback is a crucial launch for VW. It closely matches the Golf hatchback in size, with limited-run First Edition models retailing from £38,880. Eventually more entry-level models will be sold at a price closer to that of a Golf diesel, roughly £27,000.</p> \n <p>Built on the modular MEB platform, the ID 3&nbsp;offers a variety of battery options for a range of between 249 and 373 miles between charges. The final design largely remains true to the original concept, which was first revealed in 2016 and went on to inspire several other ID models, which are all due to launch over the next five years.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/1vwid3_0.jpg?itok=-7XAjkft\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <h2>October 2020</h2> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2019-ssangyong-korando-lead-brands-electrification-plans\">Ssangyong Korando EV</a></h3> \n <p>Conventional petrol and diesel versions of the South Korean firm's new Nissan Qashqai rival appeared on UK forecourts back in 2019, but an electric variant inspired by Ssangyong's recent e-SIV concept is expected to arrive very shortly.</p> \n <p>It will likely carry only minor visual changes from the standard car, but will be a proper 4x4, with all-wheel drive and strong towing ability - a key feature for many UK Ssangyong customers.</p> \n <h3>December 2020</h3> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-citroen-c4-and-e-c4-make-uk-debut-ahead-autumn-launch\">Citroen e-C4</a></h3> \n <p>The latest generation C4 will arrive with radically different coupe-crossover styling, and will be offered as an electric variant for the first time. The e-C4 sits on the PSA Group's CMP modular EV platform, currently used by the Vauxhall Corsa-e, and will use the same powertrain.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Customers can expect 134bhp and 192lb ft from the motor driving the front wheels, and 217 miles of range from the 50kWh battery. Top speed should be 93mph and the e-C4 should manage 0-62mph in 9.7sec.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"415\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/_max0195-edit-edit.jpg?itok=ueLfDLl1\" width=\"622\" /></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-eqa-electric-crossover-drops-disguise-new-images\">Mercedes-Benz EQA</a></h3> \n <p>The entry-level EQ model is set to borrow its body shape&nbsp;from the GLA compact crossover rather than the A-Class hatchback, leaving more room beneath the seats for batteries without compromising on interior space.</p> \n <p>Mercedes has yet to reveal much about the car, including which electric powertrain it will use, although the EQA is predicted to deliver 249 miles of range between charges, and will likely be priced to compete with the BMW i3. Styling should closely follow that of the EQC.</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-benz-eqv-electric-mpv-priced-%C2%A370665\">Mercedes-Benz EQV</a></h3> \n <p>The luxury van-based MPV has already made its debut, but won't be reaching UK forecourts until later this year. It will be one of the first in its class to go on sale, and borrows much of its styling from the conventional&nbsp;V-Class model.</p> \n <p>252 miles of electric range is promised, along with a choice of seating configurations, and prices starting from £70,000.</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/tesla-%E2%80%98plaid%E2%80%99-3-motor-system-coming-model-s-2020%E2%80%99\">Tesla Model S Plaid</a></h3> \n <p>Long promised by Tesla boss Elon Musk, the Model S Plaid should soon arrive to challenge Porsche's Taycan Turbo S for the electric performance saloon crown. A Model S Performance can already manage 0-60mph in 2.4sec, but the Plaid (named as a nod to Mel Brooks comedy classic Spaceballs) will gain an extra motor that allows for torque vectoring. Battery capacity should also be increased to cope with the extra performance without compromising on range.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Prototypes have been spotted testing at the Nurburgring with sizeable rear wings, larger wheels, lowered suspension and a wider rear track, but it is unclear whether any of those will make it onto the production car.</p> \n <h3>Tesla Model X Plaid</h3> \n <p>Improvements made for the Model S Plaid will almost certainly make their way into Tesla's family SUV, already the fastest-accelerating seven-seater on sale in the UK. Adding an extra motor to the Model X could see it manage 0-60mph in an even quicker time than its current 2.7sec.</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/volvo-xc40-recharge-p8-orders-open-electric-suv\">Volvo XC40 Recharge&nbsp;P8</a></h3> \n <p>The company’s very first electric vehicle, the XC40 Recharge is the first of what will quickly become an entire range of EV-adapted versions, rather than brand new ones built around batteries and electric motors. That means an electric XC90 will follow.</p> \n <p>Hardware will be shared with Polestar 2, has already arrived on UK shores, with customers having to wait until the tail-end of 2020 to see XC40 Recharge models on the roads. When it does, it will deliver 402bhp from twin electric motors, and promises 248 miles of range. Pricing was revealed at £53,000 - nudging the Recharge over the government's updated plug-in car grant maximum cost.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/volvo_xc40_bev_front.jpg?itok=XyrTWwmH\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <h3>Spring 2021</h3> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/audi-reveals-q4-e-tron-electric-suv-ahead-2020-sale\">Audi Q4 e-tron </a></h3> \n <p>The concept version of Audi's upcoming mainstream electric SUV was revealed at 2019's Geneva motor show, but a production version isn't set to arrive until 2020 as the firm's fifth electric model. It borrows styling from the e-tron, and will slot in beneath the Q5 in terms of size.</p> \n <p>It will use the VW Group's MEB platform, rather than the adapted MQ platform used by the larger e-tron. Twin motors will provide Quattro all-wheel drive and up to 302bhp - around 100bhp less than the full-size e-tron but 100 more than MEB-based hatchbacks like the VW ID.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/audi_q4_etron_2626j.jpg?itok=iNEq18vv\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-audi-e-tron-gt-porsche-taycan-sibling-seen-ahead-la-debut\">Audi E-tron GT</a></h3> \n <p>The electric grand tourer, which will share a platform with the Porsche Taycan, is expected to make its production debut towards the end of the year. Audi will likely time its reveal with the 2020 LA motor show, if it goes ahead post-pandemic, with the final car expected to go on sale in early 2021.</p> \n <p>It is predicted to use a 96kWh battery good for 248 miles of range, with 350kW rapid charging and twin electric motors producing 582bhp. The E-tron GT should be capable of&nbsp;0-62mph in 3.5sec and a 149mph top speed.</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/1900bhp-pininfarina-battista-ev-make-uk-appearance\">Pininfarina Battista</a></h3> \n <p>Only 150 Battista hypercars are set to be produced, but with individual motors for each wheel producing a total&nbsp;1900bhp, it promises to be powerful in the extreme. Lucky customers will see deliveries towards the end of 2020 from the design house-turned-manufacturer, which has partnered with Rimac for the underlying powertrain.&nbsp;</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2020-tesla-model-y-prices-specs-details\">Tesla Model Y</a></h3> \n <p>Originally revealed in March 2019, Tesla's compact SUV saw North American deliveries begin earlier this year. The sister car to the Model 3 isn't expected to arrive in the UK until next year at the earliest. The much-in-demand SUV will arrive with the option to add a third row - which could make it the go-to EV for large families. It shares a platform and powertrain with the Model 3 saloon, which will hopefully speed up Tesla's ability to deliver cars on time.</p> \n <p>A more advanced version of the company’s ‘supercomputer’ semi-autonomous driving system is also predicted, as is a more potent Performance variant.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/model_y_front_34_blue_1.jpg?itok=XJuJ_qzH\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <h3>Tesla Roadster</h3> \n <p>A flagship sports car to replace the original, Lotus-based Roadster that announced Tesla to the world, the next-generation Roadster has been previewed extensively ahead of an official debut. Tesla claims a top speed in excess of 250mph, a 0-60mph time of 1.9 seconds, and a range of 620 miles thanks to a 200kWh battery pack - the biggest in a production EV. Prices are expected to start at around £189,000 for the first 1000 cars, which will be badged as Founders Edition models. Following that, prices should be around £151,000 when general sales begin in mid-2020.</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-la-motor-show/amazon-leads-£544-million-investment-ev-start-rivian\">Rivian R1T</a></h3> \n <p>A surprise announcement at 2018's Los Angeles motor show, despite the company behind it having been first formed in 2009, the Rivian R1T is a pick-up truck reimagined for an EV generation. It has clever packaging that makes the most of available space, while the underlying powertrain promises to deliver as much as 754bhp and a 0-60mph time of under three seconds.</p> \n <p>It is set to go into production in late 2020, which might be enough time to beat Tesla's upcoming pick-up to the punch.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/94-rivian-r1t-reveal-static-front_0.jpg?itok=fSJrEFHN\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-bmw-ix3-munichs-second-ev-offers-285-mile-range\">BMW IX 3</a></h3> \n <p>An electric version of BMW’s X3 SUV, the iX3, made its debut in mid-2020 with a new rear-wheel drive powertrain comprising a single electric motor. It closely resembles the petrol-powered X3, rather than taking any design inspiration from the more radical i3 and i8, and is only the company’s second pure electric car. The motor develops 282bhp from a 80kWh battery, and is capable of delivering 285 miles of WLTP-certified range. UK deliveries will begin in March 2021.</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-2021-cupra-el-born-vw-group%E2%80%99s-first-ev-hot-hatch\">Cupra el-Born</a></h3> \n <p>The second non-VW model to launch on the MEB platform, the el-Born has a very similar powertrain and engineering to the ID hatchback, but opts for sportier styling and a more engaging driving experience. Set to arrive early next year, it will be powered by a 77kWh (82kWh gross) battery pack and promises&nbsp;310 miles of range per charge, though the brand has yet to confirm exact performance figures.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>With the VW ID 3 only reaching the UK in September 2020, it will be at least six months before the sporty EV arrives in showrooms. When it does, it is&nbsp;expected to pack around 201bhp for a 0-31mph time of 2.9 seconds.&nbsp;</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/fiat-500-reinvented-all-electric-city-car-2020\">Fiat 500</a></h3> \n <p>The new electric Fiat 500 shares much of its styling with the current petrol-powered model, but underneath it is entirely new, with a bespoke&nbsp;architecture, 117bhp electric motor and 42kWh lithium iojn battery pack. Range is quoted at 199 miles on the WLTP test cycle, giving it an edge over the Mini Electric and Honda E.</p> \n <p>Revealed online following the cancellation of the Geneva motor show in March, the electric Fiat 500 will go on sale in the first quarter of 2021. Prices will start from £29,500 at launch for a top-spec La Prima edition convertible, with hard-top models set to follow later.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/new_500_5.jpg?itok=azgZbG1I\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-la-motor-show/first-ride-2020-ford-mustang-mach-e-prototype\">Ford Mustang Mach-E</a></h3> \n <p>Ford's upcoming pony car caused controversy for several reasons. It will be the first electric car to wear the Mustang badge, and it has a crossover bodystyle. At launch, the range-topping version promises 332bhp and a 0-60 time in the mid 5-seconds, but a full GT model is expected at a later date with 459bhp and a sprint time in the threes.</p> \n <p>UK deliveries were originally&nbsp;scheduled for the third quarter of 2020, but Ford pushed that back to Spring 2021 in order to meet expected demand in its home territory. While prices have yet to be made official, it is expected to cost from around £42,000 for an entry-level model, rising to over £60,000 for the top-end version.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"625\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/86-ford-mustang-mach-e-2020-fd-otr-front_0.jpg?itok=gsx2xAKN\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/lotus-evija-new-configurator-video-released-ev-hypercar\">Lotus Evija</a></h3> \n <p>Provided lockdown restrictions are lifted in time, Lotus is expecting to begin production of its first electric car later this year, with customer deliveries due by the end of 2020. The Evija has already sold out its first year allocation, despite costing £2.04 million each and built slots requiring a £250,000 deposit.</p> \n <p>While Lotus has yet to confirm performance details, it is reportedly targeting a 0-62mph time of under three seconds, a top speed of over 200mph, and a 0-186mph sprint of less than nine seconds. Multiple electric motors will deliver all-wheel drive and a peak 1973bhp output, making it more powerful than both the 1479bhp Bugatti Chiron and 1888bhp Pininfarina Battista.</p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/skoda-enyaq-iv-revealed-first-bespoke-ev-316-mile-range\">Skoda Enyaq iV</a></h3> \n <p>The Czech company's first bespoke EV, the Enyaq iV is set to begin UK deliveries in early 2021. It will be the first time Skoda has used the VW Group's MEB platform, and will arrive in a selection of different power and battery combinations, including a flagship vRS performance model.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Physically as long as an Octavia, but with almost as much interior space as the seven-seat Kodiaq, it promises up to 316 miles of range in rear-driven 80 iV guise, or 285 miles with the all-wheel drive 80x variant. The top-spec vRS version promises 302bhp and a 0-62mph time of 6.2sec. Prices will start from £30,000 after government incentives.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE </strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/new-car-release-dates\"><strong>Complete list of new cars in 2020</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"http://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/best-cars/top-10-best-electric-cars\"><strong>Top 10 best electric cars 2020</strong></a></p> href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/hyundai\">Hyundai</a> has revamped its <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/hyundai/kona\">Kona</a> line-up for 2021, ushering in a new look inside and out, mild-hybrid technology and a performance-inspired N Line range-topper.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The updated car is told apart primarily by its heavily redesigned front end, which incorporates wider LED daytime-running lights, an extended bonnet, a new grille design and a contrasting silver skid plate.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The side profile is more familiar, but the rear end has been updated with new brake light designs and a contrasting lower bumper to match the front. Overall, the new Kona is 40mm longer than the outgoing car, which Hyundai claims gives it “a more sleek and dynamic look”.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Inside, the Kona gains an electronic handbrake, ambient lighting, coloured speaker and vent surrounds, and a raft of new colour and material options.</p> \n <p>Alongside the visual tweaks comes a new N Line trim level inspired by the brand’s<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/hyundai/i30-n\"> N performance offshoot</a>. It does away with the standard car’s contrasting cladding in favour of an aerodynamically enhancing bodykit, and gains a distinctive mesh air intake design above the front grille.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/all-new_kona_n_line_1.jpg?itok=nCa7f49Y\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>As well as bespoke wheel designs, the N Line receives a contrasting rear diffuser and a dual-exit sports exhaust, while the predominantly black interior features contrasting red stitching, metal pedals and N logos throughout.</p> \n <p>The Kona retains its range-topping 1.6-litre petrol engine, uprated from 175bhp to 195bhp&nbsp;and available with two- or four-wheel drive, but the same-sized diesel option is now equipped with 48V mild-hybrid functionality as standard for enhanced efficiency. It can be paired with a seven-speed automatic or Hyundai’s new Intelligent Manual Transmission.</p> \n <p>The entry-level 1.0-litre petrol engine can also be optionally equipped with mild-hybrid technology, while the Kona Hybrid continues to combine a 1.6-litre petrol engine with a front-mounted electric motor to produce 139bhp.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The model also promises improved ride quality and refinement over its predecessor, gaining a retuned suspension set-up, improved tyres and a recalibrated steering system.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Prices will be announced before the new Kona arrives in showrooms later this year, with the plug-in hybrid option following in 2021. The updated Kona Electric will be revealed “in the near future”, according to the brand.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/hyundai/kona/first-drives/hyundai-kona-hybrid-premium-se-2019-review\"><strong>Hyundai Kona Hybrid Premium SE 2019 review​</strong></a></p> \n <p><a +0000","feedId":13379,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"77b707b011606aa866cc7377e0041c09","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/all-new_kona_n_line_4.jpg?itok=YiVwMJlt":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn4@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-50-45-989_27ea4f299a47935f.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/all-new_kona_n_line_1.jpg?itok=nCa7f49Y":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn41@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-50-44-936_b70ebc5e74c9a8fa.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295843551},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"First drive: Aston Martin Callum Vanquish 25 by R-Reforged","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-aston-martin-callum-vanquish-25-r-reforged","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-aston-martin-callum-vanquish-25-r-reforged\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/99-callum-aston-martin-vanquish-25-fd-hero-front.jpg?itok=nHB4C9w5\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"Callum Aston Martin Vanquish 25 first drive review - hero front\" title=\"Callum Aston Martin Vanquish 25 first drive review - hero front\" /></a> Updated Vanquish is impressively improved in key areas with a whole new level of craftsmanship, albeit for a massive price \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>The original <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/aston-martin\">Aston Martin</a> Vanquish and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/slideshow/inside-ian-callum’s-personal-car-collection\">its designer, Ian Callum</a>, have always had something of an on-off relationship.</p> \n <p>Callum is proud of the car, of course; it was one of the earliest designs for which he drew practically every line. It led Aston’s change to modern construction methods and it’s a timeless shape that has matured beautifully over its 20-year life.</p> \n <p>However, there were always things the designer simply didn’t like: the old-tech lights, the lower lamps he inherited from <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/used-car-buying-guides/aston-martin-db7-used-car-buying-guide\">the DB7 V12</a>, the mirrors, the chromework, the “timid” wheels, the too-narrow tracks that didn’t quite fill the arches, and the nose and tail designs that he felt needed “more teeth”. Most of all, he was disappointed with the interior; the design theme was decent but the execution was less about craftsmanship than using existing facilities to get cars out of the door.</p> \n <p>All of which is why Callum last year revealed, after he <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/ian-callum-leaves-jaguar-after-20-years-design-director\">moved on from a distinguished 20-year career as the head of Jaguar design</a>, that the first project for the new design business he promptly launched would be a batch of 25 revised Vanquishes. They would be produced at a new studio in Warwick and be backed by the Swiss R-Reforged group that makes a speciality of high-quality, bespoke products of all kinds – not just cars.</p> \n <p>Now the building of Callum Vanquishes has begun. The details of the interior revisions, trim options and the definitive chassis and engine specifications have now all been decided by Callum and Adam Donfrancesco, the project’s head of engineering. At the Warwick headquarters a couple of weeks ago, the pair of them offered us a socially distanced meeting, a car viewing and an exclusive drive.</p> \n <p>“We’ve made a grand total of 350 changes,” Callum says, “introducing a level of craftsmanship you simply can’t get in normal production cars – even supercars. The idea is to chase even the smallest details. Only the panelwork remains the same. Our idea is to build a show car for every customer.”</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/98-callum-aston-martin-vanquish-25-fd-hero-side.jpg?itok=dfhkbq3k\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>When you approach the 2020 Vanquish, its quality hits you immediately. The lustre of the paint, the richness of the black chrome window surrounds, the new stance on more prominent wheels… they all modernise it. “I’m 20 years older than when I did this first,” says Callum, “and quite a lot has happened in the meantime. Life and fashion are different now. When the chance came to reconsider the car, I could see immediately what it needed.”</p> \n <p>The 5.9-litre Aston V12 engine gets light modifications (as well as a superb set of specially machined air intake stacks for beauty reasons) so that it now produces 580bhp – an extra 60bhp. Buyers can opt for a six-speed manual or conventional eight-speed automatic gearbox, or stick with the original car’s six-speed automated manual. Despite the bad publicity, some prefer that.</p> \n <p>Underneath, as a result of 20,000 miles of extensive testing, the car’s suspension has been rebushed and retuned with new springs, anti-roll bars and Bilstein dampers so that it rides 10mm lower and gets the best performance from Donfrancesco’s preferred Michelin Pilot Sport tyres. Even the steering wheel is stripped and machined to give a rim shape that Callum feels is more appropriate, and to reduce the diameter slightly, before being retrimmed.</p> \n <p>Such painstaking work isn’t cheap: buyers will pay around £450,000 if they bring their own car, preferably a Vanquish S (worth around £100,000). Alternatively, the team will find a suitable car on the market. The 25-strong batch is already half sold, even before most prospects have even seen a complete car, boding well for a successful completion.</p> \n <p>We spent two hours in Callum’s test car, a six-speed manual. The interior’s architecture is easily recognisable, but every surface gets a quality boost and a large range of textures and colours is now available. The seats are completely redesigned and mounted lower – something the original car badly needed. One fascinating feature is the tasteful use of what’s dubbed ‘Callum abstract tartan’ – a theme likely to be used in future creations. There’s a removable Bremont pocket watch mounted on the dashboard, too, and a custom Mulberry luggage set for the boot.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/95-callum-aston-martin-vanquish-25-fd-steering-wheel.jpg?itok=CaRaUIXH\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>As soon as you start to drive, it’s apparent the car has near-bottomless reserves of torque and power. Its V12 sounds quite different from that of the original Vanquish, courtesy of a re-engineered exhaust system that emits four distinct but harmonising sounds at once: treble and bass lines, a classic rustle from the valve gear and a faint, refined whine from the camshaft drive system. Also, a new exhaust box forms part of the large and effective underbody diffuser.</p> \n <p>Callum and Donfrancesco say the idea is to enhance the grand touring capabilities and driving quality of the Vanquish, and that’s most definitely what they’ve achieved. The engine isn’t obtrusive until it’s really pulling (which it can rarely do on a public road) and always sounds wonderful.</p> \n <p>The car rides flat and firm and has much better turn-in and grip than before, thanks to its modern hardware. It stops beautifully, too, using Aston’s latest-specification – and large – carbon-ceramic brakes.</p> \n <p>However, two things really stand out for me from the dynamic package. One is the new excellence of the steering, whose impressive precision and deliberate effort levels are now far more appropriate and deliver a whole new level of sophistication. The upshot is a much more directionally stable car.</p> \n <p>The other is the ride quality: flat, controlled and beautifully damped, accompanied by a refreshing lack of tyre noise, because so much work has been done to suppress the original obtrusive road roar. In all, the twin aims of enhancing driver reward and grand touring ability have both been impressively achieved.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/90-callum-aston-martin-vanquish-25-fd-otr-front.jpg?itok=xzEooA1_\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Callum and his friends are distinctly coy about what they might do next. After all, at their level of detail, this run of modified Vanquishes will take many months to complete. But it’s apparent that there might be an even more special Vanquish on the stocks and that other projects, automotive and otherwise, are already in the frame. Callum was once merely a designer. Now he’s a brand as well.</p> \n <p><strong>Aston Martin CALLUM Vanquish 25 by R-Reforged​ specification</strong></p> \n <p><b>Where</b> Warwickshire, UK&nbsp;<b>Price</b> £550,000&nbsp;<b>On sale</b> now&nbsp;<b>Engine</b> V12, 5935cc, petrol&nbsp;<b>Power</b> 580bhp&nbsp;<b>Torque</b> not specified&nbsp;<b>Gearbox</b> 6-spd manual&nbsp;<b>Kerb weight</b> 1835kg (estimated)&nbsp;<b>Top speed</b> 190mph (estimated)&nbsp;<b>0-62mph</b> 4.5sec (estimated)&nbsp;<b>Fuel economy</b> no WLTP figure available&nbsp;<b>CO2 </b>no WLTP figure available</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE&nbsp;</strong></p> \n +0000","feedId":13379,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"f3a37e9ab0d4dac739db3fa857e80341","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/99-callum-aston-martin-vanquish-25-fd-hero-front.jpg?itok=nHB4C9w5":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn70@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-50-44-897_42572be4bee61ae3.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/98-callum-aston-martin-vanquish-25-fd-hero-side.jpg?itok=dfhkbq3k":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn62@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-50-43-829_95f17a0054662216.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/95-callum-aston-martin-vanquish-25-fd-steering-wheel.jpg?itok=CaRaUIXH":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn29@2020_6/2020/09/05/08-50-44-717_24b64ca08f0658de.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/90-callum-aston-martin-vanquish-25-fd-otr-front.jpg?itok=xzEooA1_":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn98@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-50-45-849_c6ec0d7598f7d73c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295843551},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"Peugeot 5008 gains styling and interior tweaks for 2020","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/peugeot-5008-gains-styling-and-interior-tweaks-2020","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/peugeot-5008-gains-styling-and-interior-tweaks-2020\"><img height=\"125\" alt=\"2020 Peugeot 5008 facelift\" title=\"2020 Peugeot 5008 facelift\" /></a> SUV follows its 3008 sibling in receiving a new front end, revamped interior and overhauled trim line-up \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/peugeot\">Peugeot </a>has updated its&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/5008\">5008 family SUV</a> with a new look, enhanced technology and a streamlined trim structure, mirroring<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/peugeot-3008-receives-restyle-and-new-phev-option-2021\"> the recent facelift for its 3008 sibling</a>.</p> \n <p>Chief among the changes for the<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/skoda/kodiaq\"> Skoda Kodiaq</a> rival is a revised front end that brings the 5008 into line with Peugeot’s newer models, such as&nbsp;the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/208\">208 </a>and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/508\">508</a>. Like the 3008’s, it comprises a frameless grille that expands across the front, is connected to the bumper by fins and is flanked by the brand’s new fang-shaped daytime running lights.</p> \n <p>The model number has also been applied to the leading edge of the bonnet for the first time, with gloss black side scoops, painted tread plates and redesigned headlights rounding off the styling tweaks.</p> \n <p>LED headlights and brake lights&nbsp;are now fitted as standard across the range, with the rear ones now covered by a smoked panel that extends across the bootlid.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Inside, the 5008 gains Peugeot’s new i-Cockpit interior layout, comprising a 10.0in infotainment touchscreen, ‘piano key’ physical controls for essential functions and a customisable 12.3in digital gauge cluster that uses ‘normally black’ technology to offer higher-quality readouts than in the current car.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/peugeot_5008_2009styp_033.jpg?itok=Dv2FoX8N\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Wireless phone charging, Apple CarPlay and Android Auto are fitted at all trim levels and the facelift&nbsp;brings three new USB sockets.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>A drive mode selector is now standard on 5008 models equipped with an automatic gearbox, allowing drivers to choose between Normal, Sport and Eco. Driver aids – including night vision, adaptive cruise control, lane position assist, automatic emergency braking and an upgraded traffic sign recognition function – are also now standard fitments.</p> \n <p>As before, the 5008 can be specified with a choice of two petrol and two diesel engines, with power outputs ranging from 128bhp to 178bhp. The entry-level 1.2-litre three-cylinder petrol engine and 1.5-litre four-cylinder diesel can be specified with a six-speed manual gearbox or eight-speed automatic. The 1.6-litre four-cylinder petrol and 2.0-litre diesel are&nbsp;automatic only.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Three trim levels are available: Active, Allure and GT. Each can be upgraded with a bespoke ‘pack’ that brings additional equipment and styling changes. Entry-level Active trim, for example, features 17in aluminium wheels, hands-free start and dual-zone air conditioning, with the Allure Pack adding electrically folding mirrors, a front parking aid and a 180deg reversing camera.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Prices will be confirmed nearer to the model's launch&nbsp;towards the end of 2020 but can be expected to mark a slight increase on the 5008's current £28,980 starting price.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><strong>Read more</strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/peugeot-3008-receives-restyle-and-new-phev-option-2021\"><strong>Peugeot 3008 receives restyle and new PHEV option for 2021​</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/208\"><strong>Peugeot 208 review</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/peugeot/5008/first-drives/peugeot-5008-long-term-review\"><strong>Peugeot 5008 long-term review</strong></a></p> \n <p><span class=\"wysiwyg-embed\"></span></p> \n <iframe allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/vzx9uFsztlo\" width=\"560\"></iframe>\n <p></p> \n</div>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Thu, 03 Sep 2020 02:01:24 +0000","feedId":13379,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"ee2245d106594d1d920835a1db4356db","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/peugeot_5008_2009rc_008.jpg?itok=BPDA2SmK":null,"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/peugeot_5008_2009styp_033.jpg?itok=Dv2FoX8N":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn5@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-50-46-903_8c7a1c1d4cf5ff06.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295843550},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"Driving the secret cars of Toyota's heritage collection","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/driving-secret-cars-toyotas-heritage-collection","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/driving-secret-cars-toyotas-heritage-collection\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/30-toyota-and-lexus-heritage-fleet.jpg?itok=JWc8ppwp\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"Toyota and Lexus heritage fleet\" title=\"Toyota and Lexus heritage fleet\" /></a>\n<blockquote class=\"image-field-caption\">\n  The heritage fleet contains plenty of interesting and rare metal, including Toyota's first UK car\n</blockquote> Toyota and Lexus's UK heritage fleet is quite awesome and includes a 1994 RAV4 and original Lexus LFA \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>Cast your mind back, if you’re able, to the year 1994. May, to be precise. Manchester United have smashed Chelsea 4-0 in the FA Cup final, the Channel Tunnel has opened to great international fanfare and, of importance to car fans worldwide, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/toyota\">Toyota</a> has launched one of its boldest models in living memory: the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/rav4\">RAV4</a>.</p> \n <p>A curvy, quirky 4x4 designed more with surfers than soldiers in mind? Sacrilege to fans of the straight-edged, utilitarian <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jeep/wrangler\">Jeep Wrangler</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-land-rover-defender-2019\">Land Rover Defender</a> and even <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/used-cars/used-car-buying-guide-toyota-land-cruiser\">Toyota’s own Land Cruiser</a>. But the RAV4 wasn’t designed for them; it was made for young people who liked surfing, hiking and climbing, and it laid the foundations for the modern crossover – a vehicle class that’s at once the most popular and most polarising on the market.</p> \n <p>All of which goes some way to explaining why a blue short-wheelbase example, specified in lowly GS trim, currently takes pride of place in Toyota UK’s heritage fleet, when prices for even the most immaculate, top-rung RAV4s are some way south of the £6000 barrier. Fresh from a thorough and by all accounts arduous restoration, this example’s pristine exterior belies its 135,000-mile odometer reading.</p> \n <p>The first time Autocar drove the RAV4 on UK soil was in a 1994 twin test alongside a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/history-ford-rs-pictures\">Ford Escort RS2000</a> hot hatchback. A curious choice of contender, it seems, but here were two compact family runarounds, each with four-wheel drive and sporting aspirations. And where the Escort had the edge in outright power, the RAV4 pipped it in the lightweight stakes by around 65kg. And crucially, let’s not forget, when the RAV4 arrived, there was no<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/nissan/juke-2010-2019\"> Nissan Juke</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/ford/puma\">Ford Puma</a> or <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/skoda/karoq\">Skoda Karoq</a> to benchmark it against.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/29-toyota-rav-4.jpg?itok=lAYfl8j5\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Despite the odd pairing, this was a highly anticipated face-off; hot hatchbacks in the vein of the RS2000 had become almost impossible to insure for the average driver, while conventional off-roaders such as the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jeep/wrangler\">Wrangler</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/land-rover/discovery\">Land Rover Discovery</a> were simply too cumbersome and thirsty for everyday road usage.</p> \n <p>A new niche had to be explored, and so came the RAV4, essentially sitting between the two segments, providing a happy medium between usability, fun and affordability. It wasn’t particularly quick, granted, but a proven 0-62mph time of 8.8sec in our test was enough to embarrass the rally-honed <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/ford/escort\">Escort</a>, and allowing its driver to see over hedges and tackle the steepest of speed bumps without inviting costly bodywork repairs was a welcome bonus.</p> \n <p>Get behind the wheel now and you soon find that this curvy little 4x4’s connotations of pace and poise are faint at best. Compared with today’s crop of genuinely sporty compact SUVs, powered as they are by buzzy turbo triples or torquey diesel lumps, the RAV4’s naturally aspirated 2.0-litre engine feels a bit gutless, and the thrumming noise it makes at idle is rather more reminiscent of barns than beaches.</p> \n <p>Climb up through the gears, however, and it’s plain to see where the RAV4’s enduring appeal lies. Even on empty, flat and generally untroubling suburban streets, it inspires a confidence that’s often missing from today’s diminutive runarounds, which aren’t so disparate in terms of footprint.</p> \n <p>Potholes, kerbs and cobbles are hardly a challenging test for any 4x4, but the sense of solidity in the RAV4 is pervasive and hints at the all-terrain ability that set this car aside from its contemporary competitors and arguably even its spiritual descendants. No wonder around 90% of all RAV4s ever built are still roadworthy.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"599\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/26-toyota-mr2.jpg?itok=JXOnMEt1\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The cabin isn’t exactly inspiring by today’s standards, dominated as it is by grey plastic, black vinyl and hefty manual controls, but there’s a certain charm to be found in its honesty and, without sliding into nostalgic cliché, it’s far more intuitively laid out than the majority of newer examples.</p> \n <p>That lack of pretention, coupled with the RAV4’s enduring popularity, means that, despite the novelty of driving what is essentially a museum exhibit on public roads, no one stops and stares, bombards us with questions when we stop or rushes to snap a picture for Instagram. This is the ideal quasi-classic car for introverts: simple, affordable and subtle.</p> \n <p>Back in the flattering light of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/toyota\">Toyota’s</a> workshop and with its fresh paint polished to within an inch of its life, it’s clear just how much time and effort has been devoted to saving N897 VHN. Once the previous owner’s self-applied plastic wheel arch trims were removed to uncover near-fatal amounts of corrosion, it became obvious this was to be more than a spit-and-polish clean-up job.</p> \n <p>In a saga more befitting a priceless 1960s <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/lamborghini\">Lamborghini</a>, this RAV4’s recommissioning turned into a full-bore restoration, with the team even going so far as to buy a donor car for the sole purpose of removing its entire roof, their own car having been fitted with a leaky, non-factory-specification aftermarket sunroof.</p> \n <p>But the RAV4 isn’t the only artefact in Toyota’s workshop-cum-museum that’s worth gawping at, and it’s certainly not the car that gets the most attention. Nestled at the back of a nondescript warehouse in Sussex are some of Toyota’s and Lexus’s most important, acclaimed and popular models, kept so that they can be rolled out for big events and magazine features such as this.</p> \n <p>Behind a row of 2020 <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/toyota-tweaks-corollas-looks\">Corollas</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/first-drives/toyota-c-hr-long-term-review\">C-HRs</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/camry\">Camrys</a>, we discover proper bedroom-wall-worthy classics, including an original MR2 sports car and a legendary rear-wheel-drive <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/toyota-launches-new-heritage-division-reproduced-supra-parts\">Corolla AE86 </a>– the thinking man’s drift weapon. Full-time press fleet technician Mike Croft doesn’t hesitate in choosing the latter as his pick of the bunch. “There aren’t many of these about, especially in this sort of condition,” he says. “There are a lot of imports, rather than genuine UK cars like this one.”</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/22-lexus-lfa.jpg?itok=cP4C58n8\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>This comes from a man who was once one of just five technicians in Europe trained to work on <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/lexus/lfa/first-drives/lexus-lfa\">Lexus’s ultra-exclusive LFA hypercar</a> – an example of which sits just metres away, well out of range of door dings and dropped spanners.</p> \n <p>The 11-year-old LFA has firmly established itself as one of the most spine-tingling supercars of all time. Its 4.8-litre V10 engine revs up to its 9400rpm limit so quickly that an analogue tachometer wouldn’t be able to keep up. Its bodywork is made of carbonfibre composite and it took nearly a decade to develop.</p> \n <p>But Croft isn’t too fazed by its reputation. “Bits of it are different,” he says. “It’s got a torque tube rather than a propshaft, so the engine and clutch are at the front and the gearbox at the back. But generally, it just needs servicing and it holds up really well, even on the track.”</p> \n <p>We dare not move the LFA from its clearly designated parking spot to see for ourselves, but a quick blip of the throttle is evidence enough that this is something pretty special even by supercar standards.</p> \n <p>Croft says the oldest car in the collection, an immaculate 1966 <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/advice/coronavirus-what-motorists-need-know\">Corona</a>, is equally trouble-free. Pleasingly unmodified, save for the addition of a modern stereo (a boon on longer trips, which it still undertakes from time to time), it sits between a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/yaris-grmn\">Yaris GRMN</a>, kept on following the hot supermini’s relatively recent media launch, and a wackily restyled <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/aygo\">Aygo</a> city car, aptly called <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/aygo/first-drives/toyota-aygo-crazy\">Crazy</a> – as the ‘graffiti’ adorned across its widened flanks suggests.</p> \n <p>Crazy is what happens when you remove the rear seats from your boggo runabout, replace them with a 200bhp turbocharged motor, bolt on a rear wing from a genuine Champ Car and install a limited-slip differential… at the rear. Forget the regular Aygo’s future classic potential; this is nothing less than a rare display of lunacy from one of the industry’s more reputedly ‘sane’ companies. It thoroughly deserves a spot in the history books.</p> \n <p>As does, you could argue, the rally-ready first-generation <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/prius\">Prius</a> that’s halfway through a thorough refresh on the other side of the workshop. Created in 2002 to demonstrate the reliability of what was then a completely newfangled powertrain, this stripped-out eco warrior took part in the arduous Midnight Sun to Red Sea rally from Sweden to Jordan in 2002, and it didn’t do too badly, in spite of its electrified innards’ heft.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"599\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/24-mike-croft-and-felix-page.jpg?itok=DNOM867N\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Stickered up and with a spartan interior, it’s a far cry from the Prius that took you home from your last night out, and it played a pivotal role in the model’s early success. Hybrid technology has come a long way since, but this is yet another example of how even some of seemingly the most mundane and mainstream cars will enjoy a long-lasting legacy.</p> \n <p>Even more unexpected is the newest addition to Toyota’s treasure trove: a 2001 <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/yaris\">Yaris</a> that’s unassuming in the extreme – until you take a closer look at its odometer. Yes, it really has covered just 149 miles since it left the showroom almost two decades ago. The story goes that it was bought in Ireland, clipped the garage door when it arrived at the new owner’s home, was then repaired and has been dry-stored ever since.</p> \n <p>To all intents and purposes, it’s a brand new car – even the original tyres are present and correct – and it has now been given a permanent home here among the Toyota and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/lexus\">Lexus</a> greats.</p> \n <p>Should we have to justify the ‘classic’ status of some of these cars? Certainly there will be dissenters who argue that budget runarounds are disposable, and let’s not pretend a base-spec city car could hold its own at a concours d’élégance. But these cars have done far more for mass mobility than the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/electrified-aston-martin-db6-driving-future-proof-classic\">Aston Martin DB6</a>,<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/%C2%A352m-ferrari-250-gto-becomes-most-expensive-car-ever-sold\"> Ferrari 250 GTO</a> or <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mclaren/f1-1992-1998\">McLaren F1</a> ever did and are therefore surely deserving of some sort of commemoration.</p> \n <p>Croft sums it up pretty concisely in describing how new members of the fleet are selected. “The criteria are: very good condition, low mileage or something that’s a bit rare,” he says. “If you can get all of that, perfect.”</p> \n <p>With hypercars, track toys and even the hilarious one-off <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-video/video-toyota-hilux-bruiser-vs-110-tamiya-bruiser-rc-road-showdown\">Hilux Bruiser pick-up</a> truck on its roster, this heritage fleet is living proof that automotive history is worth not only preserving but driving as well.</p> \n <p><strong>Meeting a hero: the original MR2</strong></p> \n <p>Squat, compact, angular and resplendent as this example is in Super Red, it’s easy to see why the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/used-car-buying-guides/investment-cars-less-%C2%A310000-used-car-buying-guide\">Mk1 Toyota MR2</a> is nicknamed the baby <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/ferrari\">Ferrari</a>. Back away and squint and it could almost be an <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/ferrari/f40-1987-1992\">F40</a>.</p> \n <p>Mounted amidships is a naturally aspirated 1.6-litre four-cylinder engine borrowed from the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/corolla-touring-sports/interior\">contemporary Corolla</a>, which calls upon 127bhp and 97lb ft to send this 1030kg two-seat coupé from 0-62mph in 8.5sec – competitive for its time (1984 to 1989).</p> \n <p>Crashes and corrosion have diminished the MR2’s number over the past three decades, so it cuts a somewhat unfamiliar figure out on public roads. That’s fortunate, because if it weren’t for other road users staring, there’s every chance it could vanish under the wheels of a passing lorry. Vulnerability somewhat overrides the sense of fun around town, so sweeping B-roads provide the best opportunity for seeing if this car has stood the test of time.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/18-toyota-mr2_0.jpg?itok=5DRbt6__\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Affordable sports cars have come a long way since 1987, so a factory-spec MR2 is unlikely to be your track-day weapon of choice. Nor will it show many of today’s normal cars a clean pair of heels out on the road.</p> \n <p>But, that being said, its low ride height, point-and-shoot handling and the throaty growl of its twin-cam motor, not to mention its near-7000rpm redline, offer enjoyment on a different level. This is no longer a competitive sports car, so it doesn’t need to be driven like one. On most roads in the UK, at least, you’re guaranteed to have more fun than in any <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/lamborghini\">Lamborghini</a> or <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/pagani\">Pagani</a>, and without attracting quite so much unwanted attention from the authorities. Or crashing.</p> \n <p>However, the non-assisted steering is shockingly heavy for a car with such a light front end, your rearward visibility is sub-par at best and the luggage capacity is poor. But at around £7000 for a clean example, the Mk1 MR2 would be an enviable Sunday afternoon casual cruiser indeed.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-2020-toyota-yaris-priced-%C2%A319910-uk\">New 2020 Toyota Yaris priced from £19,910 in UK</a></strong></p> \n <p><iframe allow=\"accelerometer; Ohlins dampers… this is an E-Type, but not quite as you know it Ask me to configure a car to get down my favourite road and it would go something like this.It would need to be light, of course, and quite but not overwhelmingly powerful. I’d like to find the engine ahead of me and the driven wheels behind. That engine should have more than four cylinders and power the rear wheels through a manual gearbox. And the car should be slender, so it has more of its own side of the road on which to play. Fully independent suspension and disc brakes are, of course, a must, too.What I’ve just described to you is a 1960s Jaguar E-Type. But were you to find such a car, even if its condition reflected that in which it left the factory all those years ago, it would likely be charming on such a road, but not very good. It would be quite slow to gain speed and even slower, relatively, to lose it. It would wobble about over the humps and crests, and if you really gave it the beans, there’s a decent chance it would break.But imagine an E-Type designed today to that outline specification, but with modern tolerances, metallurgy and an attention to detail many hundreds of times greater than that enjoyed by a normal production car like a standard E-Type. If you did, and your mind was unusually fertile, you might just come up with this, the Eagle Lightweight GT.You may know Eagle and some of its more extraordinary E-Type-themed creations of the past few years. Well, this is the most extraordinary of all: a car costing over £800,000, with a waiting list of at least 18 months, during which 8500 man hours will be lovingly devoted to its creation. front\" title=\"2020 Jeep Wrangler 4xe - front\" /></a> Electrified Wrangler will be the UK's most powerful version and is capable of a 25-mile electric range \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/jeep\">Jeep</a> has introduced a new plug-in hybrid version of its <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jeep/wrangler\">Wrangler off-roader</a>, launching globally in early 2021 with 370bhp and up to 25 miles of electric-only range.</p> \n <p>The new Wrangler 4xe joins <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/jeep-renegade-4xe-phev-full-production-details-released\">hybrid versions of the Renegade </a>and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jeep/compass\">Compass</a> SUVs, revealed earlier this year and set for a UK launch in the coming months, as <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/hybrids-lead-jeeps-green-future-first-evs-follow\">Jeep gears up to electrify its entire model line-up</a> in the coming years.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The electrified Wrangler is described as the most “technically advanced and eco-friendly” iteration of the iconic 4x4 yet produced and is said to offer enhanced usability, both on&nbsp;and off road, over the standard car.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The new model’s electrified powertrain combines a 2.0-litre turbocharged four-cylinder petrol engine with a 400V, 17kWh battery pack that recuperates energy from a belt-integrated starter/generator under deceleration and can power a pair of electric motors, one mounted in front of the engine and the other just forward of the gearbox. The battery can also be replenished&nbsp;via a conventional charging port located on the front left wing.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Like the non-electrified Wrangler, four-wheel drive features, with power sent from the combustion motor to both axles through an eight-speed automatic gearbox.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The Wrangler 4xe’s combined 370bhp output represents a 102bhp increase over the most potent model currently available in the UK and its 470lb ft torque output is a 59% increase.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The battery pack is mounted underneath the rear seat for optimal protection from the elements, while preserving the standard car’s interior dimensions, and is cooled using the Wrangler’s air conditioning refrigerant. With comprehensive weatherproofing around all new electrical components, the Wrangler 4xe can match the non-electrified car’s 30in wading depth.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Three drive modes are available: Hybrid, which uses the combustion and electric motors in conjunction; Electric, which shuts out the combustion motor until the battery’s charge is depleted; and eSave, which uses the petrol engine exclusively. A new ‘Eco Coaching’ display allows drivers to monitor power flow and optimise use of regenerative braking, schedule charge times and view driving history.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>A ‘Max Regen’ function can be used to optimise electrical energy generation, using ‘more assertive’ regenerative braking.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Jeep claims that the “seamless integration of electric power into the 4x4 drivetrain elevates the Wrangler 4xe to new levels of off-road performance”. Instant torque in electric mode allows for a “more precise and controlled driving experience for climbing and crawling”, while conserving fuel and minimising noise.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Three trim levels are available. Entry-level 4xe and mid-range Sahara trims are equipped with full-time four-wheel drive, a two-speed transfer case and heavy-duty Dana 44 axles. The top-range Rubicon model brings an upgraded Rock-Track 4x4 system, axle lockers, improved articulation and a front sway bar disconnect for improved suspension travel.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Styling across the Wrangler 4xe line-up is nearly identical to that of the standard car, but blue tow hooks, badging and interior elements mark it out as the hybrid car.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Jeep boss Christian Meunier said: “We are committed to make Jeep the greenest SUV brand. The electrification of the Jeep line-up will allow commuters to travel solely on electric power, delivering an efficient and fun on-road experience and offering an ability to enjoy even more Jeep capability off road in nearly complete silence.”</p> \n <p>Prices for the new Wrangler 4xe hybrid are yet to be confirmed, but it is expected to be priced in line with the current Rubicon range-topper, available from around £51,000.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><strong>Read more</strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-jeep-grand-wagoneer-concept-previews-premium-suv-2021\"><strong>New Jeep Grand Wagoneer concept previews premium SUV for 2021</strong></a></p> \n width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"2020 Jeep Grand Wagoneer concept - front\" title=\"2020 Jeep Grand Wagoneer concept - front\" /></a> Wagoneer nameplate revived for family of premium SUVs, topped by tech-heavy Range Rover rival \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/jeep\">Jeep</a> is reviving the storied Wagoneer nameplate for a new family of premium SUVs and has previewed the range-topping Grand Wagoneer with a bold new concept that blends modern styling cues with nods to the iconic original car.</p> \n <p>The first Wagoneer – launched in 1962 - is <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/slideshow/how-jeeps-wagoneer-became-original-luxury-suv\">widely recognised as an early pioneer of the premium SUV segment</a>&nbsp;and Jeep said “its return allows us to expand to a much more premium arena with new levels of design detail and advanced safety and technology features”.</p> \n <p>The firm claims the Grand Wagoneer concept was designed with a dual focus on modernity and authenticity and “encapsulates the future of the ultimate premium SUV”. When it is&nbsp;launched in 2021, the Grand Wagoneer will supersede the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jeep/grand-cherokee\">Grand Cherokee </a>as Jeep’s flagship model and compete with more upmarket models, including the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/land-rover/range-rover\">Range Rover</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/x5\">BMW X5</a>. It's not currently destined for the UK or Europe, however.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The production car will be available with a choice of three four-wheel drive systems, independent front and rear suspension and Jeep’s Quadra-Lift air suspension, hinting that off-road capability remains a priority despite the luxury shift.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Technical details remain unconfirmed, but the Grand Wagoneer concept features a plug-in hybrid powertrain, likely closely matched to that of the new <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/jeep-renegade-4xe-phev-full-production-details-released\">Renegade and Wrangler 4xe PHEVs</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"597\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/2022-jeep-grand-wagoneer-concept-15.jpg?itok=nEuTY4QS\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Although the production design is tipped to&nbsp;be toned down slightly, the concept gives a good idea of what to expect from the Grand Wagoneer.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Elements such as the modernised interpretation of Jeep’s trademark seven-vent front grille, for example, will probably&nbsp;be carried over wholesale. Although familiar from models such as the Wrangler, Renegade and Gladiator, the intake has been updated with black trim accents and latticework inserts and is framed by a new LED signature light design, which is said to emphasise the car’s width.</p> \n <p>The concept also features LED projector headlights surrounded by genuine teak wood - a detail unlikely to make its way to production - in reference to the original Wagoneer’s wooden side panelling. Prevalent front tow hooks and a chunky black aluminium skid plate hint at its off-road capability.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The Grand Wagoneer concept features trapezoidal wheel arches like Jeep’s production cars but has 24in aluminium wheels, which - as is often the way with concept cars - will be downsized for showrooms. The copper-finished badges on the doors, bearing a new font&nbsp;designed specifically for the concept, will likely make production, though.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/2022-jeep-grand-wagoneer-concept-rear-motion.jpg?itok=KoaUnPq4\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Also likely to feature on the production car are the concept’s wraparound LED rear light clusters, subtle rear diffuser, roof rails and panoramic sunroof.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The Grand Wagoneer’s interior will offer a seven-seat layout for the first time in the model’s history&nbsp;and marks a radical shift away from the firm’s customarily utilitarian cabin design language.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Large windows, together with the full-length glass roof, offer comprehensive all-round visibility. Glass has also been used throughout the cabin itself as it’s a “sustainable, fully recyclable material that provides environmental benefits and is made of an abundant natural raw material”, according to Jeep.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>A black glass trim element runs the width of the concept’s dashboard and aluminium has been used for the dashboard support, speaker surrounds and gearstick. In a further nod to the model’s heritage, wood inlays feature on the instrument display and door panels.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Additional sustainable materials used on the concept include Dinamica microfibre suede for the headliner, recycled ‘Thrive’ carpets and ‘PUR’ synthetic upholstery on the seats, doors, console and instrument panel.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/2022-jeep-grand-wagoneer-concept-front-row-broad.jpg?itok=-M96r4bL\" width=\"900\" />&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The instrument panel itself is dominated by four large digital displays spanning a total of 45in: a 12.3in digital instrument display, a 12.1in central infotainment touchscreen, a 10.25in climate control touchscreen panel and a 10.25in touchscreen mounted directly in front of the passenger seat.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The second-row passengers also each get their own 10.1in infotainment touchscreen, with access to another 10.25in climate control touchscreen. The car’s infotainment system runs on Fiat Chrysler Automobiles’ latest-generation, Android-based Uconnect 5 software, which is claimed to run five times faster than that used by current production cars.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The concept’s 23-speaker, 24-channel audio system was developed by home audio brand McIntosh - making its automotive debut here - and is finished in the same aluminium and gloss black design as its existing products.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Christian Meunier, global president of the Jeep brand, said: \"With the electrification of each Jeep nameplate coming in the next few years, and the reintroduction of Wagoneer, we are quickly expanding into new segments and more premium space.&nbsp;“Wagoneer is unquestionably rooted in the legendary Jeep brand and its unmatched heritage of leading capability, authenticity and freedom, and its return allows us to expand to a much more premium arena with new levels of design detail, and advanced safety and technology features.\"</p> \n <p>He added: “The new Grand Wagoneer Concept is our vision of what a modern expression of this timeless icon can be, and hints at how we will redefine and recreate the benchmark premium SUV.”</p> \n
