front\" title=\"2020 Vauxhall Mokka - front\" /></a> Pair of 1.2-litre petrol engines and a 1.5-litre diesel for Vauxhall's bold new compact crossover \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/vauxhall\">Vauxhall</a> has detailed the petrol and diesel-powered variants of its radically restyled Mokka crossover, following the recent unveiling of the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/vauxhall-mokka-overhauled-new-generation-gains-ev-model\">all-electric Mokka-e</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Sitting atop the PSA Group’s Common Modular Platform (CMP), which can accommodate both combustion and electric powertrains, the Mokka will be available with the same choice of three engines - two petrol and one diesel - as its <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-frankfurt-motor-show/new-peugeot-2008-and-e-2008-prices-and-specs-revealed\">Peugeot 2008 sibling</a>.</p> \n <p>The entry-level option, a 1.2-litre turbocharged three-cylinder petrol, produces 99bhp and 151lb ft. Paired exclusively with a six-speed manual gearbox, it can manage between 49.6 and 51.4mpg on the WLTP cycle, while emitting 124-128g/km of CO2, according to preliminary figures.</p> \n <p>The more potent petrol option, using the same 1.2-litre block, pushes out 134bhp&nbsp;and 170lb ft&nbsp;for a 0-62mph time of 9.2 seconds, 1.8 seconds faster than the base motor. It can be optionally specified with an eight-speed automatic gearbox, and achieves between 50.4 and 51.4mpg, emitting 123-126g/km.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/vauxhall-mokka-512768.jpg?itok=o_n-1294\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Both petrol engines are said to offer “high efficiency and lively performance”, courtesy of their low-friction design and quick-reacting turbocharger, which boosts torque from low RPMs.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The Mokka also receives a 1.5-litre diesel option with 109bhp&nbsp;and 184lb ft. It’s available with the six-speed manual gearbox and manages 62.8-65.7mpg while emitting 114-117g/km.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Visually identical to the electric version, the new Mokka features Vauxhall’s new ‘Vizor’ front end and is characterised by its short overhangs and widened stance compared to the outgoing Mokka X. Although its wheelbase is slightly longer than that of its predecessor, it is 12.5cm shorter overall, weighs 120kg less and - in the case of the electric version - is up to 30% stiffer.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Inside, the compact SUV features a pair of widescreen digital displays - a 12.0in gauge cluster and 7.0in or 10.0in infotainment touchscreen - but retains separate controls for essential functions, “avoiding hazardous exploration into sub-menus”. Leather, Alcantara and standard cloth upholsteries are available, while the front seats are six-way adjustable as standard.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Like the Mokka-e, the combustion-powered car is equipped with an array of driver assist programmes as standard, including forward collision alert, automatic emergency braking and pedestrian detection. Adaptive cruise control, intelligent LED headlights and wireless phone charging are also equipped as standard.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>For the first time, the Mokka will be available in performance-inspired SRi range-topping trim, marked out from the standard car by its gloss black front grille, chrome exterior trim, 18in two-tone alloy wheels and red side window frame.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Pricing has yet to be confirmed, but the new Mokka can be expected to closely match its 2008 sibling. Expect a starting price of around £20,150 for the combustion car and £28,000 for the electric variant when the pair hit showrooms early next year.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><strong>Read more</strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-frankfurt-motor-show/new-peugeot-2008-and-e-2008-prices-and-specs-revealed\"><strong>New Peugeot 2008 and e-2008: prices and specs revealed​</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/vauxhall-mokka-overhauled-new-generation-gains-ev-model\"><strong>Vauxhall Mokka overhauled for new generation, gains EV model​</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/long-term-reviews/vauxhall-corsa-2020-long-term-review\"><strong>Vauxhall Corsa 2020 long-term review​</strong></a></p> \n <p><span class=\"wysiwyg-embed\"></span></p> \n <iframe allow=\"accelerometer; On the passenger car front, the all-electric Zoe supermini has been the competent and really quite pretty face of this campaign for the past decade or so; while the Kangoo ZE went on to become the best-selling commercial EV in Europe by the end of 2019. The dinky Twizy made for a fascinating support act, too.Now, though, Renault has broadened its portfolio of electrified vehicles to include powertrains that the man on the street might deem to be more accessible. So there’s a hybrid version of the Clio supermini; a new plug-in hybrid Mégane Sport Tourer estate; and this, the new Captur E-Tech PHEV.Based on the Renault-Nissan-Mitsubishi Alliance’s CMF-B platform, it makes use of a normally aspirated 1.6-litre four-cylinder petrol engine, which is paired with a 49kW electric motor and a smaller integrated starter-generator. These draw their energy from a smallish battery that’s housed beneath the rear passenger bench, and which has a usable capacity of 7.5kWh for a WLTP-certified electric-only range of 30 miles.Plugged into a dedicated home wallbox (which Renault currently provides free of charge via BP Chargemaster), its battery can be topped up from 0-100% capacity in around three hours. Drive is directed to the front wheels via a specially developed multi-mode dog-clutch gearbox that has six forward speeds.The system has a fairly modest combined output of 158bhp. Renault doesn’t specify a system output for torque, but individually the petrol engine develops 103lb ft at 3200rpm, while the electric motor produces 184lb ft. On paper, performance isn’t particularly electric, then; the Captur&nbsp;PHEV can accelerate from 0-62mph in 10.1sec, which is three-tenths of a second slower than the plug-in Mégane with which it shares its powertrain.","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Wed, 02 Sep 2020 05:01:24 +0000","feedId":13379,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"02ca8c72c9248681623228cae47157ef","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/1-renault-captur-e-tech-2020-uk-fd-hero-front.jpg?itok=ClOPA_cI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn42@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-50-43-663_fd307c1b3d9db084.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295843551},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"2021 Mercedes S-Class: luxury saloon reinvented with tech focus","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2021-mercedes-s-class-luxury-saloon-reinvented-tech-focus","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2021-mercedes-s-class-luxury-saloon-reinvented-tech-focus\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/99-mercedes-benz-s-class-official-reveal-tracking-front.jpg?itok=ZJAixM-p\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"2021 Mercedes-Benz S-Class official reveal images - tracking front\" title=\"2021 Mercedes-Benz S-Class official reveal images - tracking front\" /></a> Luxury four-door sheds weight and gains refinement, host of new interior features and extra PHEV range \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>The newly revealed <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/s-class\">S-Class saloon</a> is described as the most technically advanced car that Mercedes-Benz has ever placed into series production.</p> \n <p>Set for UK delivery in early 2021, the luxurious four-door has been comprehensively re-engineered around a new body structure that’s claimed to be 60kg lighter than the old S-Class’s despite added levels of rigidity and, it’s claimed, even greater refinement.</p> \n <p>Key among the revisions to the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/audi/a8\">Audi A8 </a>and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/7-series\">BMW 7 Series</a> rival is a newly developed plug-in petrol-electric hybrid drivetrain. The new S580e model promises an electric range of up to 62 miles on the WLTP test cycle. That’s more than double the zero-emission range of its predecessor, the S560e.</p> \n <p>Despite a renewed focus on electrification, though, Mercedes has confirmed to Autocar that it will hold true to a tradition started in 1992 by continuing to offer the S-Class with a twin-turbocharged 6.0-litre V12 petrol engine. It will be used by a new, yet to be revealed replacement for <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-maybach-gls-600-arrives-rival-bentley-bentayga\">the Maybach S650 flagship</a>.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/97-mercedes-benz-s-class-official-reveal-tracking-tracking-rear.jpg?itok=B8X5TZhV\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Bringing it in line with its key rivals, the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mercedes-benz\">Mercedes</a> flagship also offers buyers the choice of two optional rear-wheel steering systems, the most extreme of which provides the rear wheels with up to 10deg of steering angle and a turning circle that’s 1.9m tighter than the old car’s, at 10.9m, less than the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/a-class\">A-Class hatchback’s</a>. The system also boosts high-speed stability as well as low-speed manoeuvrability.</p> \n <p>In a significant move, the new S-Class, codenamed W223, will be the first Mercedes model to offer level three autonomous driving capability at speeds of up to 37mph. Although not planned from the beginning of deliveries, the new Drive Pilot system, which uses lidar among a range of different sensors, will be introduced during the second half of 2021. It allows the driver to go hands-off for extended periods in high traffic density and “suitable sections of motorway”, Mercedes says, although LED lights integrated into the steering wheel prompt the driver to take control when necessary.</p> \n <p>The Drive Pilot system can be bundled with a new function called Intelligent Park Pilot. Offered in countries where legislation permits its use, it employs level four autonomous tech to allow the driver to remotely park the new S-Class from outside the car in garages with the necessary infrastructure via a smartphone app. The system can seek out usable spaces by itself and park of its own accord.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"506\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/88-mercedes-benz-s-class-official-reveal-studio-dashboard.jpg?itok=h5i2vtW8\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The S-Class’s reputation for cutting-edge headlight technology is boosted by an optional Digital Light function. Made up of three main LEDs that, through refraction, achieve a resolution of more than 1.3 million pixels per headlight, it allows the projection of warning symbols on to the road for added safety.</p> \n <p>A further first for the S-Class is over-the-air update capability to reduce dealer visits. Many of the developments in the new S-Class will also appear on <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/mercedes-eq-s-be-flagship-%C2%A39bn-electric-model-blitz\">Mercedes’ new pure-electric EQ S</a>, aimed at competing with<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/tesla/model-s\"> the Tesla Model S</a> and forthcoming <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-frankfurt-motor-show/bmw-i-vision-dynamics-concept-inspired-i5-spark-new-era-i\">BMW i7</a>.</p> \n <p>The existing S-Class Coupé and Cabriolet are not due to be replaced, leaving the saloon, in both short and long-wheelbase guises, as the only S-Class bodystyle. As with the outgoing model, it will sire various <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/vehicles/mercedes-amg\">AMG</a>, Maybach and Pullman derivatives.</p> \n <p>The S-Class has undergone a thorough redesign for 2021. While the smooth surfacing, understated sculpting and flowing C-pillar treatment remain familiar from its predecessor, the new model sports a bolder-looking grille, slimmer headlights and new horizontally mounted tail-lights that extend into a bootlid that is not so different from the current CLS’s.</p> \n <p>For the first time on the S-Class, Mercedes is giving buyers a choice of door handles: conventional grip handles come as standard and new flush-fitting electric pop-out handles are among a long list of optional equipment.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"602\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/86-mercedes-benz-s-class-official-reveal-studio-infotainment.jpg?itok=5Romnk42\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The new S-Class is bigger than the car it replaces but not significantly so. The long-wheelbase version is 34mm longer than before, at 5255mm, with a 51mm increase in the wheelbase, at 3216mm. Width is also up by 55mm, at 1954mm, and the new car is 12mm taller, at 1503mm.</p> \n <p>Rear leg room is claimed to have risen by 24mm in the long-wheelbase model, although rear shoulder room has actually decreased by 32mm. Boot capacity is up by 20 litres to 550 litres.</p> \n <p>Despite a larger frontal area, Mercedes says, the drag co-efficient has been reduced from a previous 0.24 to a class-leading 0.22, making it one of the most aerodynamically efficient cars to enter series production.</p> \n <p>In contrast to the evolved exterior, the interior has been comprehensively redesigned with developments that will be mirrored on future Mercedes models, including the upcoming <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2021-mercedes-benz-c-class-mule-reveals-production-design\">fifth-generation C-Class </a>due in December.</p> \n <p>Up front, there’s a new-look dashboard with substantial trim elements, including open-pore wood veneer with aluminium inlays, and four centrally mounted rectangular air vents in the upper fascia. Key features include a 12.3in digital instrument display with an optional 3D function as well as an 11.9in portrait-format central touchscreen dominating the centre console. Climate functions are incorporated into this screen.</p> \n <p>There are 27 fewer analogue controls than before, with the emphasis shifted to swipe, voice and gesture controls via a further developed MBUX operating system. An advanced new head-up display featuring augmented reality and a display area claimed to be equivalent to a 77in monitor comes as an option, as does a new 30-speaker, 1750W Burmester 4D sound system that has subwoofers in the backrests of the front seats.</p> \n <p>The rear, meanwhile, receives two optional 11.6in touchscreen displays sited in the back of the front seats, also using MBUX software, in combination with a control tablet that can be used both in and outside the car. Other key developments include a rear-seat airbag that deploys from the back of the front seats.</p> \n <p>At launch, the new S-class will be offered with two in-line six-cylinder engines – both carried over from the outgoing sixth-generation car – in an initial four-model line-up.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/94-mercedes-benz-s-class-official-reveal-studio-side.jpg?itok=v9m7hNEb\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>A turbocharged 3.0-litre mild-hybrid petrol unit develops 362bhp in the S450 and 429bhp in the S500. There is also a turbocharged 2.9-litre diesel with 282bhp in the S350d and 325bhp (10bhp less than the model it replaces) in the S400d.</p> \n <p>The six-cylinder petrol engine benefits from electric boosting, with an extra 21bhp provided under acceleration by an integrated starter motor, together with brake energy recuperation and off-throttle coasting. The launch engines are mated to a nine-speed automatic gearbox.</p> \n <p>The S350d offers the choice of either rear-wheel drive or optional 4Matic four-wheel drive. All of the other launch models are four-wheel drive as standard. Further drivetrains will follow, including a 48V mild-hybrid version of Mercedes’ turbocharged 4.0-litre V8 500bhp in the S580. That model will be joined in 2021 by the S580e, which uses a turbocharged 3.0-litre in-line six-cylinder petrol engine and gearbox-mounted electric motor with a combined output of 510bhp and its electric range of more than 62 miles is made possible by a 28kWh lithium ion battery.</p> \n <p>The V12-powered Maybach flagship will be unveiled at the Guangzhou motor show in November, although it is rumoured to develop a similar 621bhp to the model it replaces.</p> \n <p>Two new AMG-badged models – the S63e 4Matic+ and S73e 4Matic+ – are also under final development but not scheduled for UK delivery before mid-2021. Official details are still under wraps, but Autocar can confirm both are set to run Mercedes-AMG’s twin-turbocharged 4.0-litre V8 petrol engine in combination with an electric motor mounted within the rear axle operating on a 400V system and a lithium ion battery with a capacity around 20kWh.</p> \n <p>In the S63e, the electric motor is said to develop 134bhp, giving the car a combined system output that AMG insiders put at “close to 700bhp”.</p> \n <p>The S73e, meanwhile, is set to get a 201bhp electric motor for a combined 805bhp, making it the most powerful S-Class model yet.</p> \n <p>The new S-Class is underpinned by the second-generation MRA (modular rear architecture) platform and a chassis with tracks that are lengthened by 36mm at the front and 51mm at the rear.</p> \n <p>An Air Matic air suspension with adjustable damping control comes as standard, with an E-Active Body Control suspension featuring a new Impulse Side function. It raises the vehicle body by up to 80mm when radar sensors detect an impending side impact for improved crash energy absorption in the floorpan.</p> \n <p>The new S-Class will be produced on a new line at Mercedes’ Factory 56 facility in Sindelfingen, Germany.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"506\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/83-mercedes-benz-s-class-official-reveal-studio-rear-seats.jpg?itok=FnkeQtj3\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p><strong>Q&amp;A with Markus Schäfer, board member for Group Research and Development, Procurement and Supplier Quality</strong></p> \n <p><strong>You describe the S-Class as the most advanced car you’ve yet created. But there is loads of technology even in small cars these days. How do you differentiate and keep the S-Class relevant even with the luxury saloon market shrinking?&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p>“The outgoing S-Class was extraordinarily strong even right up to the end of its life - remember it had no MBUX, stuff we have on our smaller cars. But we have a very loyal customer base for S-Class - extremely loyal base&nbsp;</p> \n <p>“We are extremely confident - it’s an abundance of innovation there. If you talk about S-Class it defines for me the benchmark in intelligent luxury cars.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>“We work at every angle to make it intuitive to use. We want to make it so the car really recognises you and adjusts to you so you don’t have to adjust to the car. You walk to the car, the door handles pop out - it knows its you because you’ve logged in before - it has a three-step authentication that even enables you to do payment with your car. The gesture sensors and cameras in the car can anticipate what you intend to do before the action. The car is also OTA capable, not only for the UI and the screens but also car functions. There’s plenty of computing capacity in the car so it is ready for further updates.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>“It’s cutting-edge, to be fairly honest we are working hand in hand with regulators. We are so advanced here that in some instances there is no regulation to certify the car in certain countries.&nbsp;Take the digital lights - so the lights can perform 2.6m pixels. You can play a movie in your garage with the resolution the you have.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>“So we are still working with authorities in a couple of countries to get it working and on the road. Germany has a really progressive approach so we have it legal there, but it’s different in other countries. Same with Level 3 autonomous driving, second half of next year it will be live in Germany. There are so many features - some manufacturers have some in one car but this is has everything in one place, that’s what makes it unique. “</p> \n <p><strong>We know that your petrol plug-in S-Class will offer a class-leading range. Is there a diesel plug-in planned?&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p>“There is no diesel plug-in planned for the S-class. It’s available for example for the GLE, E-Class. Key markets for the S-Class is China, Korea and the US, it’s not predominantly a European car. Diesel is not the first choice for these countries.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>“As we have already announced there is an S-Class coming [EQS]- that’s the next drivetrain we are going to see, on the same production line [as S-Class]&nbsp; So I have to keep complexity somewhat in control, and we have to make choices. “</p> \n <p><strong>We know the S-Class Coupe and Cabriolet will not return with this model. Can you detail what the reason is for this?&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p>“If you go back in our history maybe 15 years back and look at the number of variants we were creating, we had an expansion strategy, we wanted to make three million units annually, we wanted to conquer different markets such as China.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>“Then we came face-to-face with transformation - in our powertrains - so we were adding plug-ins, now we are adding EV powertrains, so at some point we have to cut back on our complexity. So we are going to ‘weed out’ a little bit. They are great cars, the coupe and cabriolet, but I can tell you there is in one or the other fashion something coming that will replace it. If you look at the new SL coming, I think we will have many customers of the S-Class cabriolet looking at this car...</p> \n <p>“Cabriolets are not something for China, they are not that strong anymore in the US, so we have to make some choices. So we will have S-Class: short, long [wheelbase], Maybach, which will be very differentiated from the long versions, but we have other icons that we have not paid attention to for a while such as SL. “</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-ride-2020-mercedes-benz-s-class-prototype\">First ride: 2020 Mercedes-Benz It also appears to gain a clamshell bonnet and a higher beltline.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/dacia\">Dacia</a> has yet to confirm details of the new car’s powertrain, although given the Sandero will arrive after the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/analysis-how-will-car-makers-meet-new-co2-laws\">EU introduces strict new CO2 regulations in 2021</a>, there is the potential for some kind of hybrid system.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/2021-dacia-sandero-camo-winter-3.jpg?itok=OMuGi1aI\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Dacia's first fully electric&nbsp;car will arrive in 2021&nbsp;as a production version of<span>&nbsp;</span><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/new-dacia-suv-will-be-europes-most-affordable-ev\">the recent Spring Electric concept</a>, complementing the new Sandero.</p> \n <p>The 2021 Sandero is expected to be based on&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/renault\">Renault</a>'s&nbsp;new modular CMF&nbsp;platform.&nbsp;The <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/groupe-renault-sales-fall-349-first-half-2020\">Renault Group</a>,&nbsp;which owns Dacia,&nbsp;plans to have 80% of its models using this by 2022. height=\"125\" alt=\"Aston Martin Victor\" title=\"Aston Martin Victor\" /></a> Latest Q Commission creation combines One-77 and Vulcan underpinnings \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/aston-martin\">Aston Martin</a>'s&nbsp;bespoke Q Commission division has revealed its latest customer creation:&nbsp;a one-off supercar that combines elements of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/aston-martin-one-77-video\">the One-77</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/aston-martin-vulcan-flat-out-silverstone\">track-only Vulcan</a>.</p> \n <p>The Victor is the most powerful road-legal&nbsp;naturally aspirated car Aston Martin has yet produced. Its 7.3-litre V12 powerplant was stripped and rebuilt by Cosworth, with power raised from 750bhp to 836bhp and mated to a six-speed manual transmission.</p> \n <p>It uses the same inboard springs and dampers as the Vulcan&nbsp;and is fitted with Brembo carbon-ceramic brakes that Aston claims can deliver braking capability on par with a GT3 race car.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> \n <p>An aerodynamically optimised front splitter and rear diffuser produce 621lb ft&nbsp;of downforce at 100mph, which is more than a race-prepared <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/aston-martin/vantage\">Vantage</a> GT4.</p> \n <p>The car began life as a One-77 prototype that has been significantly overhauled over an 18-month period. It features extensive use of carbonfibre, with the entire chassis weighing less than an original One-77.</p> \n <p>The team used Aston’s muscle car era for inspiration, specifically the 1980s Vantage, and worked closely with the customer to develop the fully bespoke body. It borrowed elements from current Aston Martin models, including the rear rail light seen on the upcoming Valkyrie and vents found in the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/aston-martin/dbx/first-drives/aston-martin-dbx-2020-uk-review\">DBX SUV</a>.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/3000-aston-martin-victor.jpg?itok=f5Cbk4oA\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Inside, cashmere, polished titanium and walnut materials contrast with the leather-finished racing bucket seats and four-point harnesses, exposed carbonfibre and motorsport-derived steering wheel based the Vulcan’s.</p> \n <p>According to an Aston Martin representative, the Pentland Green paint dried mere hours before the car made its public debut at the Concours of Elegance at Hampton Court Palace.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>It was unveiled to commemorate the 70th anniversary of the Vantage name&nbsp;and named Victor after Victor Gauntlett, the man widely credited for reviving Aston's&nbsp;fortunes in the early 1980s. The car's owner, a Belgian collector, hasn't been named.</p> \n <p>Q by Aston Martin has previously worked on the company’s <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-aston-martin-db5-goldfinger-continuation-built\">DB5 Goldfinger Continuation models</a>&nbsp;and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-goodwood-festival-speed/limited-run-aston-martin-v12-vantage-v600-tackles\">limited-run V12 Vantage V600</a>.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-aston-martin-callum-vanquish-25-r-reforged\">First drive: Aston Martin Callum Vanquish 25 by R-Reforged</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/aston-martin-plots-long-wheelbase-dbx-and-coupe-version\">Aston Martin plots long-wheelbase DBX and coupe version</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/dear-tobias-how-new-ceo-can-fix-aston-martin\">Dear Tobias: How the new CEO can fix Aston Martin</a></strong></p> \n <p><iframe allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/vzx9uFsztlo\" width=\"560\"></iframe></p> \n</div>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Fri, 04 Sep 2020 11:31:17 +0000","feedId":13379,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"4b825aaaa1f6919772e0846229cf9dc4","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/100000-aston-martin-victor.jpg?itok=7ilQwymN":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn54@2020_4/2020/09/05/08-50-43-837_20e1669f7ed41bbc.webp","https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/3000-aston-martin-victor.jpg?itok=f5Cbk4oA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn82@2020_2/2020/09/05/08-50-43-730_8b6cfa82fc2d5830.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295843549},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"First drive: 2021 Volkswagen ID 4 prototype","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-2021-volkswagen-id-4-prototype","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-2021-volkswagen-id-4-prototype\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/99-vw-id-4-prototype-drive-2020-hero-front.jpg?itok=fDVtjeqg\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"2021 Volkswagen ID 4 prototype drive - hero front\" title=\"2021 Volkswagen ID 4 prototype drive - hero front\" /></a> VW’s first electric SUV boasts a familiar depth of engineering, quality and versatility. Initial signs suggest its mainstream ambitions are well warranted \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>“Never before has an electric vehicle been conceived with such a global outlook.” That’s how Ralf Brandstätter, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/volkswagen\">Volkswagen’s</a> new CEO, introduced <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/volkswagen-id-4-2021-electric-crossover\">the ID 4</a> before our first drive of a near-to-production-ready prototype – and he is nothing but bullish about its mainstream market ambitions.</p> \n <p>The second model from VW’s electric-only ID sub-brand sits in the world’s fastest-growing segment and will be built in five factories on three continents, starting at its Zwickau plant in Germany, from which right-hand-drive UK versions will begin rolling later this year. “The ID 4 will have a big impact in each of our three most important markets – Europe, China and North America,” said Brandstätter. “We see the potential for significant volumes.”</p> \n <p>As well as being key to VW’s aim to sell up to 1.5 million EVs annually by 2025, the ID 4 also forms the basis for upcoming siblings such as <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/audi-q4-sportback-e-tron-maker%E2%80%99s-seventh-ev-2021\">the Audi Q4</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-frankfurt-motor-show/cupra-tavascan-emotive-ev-concept-shown-frankfurt\">Cupra Tavascan</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/skoda-enyaq-iv-revealed-first-bespoke-ev-316-mile-range\">Skoda Enyaq</a>.</p> \n <p>Like <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/id-3\">the smaller ID 3</a>, it’s based the MEB electric car platform and will be sold with a range of power outputs in rear- and four-wheel-drive guises and two battery sizes. There are four initial rear-wheel-drive models, with a 146bhp, 168bhp, 173bhp or 201bhp motor. The lower-powered two have a 52kWh battery, the other two a 77kWh battery.</p> \n <p>A pair of four-wheel drive models will arrive in 2021. They’ll use the 77kWh battery and two electric motors – a smaller one up front and a main unit at the rear, developing a combined 262bhp or, in <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/volkswagen-id-4-suv-gains-hot-gtx-badge\">a yet to be confirmed GTX-badged range-topper</a>, 302bhp.</p> \n <p>Volkswagen says the 77kWh battery gives a WLTP range of up to 323 miles in mid-range 173bhp rear-wheel-drive guise. This compares with 301 miles for the 64kWh Hyundai Kona Electric and 336 miles for the 62kWh Telsa Model Y.</p> \n <p>Although our prototype carries light disguise, the ID 4 holds true to the look of the 2017 ID Crozz concept. It’s contemporary looking, with heavy crossover tones and unmistakable electric vehicle proportions. With a 0.26 drag co-efficient, it’s also among the most aerodynamic SUVs.</p> \n <p>VW offers two charging options. The 52kWh battery can be charged at up to 100kW, the 77kWh battery at up to 125kW. As a guide, VW says 30min of charging provides up to 199 miles on the more powerful system. In most cases, you’ll have to pay for the privilege, though. The base model supports 50kW charging as standard.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/98-vw-id-4-prototype-drive-2020-hero-side.jpg?itok=buNn7Un_\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <h3>What's it like?</h3> \n <p>Enough figures. Time to drive. The driver’s door opens wide and you step up into the ID 4 over a high body-coloured sill. The front seats are elevated but not excessively so and the floor is completely flat up front, without any defined footwells, because the battery is within the floorpan.</p> \n <p>The multi-layer dashboard houses two displays: a 5.3in digital instrument panel and a 10.0in central infotainment screen as standard, although our prototype has an optional 12.0in unit and augmented reality head-up display.</p> \n <p>The cabin is roomy, with the greater rear leg room than in a standard-wheelbase Tiguan and excellent versatility, thanks to typical features such as a 40:20:40-split folding rear seat. The boot, despite a high-ish loading lip, is also quite commodious.</p> \n <p>Hit the starter button and twist the gear selector. One notch forward gets you the standard drive mode and two notches Battery mode, which triggers the brake energy regeneration. It’s the same controller used by the ID 3, proving straightforward from the outset. Further drive modes – Eco, Comfort, Sport and Individual – alter steering, throttle, powertrain and adaptive damping responses.</p> \n <p>We’re driving the most powerful rear-wheel-drive ID 4. With 229lb ft on tap from the moment you nudge the throttle, it is brilliantly responsive. It has instant performance and excellent traction.</p> \n <p>Once rolling along, it gathers speed in quite a determined fashion on an open throttle. To be honest, it’s probably more spirited than it needs to be up to. At a cruise, it’s quiet and relaxed, although performance begins to fade at motorway cruising speeds. VW is yet to reveal performance figures, although initial rear-wheel-drive models will be limited to 100mph.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/92-vw-id-4-prototype-drive-2020-gk-driving.jpg?itok=_ttbrWmt\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>In standard drive mode, it coasts with a very faint hint of brake regeneration when you lift off the throttle. Battery mode’s regen means you rarely need to touch the brake pedal.</p> \n <p>Beyond the acoustic pedestrian warning, which switches off above 12mph, the powertrain is virtually silent. More noticeable is some tyre roar from the optional 235/45 R21 and 255/40 R21 Bridgestone Turanzas and wind buffeting around the door mirrors at speed.</p> \n <p>Dynamically, there’s quite a lot to like. The well-geared steering is nicely weighted and delivers a surprising amount of road feel. There’s also a 10.2m turning circle, so manoeuvrability and agility are outstanding.</p> \n <p>The chassis features MacPherson struts up front and a multi-link arrangement at the rear and it comes with optional adaptive damping control. There’s a measured rear-wheel-drive fluency to the handling, characterised by excellent lateral body control, strong grip and excellent traction in Sport mode. Despite the low-profile, large-diameter tyres of our prototype, the ride is very acceptable when you switch into Comfort, too.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/-vw-id-4-prototype-drive-offroad-rear.jpg?itok=cxykHXM3\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <h3>Should I buy one?</h3> \n <p>If you’re considering an EV for everyday use, the ID 4 should be on your shopping list. It’s a car you adapt to quickly and it’s engagingly responsive and agile. Further appeal comes through its clever interior, versatile nature, feeling of deep-seated engineering integrity and, with the 77kWh battery, ample range.</p> \n <p>If Volkswagen prices it right – we reckon it’ll be around £33,000 pre-government grant – the ID 4 promises to leave quite a mark, not only on its electric rivals but also the compact SUV class as a whole.</p> \n <p><strong>Volkswagen ID 4 77kWh specification</strong></p> \n <p><strong>Where</strong> Germany Price&nbsp;<strong>Price</strong>&nbsp;£33,000 (est) <strong>On sale&nbsp;</strong>xxx alt=\"2020 Volkswagen Arteon Shooting Brake R - hero front\" title=\"2020 Volkswagen Arteon Shooting Brake R - hero front\" /></a>\n<blockquote class=\"image-field-caption\">\n  New Arteon R takes its power from an uprated version of the Golf R's 2.0-litre turbocharged engine\n</blockquote> New Arteon fastback and Arteon Shooting Brake now available to order from £35,435 and £37,640, with cheaper variants on the way \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>Volkswagen has opened order books for the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/volkswagen-arteon-gets-shooting-brake-and-316bhp-r-variants\">new Arteon fastback </a>and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/volkswagen-arteon-gets-shooting-brake-and-316bhp-r-variants\">Arteon Shooting Brake</a>, with prices currently beginning from&nbsp;<span>£</span><span>35,435&nbsp;and&nbsp;</span>£37,640 respectively.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><span>Cheaper variants of each body type will be introduced later, but&nbsp;for now&nbsp;t</span>he price for the fastback marks a slight premium over the outgoing model. The new R-Line variant tops&nbsp;the range&nbsp;at £38,255 in four-door form and £39,055 as a shooting brake.</p> \n <p>Prices for the new plug-in eHybrid variant will be revealed at a later date. That car and a&nbsp;hardcore&nbsp;R version&nbsp;are expected to arrive in early 2021.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/arteon\">Arteon</a> was launched in 2017 but has so far been offered in only a fastback bodystyle. The new Arteon Shooting Brake variant features a separate design from the B-pillars back, with an extended roofline, a tapered glasshouse, prominent haunches over the rear wheels and an angled tailgate.</p> \n <p>Official figures show the Shooting Brake offers 565 litres of boot space (versus 563 litres in the fastback) and 1632 litres with the seats folded (1557 litres), but <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/volkswagen\">Volkswagen</a> says that because the space above the beltline isn't included in these measurements, the Shooting Brake's load space is actually significantly larger.</p> \n <p>Both models will be launched early next year, with the R versions arriving as part of the continued range expansion of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/volkwagen-pushing-r-division-due-recent-success\">Volkswagen's R performance division</a>. They will use the fourth evolution of the company's venerable EA288 2.0-litre four-cylinder turbo petrol engine, producing 316bhp and 310lb ft, a seven-speed dual-clutch automatic gearbox and an updated version of the 4Motion four-wheel drive system.</p> \n <p>A new R Performance torque vectoring system is said to have been inspired by similar systems on racing cars. It can bias up to 100% of the motor's power output \"within miliseconds\" to either axle or any of the four wheels, making the Arteon \"perceptively more agile\",&nbsp;Volkswagen claims. Torque distribution is determined by a combination of steering angle, accelerator input, lateral acceleration, yaw rate and speed.</p> \n <p>The new Arteon eHybrid, available in both bodystyles, uses the plug-in hybrid powertrain from<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/passat-gte\"> the Passat GTE</a>: a 154bhp 1.4-litre four-cylinder turbo petrol engine with a 113bhp electric motor. The two units have a combined output of 215bhp, which is sent to the front wheels through a six-speed dual-clutch automatic gearbox. The eHybrid offers an electric-only range of 33 miles and can operate in zero-emissions mode at speeds of up to 87mph.</p> \n <p>There are also three turbo petrol and two diesel engines in the Arteon line-up. The petrols range from 187bhp to 276bhp, while the 148bhp and 197bhp diesels are fitted with an updated selective catalytic reduction (SCR) filter and a new AdBlue system that, Volkswagen claims, reduces NOx emissions by around 80%. Buyers can choose between a six-speed manual or a seven-speed dual-clutch automatic gearbox, with four-wheel drive offered across the range.</p> \n <p>Unlike <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2020-volkswagen-golf-pictures-performance-on-sale-date\">the new Golf</a>, the Arteon isn't available with mild-hybrid powertrains because it still sits atop the original-specification MQB platform. This&nbsp;means we're unlikely to see mild-hybrid variants introduced until the second-generation model arrives.</p> \n <p>The restyled Arteon receives a raft of design changes, including a new grille with a light band, revised LED headlights and a range of new alloy wheel designs ranging in diameter from 18in to 20in. There are four different styles: basic, Elegance, R-Line and R. The performance models feature typical R styling cues, including a beefed-up front bumper with large cooling ducts, blue-painted brake calipers, chrome exhaust pipes and 20in 'performance' alloys.</p> \n <p>Inside, there’s a redesigned dashboard with a new upper section, a standard 10.25in digital instrument display, a new multifunction steering wheel and Volkswagen's latest infotainment system, with a standard 8.0in or optional 9.2in touchscreen.</p> \n <p>Martin Hube, spokesman for the Arteon model line, said: “We listened to feedback from our Arteon customers to further improve the Arteon family, not only adding a new derivative but also giving it a completely new and very sophisticated interior, which is very premium in terms of material. It has, basically, a Touareg interior.”</p> \n <p>Equipment levels vary according to trim, but standard kit includes a new multifunction steering wheel with touch-sensitive controls, illuminated trim panels and digital air conditioning controls. R models add black carbon trim elements, leather-upholstered sports seats with integrated headrests and an additional Race driving mode, while mid-range Elegance and R-Line cars feature stainless steel footrests, a sports steering wheel and velour/leather seats.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2020-volkswagen-golf-pictures-performance-on-sale-date\">New 2020 Volkswagen Golf: all the details</a></strong></p> \n <p><strong><a which had seen the two firms work together <a href=\"http://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/lotus-evija-new-configurator-video-released-ev-hypercar\">on the all-electric Evija hypercar</a>.</p> \n project.</p> \n <p>\"As the programme entered its latter stages pre the Covid lockdown, Lotus elected to bring the project in&nbsp;house due to delivery problems from Williams Advanced timetable.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> \n <p>\"The end result will be a better product as we introduce not only the most powerful production car in the world, but also the world's best electric car for the drivers.\"</p> \n <p>WAE claims Lotus’ decision is “wrongful and without any legal basis, made for Lotus/Geely’s unrelated commercial reasons”.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The engineering firm also claims that any allegations from Lotus that it breached the terms of the agreement, signed in January 2019, are “false and contrived”.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>WAE is now taking legal action against Lotus on grounds of wrongful termination&nbsp;and will pursue compensation for invoices that are claimed to have gone unpaid since April 2020.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>According to WAE, the decision puts a number of UK jobs at risk&nbsp;and jeopardises the launch of the Evija, which was <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/exclusive-lotus-evija-launch-pushed-back-until-mid-2021\">recently delayed because testing could not take place during the pandemic</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>WAE claimed the project is “now in its latter stages”&nbsp;and that it had “continued to perform outstanding work and progress the project despite the global impact of the Covid-19 pandemic”.</p> \n <p>“WAE wishes to make clear that this issue has no impact on its existing projects, customers and partners,” it added.</p> \n Abiteboul \n<div> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/renault\">Renault</a> has detailed a plan to revive its fortunes by restructuring the business around four core pillars. One of them is <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/alpine\">Alpine</a>, which has a new brand boss and a secure future after months of speculation.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The new strategy is being deployed by the group’s new boss, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/ex-seat-chief-luca-de-meo-appointed-new-renault-boss\">ex-Seat CEO Luca de Meo</a>. The four core business units are the Renault, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/dacia\">Dacia</a> and Alpine brands, plus a New Mobility operation.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>\"The company needs to change its ‘game module’ and move from a search for volume to a search for value and profitability,” said de Meo. “The organisation around four strong brands and large cross-functional functions would make it possible to work in a simpler way, more oriented to the markets and customers, with a team spirit, to seek the best possible result.”</p> \n <p>De Meo&nbsp;heads up the Renault brand, with sales and marketing EVP Denis le Vot piloting the new structure at Dacia and deputy CEO and CFO Clotilde Delbos taking control of New Mobility.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>But the biggest news is the appointment of Cyril Abiteboul – Renault Sport Racing boss and a pivotal figure in Renault’s return to Formula 1 as a works team – as head of Alpine. While this is good news for the sports car brand, it is speculated (but unconfirmed) that the F1 outfit could be renamed to incorporate Alpine branding.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Alpine’s future <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/alpine-could-become-electric-only-performance-brand\">had been called into question </a>earlier this year, with a number of key figures in the A110’s development leaving and an uncertain future for its Dieppe base.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Renault said in May that it was staging an “open reflection” on the future of the French facility once production of the A110 ends. Autocar understands that a plan has been worked up to turn Alpine into an all-electric performance brand, but nothing has been confirmed.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Renault also announced in May that it <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/updated-renault-cut-15000-jobs-part-major-cost-cuts\">would be slashing its fixed costs by more than €2 billion (£1.7b) in the next three years</a>, leading to the loss of 15,000 jobs worldwide. It posted heavy losses and was already proposing to restructure before the pandemic-induced sales slump made it more urgent.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Renault has declined to comment beyond the released details and de Meo’s statement. Further details of brand-specific organisational changes are expected to be detailed later this year.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><strong><span>READ MORE</span></strong></p> \n <p><a width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"Mercedes-Benz S-Class\" title=\"Mercedes-Benz S-Class\" /></a> It's described as the most advanced car Mercedes makes, but our man reckons that may not be enough to keep the luxury saloon relevant \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>It’s great to see the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2021-mercedes-s-class-luxury-saloon-reinvented-tech-focus\">2021&nbsp;Mercedes&nbsp;S-Class</a> continue its decades-long gentle exterior evolution that makes it so identifiable, but permit me some (perhaps premature) cynicism regarding the interior.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>While I can only comment on the images we've seen as part of the unveil – we’ve yet to get close to one in the metal because the reveal is virtual – I am concerned that Mercedes has caught the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/tesla\">Tesla</a> bug a bit too acutely.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Every S-Class generation has been a technological step change, so it’s only natural that advanced cabin tech dominates. But whereas you can get in, say, a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/history-mercedes-s-class-picture-special\">20-year-old W220</a>-generation&nbsp;S-Class and it still feels like an expensive, special place to sit, I can’t help but feel this one won’t date too well, given&nbsp;so much of the interior architecture is focused so strongly around the digital features.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/88-mercedes-benz-s-class-official-reveal-studio-dashboard_0.jpg?itok=wI-XKe0F\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>It’s the same with most modern cars as touchscreens now dominate interior designs and it's particularly acute at the luxury end of the market, where such a big financial investment means these cars&nbsp;are often kept for longer. Even if you update software over the air (which you can with the new S), what will the actual hardware and screen itself feel and look&nbsp;like in a decade’s time? And more to the point, should we really become so reliant on touchscreens when our readers frequently tell us they are a distraction?</p> \n <p>This is a debate that has raged on for years&nbsp;and it won't end any time soon. I hope these concerns are unfounded and Mercedes has created an S-Class that prioritises ergonomics and a sense of feeling ‘special’ inside over an endless list of gizmos that may never be used by owners.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The luxury saloon market is floundering in Europe in terms of sales, with core brands fighting over an increasingly small part of the pie. And it's not hard to see the problem. The tech you can get even in an <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/a-class\">A-Class</a> these days is extensive, so pricier luxury models have to differentiate with exemplary fit and finish, world-beating refinement and a real sense of occasion as priorities.&nbsp; Otherwise, what’s the point?</p> \n <p>&nbsp;</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n height=\"125\" alt=\"2020 Alpine A110 Légende GT in UK\" title=\"2020 Alpine A110 Légende GT in UK\" /></a> French sports coupé one of two limited edition models due to go on sale in 2020 \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/alpine\">Alpine</a> has brought its limited edition A110 Légende GT to the UK for the first time.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The French sports car made back-to-back&nbsp;appearances&nbsp;at the London Concours&nbsp;and&nbsp;Concours of Elegance Hampton Court Palace - two of only a handful of motor shows to go ahead since the beginning of the coronavirus pandemic.</p> \n <p>The&nbsp;Légende GT is billed as&nbsp;“the most refined interpretation of the A110 to date”, and conceived&nbsp;as a more long distance-friendly version of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/alpine/a110\">the acclaimed sports car</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Based on the current A110 Légende, the GT can be told apart from the standard car by its gold badging and 18in alloy wheels, translucent white rear light clusters and amber-coloured leather seats. It will be sold in three colours: Deep Black and Abyss Blue, which are already available on the standard A110, and a new option called Mercury Silver, seen in public for the first time here.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The car’s seats are six-way adjustable as standard, while additional bespoke interior features include a 12 o’ clock steering wheel marker, brown panel stitching, carbonfibre trim elements and a commemorative numbered plaque on the centre console. An extra storage unit between the two seats underlines the variant’s touring potential.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The A110’s 1.8-litre turbocharged engine is unaltered;&nbsp;the Légende GT packs 249bhp, can accelerate from 0-62mph in 4.5 seconds and will hit a top speed of 156mph. A performance exhaust, uprated Brembo brakes, parking sensors, a reversing camera and upgraded speaker system feature as standard.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Just 400 units will be offered worldwide, with prices starting from £59,140 in the UK&nbsp;– roughly a £10,000 premium over the standard A110 Pure.</p> \n <p>Alpine has also revealed the A110 Color Edition, which will be available for a limited time in a new, unique colour each year. For 2020, the Color Edition is painted in Sunflower Yellow, a shade taken from Alpine’s original colour palette from the 1960s.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/geneva_images_1.jpg?itok=zQIAHOI5\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The Color Edition is based on the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/alpine/a110-s/first-drives/alpine-a110-s-2019-review\">range-topping A110 S</a>, and as such is powered by an uprated version of the A110’s four-cylinder motor, producing 288bhp. That model’s performance-oriented chassis set-up also features.</p> \n <p>Rounding off Alpine’s three-pronged unveiling is the Atelier Alpine personalisation programme, which will offer 29 new heritage-inspired paint colours for the A110, each of which will be applied to just&nbsp;110 cars. The special hues can&nbsp;be specified for&nbsp;all models in the A110 range&nbsp;for an additional £4200.</p> \n <p><strong>Read more</strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/alpine/a110-s/first-drives/alpine-a110-s-2019-review\"><strong>Alpine A110 S 2019 review​</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/alpine-unveils-rally-inspired-a110-sportsx-concept\"><strong>Alpine unveils rally-inspired A110 SportsX concept</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/andrew-frankels-car-decade-alpine-a110\"><strong>Andrew Frankel's car of the decade: Alpine A110​</strong></a></p> \n <p><span class=\"wysiwyg-embed\"></span></p> \n <iframe allow=\"accelerometer; Of course it was – although exactly when those days were likely depends on when you first became a fan. That’s nostalgia for you. In truth, the F1 of whichever era you look back on most fondly probably wasn’t quite as good as you remember.</p> \n <p>Still, F1 fans are often prone to nostalgia, in part because the sport itself is fixated on the future. Most sports remain the same in essence for decades, but F1 is forever evolving, due to a never-ceasing drive to push the limits of technology. And that creates a disconnect between long-time fans and the contemporary sport.</p> \n <p>With 2020 marking <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/f1-70-why-car-firms-cant-resist-thrill-racing\">70 years of the F1 World Championship</a>, the sport’s bosses have been nodding to the past: the TV intro features loads of archive footage and there was even a 70th Anniversary Grand Prix. But I have a really simple idea to really engage with nostalgic fans: we need a throwback race.</p> \n <p>Full disclosure: this isn’t my idea. I’ve stolen it from Nascar, another category that has struggled to hold onto its fans as it has evolved over the years.</p> \n <p>For each of the past five years, Nascar has run the Southern 500 at Darlington Raceway as the Throwback Weekend. The storied event was first held in 1950, and the old-school oval is a favourite of drivers and long-time fans.</p> \n <p>Each year has featured a different theme, with the cars painted in special liveries that reflect it – often requiring sponsors to agree to their logos appearing in completely off-brand colour schemes. But as the tradition has grown, most sponsors have embraced it.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.nascar.com/gallery/paint-scheme-preview-darlington-throwback-race-2020/#photo-1\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"(C) NASCAR 2020\" class=\"image-body-image\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/hero-template_2020_darlington_9-5.jpg?itok=Mk0eXiHg\" /></a></p> \n <p>Past years have celebrated the 1970s, 1980s and 1990s. For this Sunday’s Southern 500, the theme is champions, and there are some cracking liveries. My favourite is the scheme that Austin Dillon is running, reflecting one used by the legendary Junior Johnson (who never won a title as a driver but did as a team owner).</p> \n <p>Elsewhere, Hendrick Motorsports’ four cars pay tribute to seven-time champion Jimmie Johnson in his final full season. Johnson’s team-mates are running liveries from his career, while his car celebrates fellow seven-timers Richard Petty and Dale Earnhardt.</p> \n <p>Predictably, the Throwback Weekend has proved to be a huge success – and I think F1 should copy it. While you wouldn’t want teams changing liveries every week (as they do in Nascar), a once-a-year retro grand prix would surely be a hit. <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mercedes-benz\">Mercedes</a> – which is using its livery this year to highlight racism – could run a scheme reflecting Juan Manuel Fangio’s 1950s W196. How about George Russell driving a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motorsport/exclusive-williams-f1-team-outlines-bold-recovery-plan\">Williams</a> painted to reflect fellow battling Brit Nigel Mansell’s 1992 title winner? <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/aston-martin-and-red-bull-plan-more-incredible-products-under-new-deal\">Red Bull</a> could even go back to its roots as Stewart and break out some tartan…</p> \n <p>Clearly, this idea <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motorsport/how-fix-formula-1-according-autocar\">won’t fix the problems that hamper F1</a> and make many nostalgic for (what we remember as) the good old days. But for the sake of a bit of paint, some creative thinking and a few understanding sponsors, it’s a simple idea that could help to build interest and entertain long-time fans.</p> \n <p>Admit it: you’re already thinking of which liveries you’d like revived, aren’t you?</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motorsport/f1-2020-four-new-races-added-calendar\">F1 2020: four new races added to calendar</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motorsport/f1-2020-everything-you-need-know-season-restarts\">F1 2020: everything you need to know as the season restarts</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/opinion/motorsport/racing-lines-how-f1-can-become-more-competitive\">Racing lines: How F1 can become more competitive</a></strong></p> \n <p><iframe diesel and hybrid versions of the next-generation 7 Series from 2022</a>, the i7 will sit atop BMW’s flexible CLAR platform and likely take its power from a variation of the electric powertrain featured in the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-bmw-ix3-munichs-second-ev-offers-285-mile-range\">new iX3 SUV</a>.</p> \n <p>The iX3 features BMW’s fifth-generation eDrive system, which comprises a rear-mounted motor that drives the rear axle only through a single-speed gearbox&nbsp;and&nbsp;takes its power from an 80kWh lithium ion battery for a WLTP-certified range of 285 miles.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The&nbsp;more upmarket i7, however, will likely pack significantly more power to bring it into line with its Jaguar and Mercedes rivals, both of which will place a heavy emphasis on performance&nbsp;and offer a range of nearer 400 miles.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>BMW recently claimed the electric 7 Series would be “the top, most powerful” model in the line-up, suggesting it could be offered as a performance variant that would approach the V12-powered 760Li’s 601bhp output.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>A brief glimpse of the interior suggests the i7 will feature a similar cabin layout to BMW's iNext electric SUV, with a prominent central infotainment display and curved digital gauge cluster. This prototype, however, doesn't appear to feature the larger car’s polygonal steering wheel.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The i7 will likely offer similar autonomous driving functions to the iNext, however, which is described as the first BMW in which the driver is no longer required to take care of the task of driving.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Although under heavy wraps, this i7 prototype gives clues as to the styling of the seventh-generation 7 Series. It looks like the current car’s controversial large kidney grilles are here to stay, in line with BMW product boss Peter Henrich’s recent affirmation that <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/bmw-continues-defend-new-styling-direction\">customers want “strong characters and bold design</a>”, although those on the electric model will be blanked off, as is customary.</p> \n <p>The next-generation 7 Series'&nbsp;proportions are also familiar, with a long wheelbase, extended front and rear overhangs and a low ride height.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The i7 forms part of BMW’s drive to electrify a quarter of its fleet by 2021, a third by 2025 and half&nbsp;by 2030. It will be joined in showrooms by the iX3, i4 saloon, iNext and&nbsp;upcoming electric variants of the X1, 5 Series and 3 Series.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The latter&nbsp;won't be called the i3,&nbsp;<a today.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2021-mercedes-s-class-luxury-saloon-reinvented-tech-focus\"><strong>The new S-Class has been officially unveiled - see it here.</strong></a></p> \n <p>The latest version of the luxury saloon is due to debut ahead of its arrival in showrooms early next year, with a focus on technology and refinement. Mercedes has confirmed it will be the first model to be producted in the&nbsp;new&nbsp;Factory 56 hall&nbsp;at its Sindelfingen, Stuttgart plant.</p> \n <p>In the run-up to the reveal, Mercedes has teased some of the technology that will feature in the new generation car, giving a first look at its augmented reality heads-up display ahead of the luxury saloon's official arrival.</p> \n <p>A teaser video posted to Mercedes' official twitter account shows the AR-HUD in action, overlaying live distance indicators and&nbsp;navigation directions onto the windscreen. The system can detect traffic and suggest a suitable gap to keep with the car in front, using coloured bars to suggest when you're too close, while navigation instructions update constantly to direct the driver around roundabouts and when filtering between lanes.&nbsp;Active lane keeping assist also uses coloured indicators to suggest when not enough steering lock has been applied through a corner.&nbsp;</p> \n <blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-partner=\"tweetdeck\">\n  <p dir=\"ltr\" lang=\"en\" xml:lang=\"en\">Ready for the next level of displays? The augmented reality head-up display (AR-HUD) of the new <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/SClass?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#SClass</a> provides loads of <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/AugmentedReality?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#AugmentedReality</a> content for <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/DrivingAssistance?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#DrivingAssistance</a> systems and navigation information.<a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/MBUX?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#MBUX</a> <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/MercedesBenzUK?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#MercedesBenzUK</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/cYBtAugepM\">pic.twitter.com/cYBtAugepM</a></p> \n  <p>— Mercedes-Benz UK (@MercedesBenzUK) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/MercedesBenzUK/status/1285133242564251648?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 20, 2020</a></p>\n </blockquote> \n <script async=\"\" src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script>\n <p>The new S-Class will put an even greater emphasis on technology <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/s-class\">than previous models</a>. When&nbsp;<span>Mercedes recently revealed the upcoming car's&nbsp;interior, it comfirmed spy photos taken earlier this year that showed off&nbsp;</span>a minimalist dashboard dominated by a Tesla-style portrait display - significantly larger than any screen Mercedes has offered in previous models - paired with a freestanding digital instrument display.&nbsp;<span>It will feature the second-generation version of the firm's MBUX infotainment system - with fewer physical controls, five touchscreens and an array of motion-detector, sensor-operated functions.&nbsp;</span></p> \n <p>Ahead of launch, prototypes of the flagship saloon have already bee&nbsp;seen with minimal disguise.&nbsp;<span>In the latest pictures, we can now see clearly that the&nbsp;seventh-generation</span><span>&nbsp;</span><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/first-drives/bmw-730ld-2019-uk-review\">BMW 7 Series</a><span>&nbsp;rival takes an evolutionary approach to the exterior&nbsp;redesign, with a similarly curvy look to today's car. This particular mule, which is covered only in a thin plastic wrapping,&nbsp;shows off undisguised headlights and&nbsp;tail-lights, taking&nbsp;inspiration from that of the&nbsp;</span><span>latest&nbsp;</span><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/cls\">CLS</a><span>.&nbsp;</span></p> \n <p><span>Further visible details include&nbsp;a new interpretation of the classic Mercedes-Benz grille and door handles that sit flush with&nbsp;bodywork and pop out when the car is unlocked. The latter is understood to be one factor contributing to best-in-class aerodynamic properties.&nbsp;</span></p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"601\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/mercedes_s-class_spyshots3.jpg?itok=1UUg1HS4\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The seventh-generation S-Class looks set to regain its place at the forefront of the brand's technical know-how, with a range of new electrified powertrains and&nbsp;advanced driver assist features. Comfort and technology levels will take a boost, with the target of lifting it beyond rivals such as the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/7-series\">7 Series</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/audi/a8\">Audi A8</a>.</p> \n <p>The new Mercedes flagship, which is due in UK showrooms next year, has been developed to support two distinctly different saloon models for the first time. While standard versions are set to receive a range of plug-in hybrid drivetrains, the German car maker will also launch an aerodynamically optimised <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/mercedes-eq-s-be-flagship-%C2%A39bn-electric-model-blitz\">pure-electric version</a> that will serve as the flagship model for its&nbsp;new <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-eq-range-lead-daimler-ev-product-offensive\">EQ electric vehicle sub-brand</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Badged <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/mercedes-eq-s-be-flagship-%C2%A39bn-electric-model-blitz\">EQS</a>, the new model will offer a claimed range in excess of 310 miles on the latest WLTP test cycle when it goes on sale in 2022. Plug-in hybrid versions of the S-Class will feature part-time zero-emission capability for distances of up to 62 miles, together with the option of a newly developed 4Matic four-wheel drive system with fully variable apportioning of drive between the front and rear axles.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"601\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/_sb11477.jpg?itok=P8pBFBmp\" width=\"900\" />&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The EQS forms part of Mercedes’ £9 billion programme to introduce more than 10 dedicated electric vehicles to the UK market within the next six years.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>In a further change, it is believed that Mercedes-Benz has decided to do away with its long tradition of offering the standard S-Class, which goes under the internal codename W223, with two different wheelbases. Nothing is official at this stage, but it is understood that the growth of the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/e-class\">E-Class</a> to a length of 4920mm is behind a decision to produce the new S-Class exclusively in long-wheelbase guise, with the car measuring around 5280mm in length.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"601\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/_sb11458.jpg?itok=tP_cItpL\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>However, while the standard S-Class sits on the MRA platform, the more technically advanced four-wheel-drive EQS will be the first Mercedes-Benz model to be based on the new Modular Electric Architecture (MEA) platform. Unlike the structures being developed to underpin smaller EQ models, it is not based on an existing platform but has been developed as dedicated EV architecture with a flat floor to house batteries.</p> \n <p>The drivelines set to power hybrid versions of the new S-Class are based around Mercedes’ latest 3.0-litre and 2.9-litre in-line six-cylinder petrol and diesel engines and the AMG-developed 4.0-litre V8, all of which operate in combination with a disc-shaped electric motor housed within the automatic gearbox and a lithium ion battery located in the boot floor.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The electric EQS is set to receive two electric motors – one acting on the front axle and the other driving the rear – providing permanent four-wheel drive in all variants. In the EQC, this set-up delivers more than 400bhp and some 516lb ft, although engineers involved on the development of the EQS suggest it will offer even greater levels of power and torque, with a planned AMG performance model earmarked to produce more than 600bhp.</p> \n <p>Despite the differing platforms, both the standard S-Class and the EQS are set to share the same active suspension system. A development of the existing S-Class’s AirMatic+ system, it works in combination with a 48V electrical architecture and a stereo camera that scans the road ahead to adjust the spring and damper action on each wheel, allowing it to not only counteract body lean in corners but also to better control pitch.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The EQS will adopt its own distinct styling. Reflecting the packaging advantages inherent in electric vehicles, it receives a shorter bonnet and more heavily raked windscreen than the standard version of the new S-Class, similar to that of the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/cls\">CLS</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><strong>Read more</strong></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/mercedes-reduce-model-line-platforms-and-powertrains\"><strong>Mercedes to reduce model line-up, platforms and powertrains</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-eqs-electric-luxury-limo-spawn-amg-version\"><strong>Mercedes EQS: electric luxury limo to spawn AMG version</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/features/farewell-v12-celebrating-endangered-engine\"><strong>Farewell to the V12: celebrating the endangered engine​</strong></a></p> \n <p><span class=\"wysiwyg-embed\"></span></p> \n <iframe allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"
