alt=\"Jeep Renegade 4xe front\" title=\"Jeep Renegade 4xe front\" /></a> Jeep's first plunge into electrification is on in its most popular and smallest model. Is it worth splashing out for? \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> “It’s the start of a new era!” Jeep says. “It’s to reduce your fleet CO2 average!” we say. Regardless, it’s a show of confidence in the rough and tough US maker that it’s the first Fiat Chrysler Automobiles brand with a European presence to receive a plug-in hybrid powertrain.&nbsp;And it won’t be the last. It’ll come as no surprise that Jeep is one of the biggest polluters in the group’s stable, and even FCA’s emissions credit pooling with Tesla will go only so far to remedying that. So Jeep needs electrification to do some of the legwork. The ever-popular Renegade takes priority but soon to follow are a plug-in Compass and Wrangler, and all models will feature some form of battery propulsion by 2022.&nbsp;The Renegade 4xe (pronounced 4-by-e) joins an ever-growing rank of plug-in SUVs, but Jeep touts the Mini Countryman PHEV&nbsp;as its main challenger. Pricing is broadly similar, although the Jeep is more comprehensively equipped as standard.&nbsp;It makes use of a 1.3-litre turbo petrol engine, itself giving 128bhp (or a sprightly 177bhp in top-spec Trailhawk trim, which we’re not driving here). That’s combined with a 59bhp electric motor mounted over the rear axle in all models for four-wheel drive without the need for a second driveshaft.Those output figures are healthy enough, but they’re lugging a car that’s between 130kg and 200kg heavier (depending on spec) than the pure combustion-engined variants. Despite an 11.4kWh battery crammed under the passenger compartment, Jeep claims there has been no loss of space, although the hardware under the boot floor robs 20 litres of outright capacity.&nbsp;","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Fri, 04 Sep 2020 11:30:33 +0000","feedId":13379,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"88c73509df463294398f6c91828ca04d","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/jeep-29072020_0317.jpg?itok=wjuN6JG9":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295843549},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"2021 Ineos Grenadier makes UK debut alongside off-road icons","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/ineos-grenadier-2021","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/ineos-grenadier-2021\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/40-ineos-grenadier.jpg?itok=d3NFn9Fp\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"Ineos Grenadier\" title=\"Ineos Grenadier\" /></a>\n<blockquote class=\"image-field-caption\">\n  Grenadier's design is mainly Defender-influenced, but hints of other cars feature too\n</blockquote> Singular utilitarian focus is matched with modern tech and powerful BMW engines \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>Sir Jim Ratcliffe’s rugged new off-roader, the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2021-ineos-grenadier-first-prototype-caught-testing-disguise\">Ineos Grenadier</a>, has appeared for the first time in public, displayed at London's Concours of Elegance alongside the 4x4 icons that inspired its design.</p> \n <p>The Grenadier will be parked up next to the collection of historic off-roaders that make up Ineos' own private fleet, including an original Mercedes G-Wagen, a Toyota Land Cruiser FJ40, a Willys Jeep and the earliest known production example of the original Land Series I.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Ineos designer Toby Ecuyer said:&nbsp;“At the outset of the Grenadier project, we brought some of the great 4x4s of the past into the studio to look closely at what made them so enduring. And now, it’s fantastic to see Grenadier in the company of these legends.</p> \n <p>\"You can see common design traits and proportions, and certainly the same clarity of purpose. I think the Grenadier sits very naturally among these 4x4 icons, and if others agree, then we’ve achieved our design objective.”</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/13-ineos-grenadier-static-rear.jpg?itok=1ehzWY0s\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Despite the new car's resemblance to cars like the Defender, the Grenadier is an all-new 4x4 created by a ground-up team and brand, with modern components, a state-of-the-art powertrain and possibly an even more singular purpose than the icon that it seeks to supplant.</p> \n <p>Similar in size to the latest <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/g-class\">Mercedes-Benz G-Class</a> and powered by a modular range of six-cylinder <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/bmw\">BMW</a> diesel and petrol engines, it’s expected to be priced from £40,000 when it hits the market late next year, initially as a five-door station wagon then “soon afterwards” as a four-door pick-up truck. A short-wheelbase car may come after, alongside other versions.</p> \n <p>Production will take several years to ramp up for markets around the world, but insiders say it will be profitable at an annual output of about 25,000.</p> \n <p>Ratcliffe, founder and majority owner of the £50 billion British petrochemicals group Ineos, is a steadfast devotee of the old Defender. He came up with the idea of building a replacement of his own when <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/car-industry-now-how-will-jaguar-land-rover-look-after-crisis\">Jaguar Land Rover</a> declined to sell him its designs or tooling to continue when production ceased at Solihull after 67 years in January 2016.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/19-ineos-grenadier-static-rear.jpg?itok=Y5CUhLDo\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Two years ago, after forming Ineos Automotive, Ratcliffe enlisted his friend and favourite superyacht designer, Toby Ecuyer – who is usually based on the south coast of England – to form and lead the Grenadier design team. He also appointed former chemical engineer Dirk Heilmann as Ineos Automotive CEO and set him the task of creating the 4x4’s mechanical package, working with a band of engineers based mainly at Magna Steyr in Graz, Austria.</p> \n <p>Named after Ratcliffe’s favourite pub in Belgravia, London, the Grenadier is being unveiled now, 18 months before its expected on-sale date, because its creators believe they will find it easier to complete a tightly planned million-mile global test programme if they can drive it “in plain sight”. Testing began last winter in Sweden. Meanwhile, two new factories are being built: one in Portugal for chassis-making and one in South Wales for final assembly.</p> \n <p>Last week, Autocar held a virtual meeting with Ecuyer, Heilmann and commercial director Mark Tennant to see the wraps come off the Grenadier and hear more about its purpose and capabilities. We saw the finished exterior but not the “hose-it-out” interior Ratcliffe has ordered because details are still being finalised.</p> \n <p>“We’re using the line ‘Built on Purpose’ for the Grenadier,” said Tennant, “because for this project, function must always lead. We’re focusing on a high standard of off-road performance first, and there’s an Ineos tradition of using straightforward, simple language for a straightforward, simple car. Not that we’re Luddites; it’s not spartan or out of date. It will have all the connectivity and screen technology you would expect. And it will be comfortable, too, because owners will spend many hours in their machines.”</p> \n <p><strong>Body design</strong></p> \n <p>Ecuyer doesn’t shy away from remarks about the Grenadier’s resemblance to the Defender but stresses that the team came to the current design and specification after researching a large number of competitor vehicles, many of which were bought for benchmarking.</p> \n <p>He said: “We had <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/jeep\">Jeeps</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/land-rover\">Land Rovers</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/toyota/hilux\">Toyota Hiluxes</a>, a <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/used-cars/used-car-buying-guide-toyota-land-cruiser\">Toyota FJ40 [Land Cruiser]</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mitsubishi-still-aiming-develop-new-shogun-roader\">Nissan Patrols</a>, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-detroit-motor-show/fords-baby-bronco-suv-leaked-dealer-presentation\">Ford Broncos</a>. And we looked at vans, lorries, Unimogs, military vehicles, tractors. African-spec vehicles were particularly interesting. They all shaped our plan for a vehicle that would be extremely capable but also very honest and uncomplicated.”</p> \n <p>The result is a simple, well-proportioned and familiar-looking off-roader with straight sides, a clamshell bonnet rising above flat-topped front wings, a steep, fairly flat windscreen and a flat roof with rain gutters running all the way around.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/15-ineos-grenadier-close-up.jpg?itok=UvajLWNn\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The grille is simple and vertical, the LED headlights are round and the large wheels are positioned to minimise body overhangs and take advantage of rubberised wheel arches.</p> \n <p>The station wagon body has three windows each side. Like the windscreen, they and a lot of the panelling appear to be flat, but they aren’t quite. Ecuyer said very gentle curvature confers a modern sophistication on the design it otherwise wouldn’t have.</p> \n <p>Most reminiscent of the Defender is the Grenadier’s body ‘shoulder’ that runs from the top of the front wings in a dead straight line right to the rear end. Ecuyer said this gives room for ‘stuff’ inside the bottom half of the doors while allowing their tops to be “no thicker than they need to be”.</p> \n <p>The doors have external hinges that help with the door removal that will suit some users and give the car’s design the honesty Ecuyer sought.</p> \n <p>“It was really important to us that this design should be easily read, with nothing complicated or mysterious about it,” said Ecuyer. “You can see how the doors and bonnet are attached. There are no hidden pillars or tricks with glass. It’s comfortable to be around, not too clever. And there’s none of the clever technology people have developed to sanitise big SUVs. It’s just honest.”</p> \n <p>Ecuyer admitted to plenty of debate about the Grenadier’s rear-end design: for a long time, the team were settled on a classic split tailgate, before deciding late in the day on the big-door-small-door layout.</p> \n <p>Tailgates can make vehicles hard to load or unload, said Ecuyer, and the swing-out spare wheel carrier would have been “a nightmare”.</p> \n <p>The small door can be opened before the large one to provide access to the space-saver tool compartment that’s innovatively pressed into its skin below the glass.</p> \n <p>The round tail-lights “share a common language” with the round headlights and are mounted ideally on the extra space provided by the body shoulder, happily where modern law requires them to be visible. “They’re the result of a very practical problem,” said Ecuyer, “not a wafty sketch in a cafe somewhere…”</p> \n <p>Interesting evidence of Ecuyer’s nautical design background abounds. The roof can be used to carry loads without a rack, and one artful touch is the provision of four tie bars on the sides of the roof that look a lot like the roof lights of an old Land Rover.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/17-land-rover-defender-hero-front.jpg?itok=6djOZVum\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>There are also pre-wired “utility rails” running through the doors and under the rear side windows, because Ineos expects owners to use their Grenadiers for camping. These rails will allow for the mounting of lights, for example.</p> \n <p>Although they’re not talking about the interior today, the Ineos team makes clear that it includes more such features. “We haven’t swathed the dash just to make it look nice,” said Ecuyer. “If there’s space available, we open it up for use.”</p> \n <p>Ineos will design factory-fit options and aftermarket kit for the Grenadier but isn’t shy about making it ‘open-source’ so other equipment makers can produce add-ons to suit.</p> \n <p>“Every owner’s use for their vehicle will be different,” said Heilmann, “and we’re very happy with that.”</p> \n <p><strong>Chassis and powertrain</strong></p> \n <p>Heilmann said he expects the Grenadier to be heavier than the old Defender 110, which is narrower but slightly longer, but that’s mostly because the Land Rover is a considerably simpler, less well-equipped vehicle with a much lighter powertrain. The target weight is around 2400kg, but today’s initial prototypes are 80kg too heavy, so weight must be reduced to improve the Grenadier’s all-important off-road performance.</p> \n <p>Ineos’s engine choice is the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2017-bmw-5-series-saloon-and-estate-latest-spy-pictures\">BMW B57/B58</a> family, so each Grenadier will have a modular 3.0-litre petrol or diesel straight six that sends its drive through a ZF-supplied eight-speed automatic gearbox (and a separate low-range transfer case). Depending on spec, these engines make anything from 261bhp to nearly 400bhp in their BMW applications.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/12-ineos-grenadier-hero-front.jpg?itok=nKaS86iL\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Heilmann said that although the Grenadier’s performance will make off-roading a priority, its on-road ability will be “fine for anyone who’s used to driving, say, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jeep/wrangler\">a Jeep Wrangler</a>”. However, the performance potential will probably require an on-road speed limiter.</p> \n <p>The car’s relatively old-tech body-on-frame chassis, twin live axles and non-independent coil suspension are a rarity nowadays; even the Hilux has independent front suspension. However, the body is a complex mixture of aluminium, high-strength steel and composites.</p> \n <p>“We’ve had to learn that aluminium isn’t always the best choice for strength and crash purposes,” said Heilmann, “so we’ve chosen the right materials for the right jobs.” But much of the outer skin – the bonnet, the doors and the mudguards – is aluminium.</p> \n <p><strong>Timetable and marketing</strong></p> \n <p>Tennant and Heilmann say the project is running only a few weeks behind, despite <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/advice/coronavirus-what-motorists-need-know\">Covid-19</a>, and they’re looking now at ways of getting that time back. “It’s a tight schedule,” Heilmann said, “but by 2021 we want to be doing our first production runs, and at the end of 2021 we should have production cars coming off the line.</p> \n <p>“For now, the time-critical areas are going well. Our key suppliers – people like our axle partner in northern Italy – are with us. The challenge is to get the components together and have them properly tested.”</p> \n <p>Tennant said decisions about the dealer network are still being made but that Ineos wants to sell the Grenadier as directly as it can. He plans an announcement soon about how and where cars will be serviced.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/16-ineos-grenadier-static-side.jpg?itok=FIgylFqq\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>“The world of car retailing is moving rather rapidly at present,” he said ruefully.</p> \n <p>For a start, Europe and North America will be the key markets, but Ineos is also very interested in Australia, Africa and South-East Asia, where it is confident the Grenadier’s ruggedness will go down well.</p> \n <p>“Experience centres will be a high priority,” said Tennant. “No one is going to want to buy one of these just by driving it around the block.”</p> \n <p><strong>Q&amp;A: Toby Ecuyer. Ineos Grenadier design leader</strong></p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/11-toby-ecuyer.jpg?itok=p607KOjR\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p><em><strong>So you’re not a car designer?</strong></em></p> \n <p>“No, at least not until now. I grew up on a farm in Derbyshire around tractors and Land Rovers, but I was interested in cars.</p> \n <p>“When I was about nine, I wrote to Austin Rover with some car sketches. They wrote back politely, basically saying the cars were terrible but that they had a design department and, when I was old enough, I should try to join their training scheme. Until then, I didn’t realise design was an actual job, and that really sparked my interest to know how things were created.”</p> \n <p><em><strong>How did you get into design?</strong></em></p> \n <p>“I trained as an architect and then got into boat design – long projects, 80-metre superyachts and for private customers. That’s how I got to know Jim Ratcliffe. I designed a couple of boats for him and looked after a building project. I was involved in the early talks about the Grenadier, then Jim asked me if I would like to be involved. It sounded interesting, and it has been fascinating.”</p> \n <p><em><strong>Has learning a new discipline been hard?</strong></em></p> \n <p>“Well, I’ve learned that it isn’t necessarily wrong to change horses. There are some interesting parallels in surface design and design thinking. And although I’m the design leader, there are others in the team. I haven’t done all this on my own.”</p> \n <p><strong><em>What’s it like working with Jim Ratcliffe?</em></strong></p> \n <p>“Jim loves the design process, and he gets very involved. He has brilliant ideas. My job is to help him get them onto paper. When you’re building a superyacht, you’re talking about a four-year programme, so you get to know a person really well. We had a good friendship – and a mutual enjoyment of cars.”</p> \n <p><em><strong>Is this a car to love or a tool?</strong></em></p> \n <p>“Both, really. We were very interested in vehicles that had both proven themselves in the field and found their way into people’s hearts.</p> \n <p>“Not all modern SUVs were like this. There’s an honesty about cars in our collection that people tend to adopt and identify with, and we wanted that for Grenadier. That’s why we assembled our collection of vehicles for benchmarking. They were all vehicles that were well-respected.”</p> \n <p><em><strong>What will you think when people draw similarities to the Land Rover Defender?</strong></em></p> \n <p>“It has been fascinating, benchmarking all the cars we have. One thing I’ve learned is how little there is between cars. I mean, you only have to change a vehicle a little to make it look like something different. Shift the headlights a bit and you’ve suddenly made a Ford Bronco.”</p> \n <p><em><strong>How did you define your objectives for the Grenadier?</strong></em></p> \n <p>“We made a list of qualities we wanted to achieve: assured, robust, faithful, dependable and purposeful. We used them as a kind of checklist. Every time we had a decision to make about the car, we would run through the list to see if it met them. I’m hoping people will recognise those things in the production car.”</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/official-ineos-confirms-bridgend-factory-grenadier-4x4\">Official: Ineos confirms Bridgend factory for Grenadier 4x4</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>Brabham Automotive has revealed a road-legal version of its<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/brabham-bt62-700bhp-track-only-hypercar-demonstrated-goodwood\">£1 million Ultimate Track</a> and <a chassis and aerodynamic hardware with those other models. Although <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/brabham-bt62-hypercar-adds-entry-level-%C2%A3750000-competition-variant\">Brabham</a> says it's tuned for the road, the firm also says the BT62R is equally \"at home on the track\".</p> \n <p>Just 70 BT62 cars will be built, encompassing all three variants. Brabham expects the GT62R to account for&nbsp;between 30% and 50% of these models.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>During the launch of the road-going variant, Brabham also announced plans for further expansion, confirming it will reveal more about another new model, described as a “fully homolated road car”, in the next few months.</p> \n <p>The BT62R retains the 5.4-litre naturally aspirated V8 engine used in the other two variants, but with revised engine mapping for use on the road. It develops 700bhp and 492lb ft of torque, which is delivered through a six-speed sequential gearbox.</p> \n <p>The car sports the same carbonfibre body as the track variants but with a few crucial changes to aid better on-road vehicle dynamics. The model features a revised front splitter and rear diffuser, a new top-mounted air intake and a redesigned and road-compliant single-plane rear wing.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/brabham_bt62r_-6.jpg?itok=y4KJb3uk\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>Brabham said the result is a car that “maintains the incredible dynamics of a race car - acceleration, deceleration and lateral variation - and combines them with the manners and comfort of a road car.”</p> \n <p>Two different versions of the road car are offered, dubbed Signature and Celebration Series. The Celebration version is distinguished by one of 35 racing liveries marking Brabham’s 35 wins in Formula 1 and gold badging.</p> \n <p>Inside, the BT62R is significantly more luxurious than the stripped-back Ultimate Track and Competition variants. Brabham claims a “special emphasis was placed on everyday drivability” during the car’s development. Customers can choose from either leather- or Alcantara-finished carbonfibre seats, with contrast stitching. Brabham has also added a new climate control system and digital control panel, including a digital rear camera.</p> \n <p>Brabham Automotive boss Dan Marks said: “Launching the BT62R is a great achievement for the team at Brabham Automotive. All the requisite design and engineering to turn the track BT62 into the road-going BT62R has been done in-house by our team of engineers, which is a great testimony to their endeavour and expertise.”</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"Porsche Taycan\" title=\"Porsche Taycan\" /></a>\n<blockquote class=\"image-field-caption\">\n  Porsche introduced its first electric car, the Taycan, earlier this year \n</blockquote> German marque follows Volkswagen and Bentley siblings in researching e-fuels and aims to build factories to prove viability \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>Porsche has announced that it wants to “drive forward the development of synthetic fuels [e-fuels]” and is seeking partners to build pilot factories to prove&nbsp;e-fuels' viability.</p> \n <p>Although <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/porsche\">Porsche</a> is investing in electrification, as evidenced by the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/porsche-taycan-specs-sale-date-performance\">introduction of the Taycan EV </a>earlier this year, it believes&nbsp;the technology is not reducing its carbon footprint quickly enough.</p> \n <p>Porsche’s R&amp;D boss, Michael Steiner, said: “Electric mobility is an exciting and convincing technology but, taken on its own, it is taking us towards our sustainability targets at a slower pace than we would like. That’s why we are also committing to e-fuels – and not ignoring possible applications in motorsports, either.”</p> \n <p>Another reason&nbsp;Porsche is investing in e-fuels, he said, is because they are a “fundamental component” of improving the sustainability of existing fleets. A further advantage is that, unlike electrification, they do not require significant mechanical changes to existing cars.</p> \n <p>E-Fuels have long been of interest to the car industry. They function similarly to kerosene, diesel or petrol processed from crude oil but are produced from CO2 and hydrogen using renewable energy.</p> \n <p>Porsche’s VW Group sibling brands, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/volkswagen\">Volkswagen</a> and <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/bentley\">Bentley</a>, are researching the technology, as is <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mclaren\">McLaren</a>. However, not all firms are as enthusiastic. <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/mercedes-benz\">Mercedes</a> has recently snubbed e-fuels, <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/mercedes-rd-boss-synthetic-fuel-not-viable-option\">questioning their viability</a>.</p> \n <p>Although Porsche aims for half of its vehicles sold to be <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/next-gen-porsche-cayenne-could-be-fully-electric\">electric by 2025</a>, the marque is committed to pure-combustion engines in the medium term. Steiner stressed that Porsche’s existing fleet is large, and although its hybrid vehicles are powered electrically for short drives, they frequently undertake longer trips, which require combustion engines.</p> \n <p>Porsche’s focus on synthetic fuels reflects wider trends. Earlier this year, the government announced that it<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/government-plans-e10-petrol-switch-2021\"> plans to introduce lower-carbon E10 petrol</a>, which is made with 10% ethanol, as <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/government-plans-e10-petrol-switch-2021\">standard at UK filling stations in 2021</a>.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/volkswagen-combustion-engine-has-life-it-yet\">Volkswagen: Combustion engine has life in it yet</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/mclaren-advocates-synthetic-fuel-alternative-evs\">McLaren advocates synthetic fuel as alternative to EVs</a>&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/mercedes-rd-boss-synthetic-fuel-not-viable-option\">Mercedes R&amp;D boss: synthetic fuel not a viable option</a></strong></p> \n <p><iframe allow=\"accelerometer; We have the info \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>What’s in a name? We all loved the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/skoda/yeti-2013-2017\">Yeti</a>, even though it looked insane and had an odd moniker. The <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/skoda/karoq\">Karoq’s</a> name is odd, too, but the car beneath the badge is entirely and in some instances delightfully conventional. Larger than the Yeti both inside and out, the Karoq was created with practicality as its main brief – so it retained the smart touches and versatility that made its predecessor so popular, if not that standout styling.</p> \n <p>There’s a good array of engines. The petrol range has consisted of 113bhp 1.0-litre, 148bhp 1.5-litre and 187bhp 2.0-litre units. For diesel, you can pick between a 113bhp 1.6-litre and two 2.0 diesels of 148bhp and 187bhp. You can also seek out a dual-clutch automatic gearbox, while four-wheel drive is available on the 1.5 and 2.0 petrols and the 2.0 diesel models.</p> \n <p>There are varying trim levels, too. SE brings 17in alloy wheels, dual-zone climate control, front and rear electric windows and an 8.0in touchscreen that features smartphone mirroring. SE Technology adds adaptive cruise control and front and rear parking sensors, while SE L has a dedicated built-in sat-nav. Later Sport Line trim features 19in alloys and sports seats, while top-rung Edition spec adds a wider, 9.2in infotainment screen and a panoramic sunroof.</p> \n <p>To drive, the Karoq is a very pleasant thing. It isn’t quite as sharp in the handling department as <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/seat/ateca\">the Seat Ateca</a>, with which it shares a platform, but it’s tidier and more agile than its other platform mate,<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/tiguan\"> the Volkswagen Tiguan</a>. It comes up trumps for comfort, with a well-judged ride that smooths off all but the harshest bumps in town and is delightfully plush at higher speeds.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"596\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/30-skoda-karoq-scout-2019-rt-otr-side_0.jpg?itok=RXl3hinZ\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The Karoq’s greatest asset, however, is its interior. It’s smart and beautifully built, and there’s loads of room for driver and front passenger, and an excellent driving position.</p> \n <p>The car’s appeal remains strong as you go further back in it because the rear doors open nice and wide and the rear bench is pretty spacious. If you choose an SE L or Edition, you get a fantastically useful 40/20/40-split folding rear seat – or the option to remove the rear seats entirely to maximise boot space. This system was also available as part of the VarioFlex package on SE and SE Technology models.</p> \n <p>The boot isn’t the biggest in the class, but it is very well shaped, which means you can carry a useful amount in it. And if you don’t choose a car with the VarioFlex seating, your consolation prize is an adjustable boot floor with a hidden space beneath the cover for smaller items.</p> \n <p>Prices for used Karoqs start at a decent £15,000. Up the budget to £16,000-£18,000 and you’ll find plenty of 2018 cars and 2019 cars. Spend around £19,000-£21,000 on a more recent Karoq.</p> \n <p><strong>Need to know</strong></p> \n <p>The 1.0-litre petrol has a WLTP figure of 43.5mpg but the 1.5-litre petrol is only slightly less, at 41.5mpg, thanks to fuel-saving cylinder-deactivation tech. The 1.6-litre diesel is rated at 49.6mpg but the 148bhp 2.0-litre is slightly better still, at 50.4mpg.</p> \n <p>It’s possible that a small number of Karoqs built in February 2019 have a cracked left front seat frame. A Skoda dealer will be able to inspect your seat and replace the frame if necessary.</p> \n <p>There have been two recalls for the rear head restraints in the Karoq. Your local dealer can tell you if your car needs to have any recall work carried out.</p> \n <p><strong>Our pick</strong></p> \n <p><strong>Karoq 1.5 TSI 150 SE: </strong>We love the pace, refinement and efficiency of the 1.5 petrol and there’s a good choice of used ones. Entry-level SE is well equipped, but seek out a car that has the VarioFlex seating option.</p> \n <p><strong>Wild card</strong></p> \n <p><strong>Karoq 2.0 TSI 190 Sport Line 4x4 DSG: </strong>With stylish 19in alloy wheels, Sport Line is near the top of the tree, and paired with the rare and more powerful petrol 2.0 and an auto ’box, it’s a bit of a peach.</p> \n <p><strong>Ones we found</strong></p> \n <p>2017 Karoq 1.5 TSI 150 SE, 36,000 miles, £14,950</p> \n <p>2018 Karoq 2.0 TDI 150 SE L, 29,000 miles, £16,950</p> \n <p>2019 Karoq 1.5 TSI 150 Edition, 12,000 miles, £19,500</p> \n <p>2020 Karoq 2.0 TSI 190 Sport Line 4x4 DSG, 8000 miles, £26,995</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a \n<div class=\"iframe-container-www-youtube-com\"> \n <p>Gordon Murray Automotive (GMA) has confirmed it will produce a racing version of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/gordon-murray-t50-v12-powered-mclaren-f1-successor\">the recently revealed T50 supercar</a>.</p> \n <p>Just 25 examples of the track-only car, codenamed T50s, will be built, each with&nbsp;extensive revisions that promise to make it even lighter than the road-going version, at just 890kg.</p> \n <p>Each example will cost £3.1 million before taxes - a substantial increase over the road car's £2.36 million plus taxes. Over half of the production run had already been accounted for before the car's existence was revealed to the public.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The Cosworth-developed, naturally aspirated V12 engine powering the T50 has been re-engineered with&nbsp;revised cylinder heads, a higher compression ratio&nbsp;and an all-new free-flow exhaust system&nbsp;to produce beyond 700bhp. According to Murray himself, this was only possible in a track car, which doesn't have to contend with noise or emission regulations. A bespoke new six-speed transmission has new drive ratios and replaces the road car's manual gearstick with paddle shifters.</p> \n <p>Significant upgrades to the car's aerodynamics pair the road-going T50's&nbsp;signature rear-mounted fan&nbsp;with a new 1758mm-wide rear wing, new front splitter, underbody aerofoil and adjustable diffusers. Combined, the changes allow the&nbsp;T50s to&nbsp;generate more than 1500kg&nbsp;of downforce. A new roof-mounted aero fin also helps boost cornering stability, allowing the car to generate 2.5-3g under braking.</p> \n <p>Unlike the road car, which has multiple aerodynamic modes, the T50s will run in High Downforce mode at all times, with the diffuser ducts fully open and the fan running permanently at 7000rpm.</p> \n <p>Ride height has been lowered by 40mm front and rear,&nbsp;oil cooling systems relocated to improve airflow to the rear wing&nbsp;and new brake ducting added to assist with temperature management. Forged&nbsp;magnesium wheels significantly reduce the car’s unsprung mass, but as&nbsp;per Murray's insistence that supercars don't require bespoke tyres, the T50s will ride on&nbsp;Michelin Cup Sport 2s.</p> \n <p>Stripping back the interior has helped shave 94kg compared with the road-going car, with air conditioning, infotainment, storage and sound-deadening materials all removed. Road-going displays have also been removed, with performance-focused information moved to an F1-style rectangular steering wheel.</p> \n <p>The centrally positioned&nbsp;driver's seat has been&nbsp;exchanged for a carbonfibre racing bucket and six-point racing harness, while one of the two passenger seats has been deleted in the name of lightness.</p> \n <p>“With an unwavering focus on performance, and free from road-going legislation and maintenance considerations, the T50s will achieve astonishing performance on track, demonstrating the full extent of the car’s capabilities,\"&nbsp;Murray said. \"We’ve thrown everything at pushing this car beyond the levels of anything that’s been done before. It’s a celebration of British engineering and our team’s extensive motorsport experience.”</p> \n <p>GMA is currently discussing the potential for a GT1 sports club and race series with the SRO Motorsports Group, with Murray's team offering a full range of pit, garage, and support equipment for owners. Owners will receive a 'Trackspeed' customisation pack that includes set-up, training, racing and support, with options to fine-tune suspension and chassis balance to suit their driving style.</p> \n <p>According to the company, the T50s will carry a \"historically significant\" name, which is set to be announced later this year alongside the official reveal of the car. This suggests it could carry the GTR name seen on track-only versions of <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mclaren/f1-1992-1998\">the Murray-penned McLaren F1</a>, to which the T50 is a spiritual successor. There's a chance it will reference the&nbsp;BT46 designation carried by the original Brabham fan car, also designed by Murray.</p> \n <p>The road-going T50 sold out within 48 hours of its official unveilling. Just 100 cars will be built, in the UK, throughout 2022. Production of the 25 racing T50s cars will then follow in early 2023.</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE&nbsp;</strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/gordon-murray-t50-v12-powered-mclaren-f1-successor\">Gordon Murray T50 is V12-powered McLaren F1 successor​</a></strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/gordon-murray-making-£28m-t50-supercar-reality\">Gordon Murray on making the £2.8m T50 supercar a reality​</a></strong></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/opinion/new-cars/why-gordon-murray-t50-could-be-daily-driver\">Why the Gordon Murray T50 could be a daily driver​</a></strong></p> \n <p><span overhaul \n<div> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/hyundai\">Hyundai</a> has given the first official glimpse of the new <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/hyundai/tucson\">Tucson</a> ahead of its unveiling&nbsp;on 15 September, promising a “revolutionary redesign” for the SUV.</p> \n <p>The Korean manufacturer lights’.&nbsp;The&nbsp;daytime running lights are integrated into the grille, with Hyundai saying they will only be visible when switched on.</p> \n <p>The new Tucson's interior showcases Hyundai’s vision of a “dual cockpit layout”, with a large portrait-angled touchscreen built into the centre of the dashboard and minimal use of physical switchgear.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Sangyup Lee, Hyundai’s global Audi also promises sharper handling yet also greater ride comfort, along with a tech-heavy interior.&nbsp;Pricing is expected to start at around the £26,000 mark.</p> \n <p><b><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-audi-a3-saloon-gets-mild-hybrid-and-coupe-looks\">New Audi A3 saloon gets mild hybrid and coupé looks</a></b></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/audi/q5\">Audi E-tron S and E-tron S Sportback</a></p> \n <p>Audi has revealed its first electric S performance models, in the form of a large SUV and its coupé-styled sibling. The E-tron S duo use three electric motors to produce 496bhp.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-audi-e-tron-s-and-e-tron-s-sportback-arrive-hot-electric-suvs\"><strong>New Audi E-tron S and E-tron S Sportback arrive as hot electric SUVs</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/audi/s3\">Audi S3 Sportback and S3 Saloon</a></h3> \n <p>The hot versions of the new A3 hatchback and saloon arrive with a sporty bodykit and&nbsp;306bhp&nbsp;courtesy of the same turbocharged 2.0-litre four-cylinder engine used by the new Cupra Leon and Volkswagen Golf GTI. They'll be followed by an even faster RS3 duo early next year.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-audi-s3-sportback-and-saloon-arrive-306bhp\"><strong>New Audi S3 Sportback and Saloon arrive with 306bhp</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2020-audi-sq7-and-sq8-gain-new-500bhp-petrol-v8\">Audi SQ7 and SQ8 TFSI</a></h3> \n <p>The hot version of the seven-seat Q7 SUV has reverted back to petrol power after a short stint with diesel, while its coupé-influenced, even more upmarket sibling, the SQ8, makes its green-pump debut. Both use a 500bhp&nbsp;<span>twin-turbocharged</span> 4.0-litre V8.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2020-audi-sq7-and-sq8-gain-new-500bhp-petrol-v8\"><strong>2020 Audi SQ7 and SQ8 gain new 500bhp petrol V8&nbsp;</strong></a></p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2020-bmw-4-series-coupe-revealed-dramatic-new-look?page=4\">BMW 4 Series Coupé</a></p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/gallery_slide/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/p90390168.jpg?itok=HOdjIlkB\" /></p> \n <p>Prepare for a grilling: the all-new, second-generation BMW 4 Series is on its way, set to feature that 'controversial' front end seen on the concept car late last year. Once again, the 3 Series-related machine will be available in two-door, four-seat coupé, convertible and four-door Gran Coupé forms.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/first-drive-2020-bmw-4-series-prototype\"><strong>First drive: 2020 BMW 4 Series prototype</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/audi/q5\">BMW X2 facelift</a></h3> \n <p>After three years on sale, BMW is updating its, erm, SAC – that's sports activity coupé, or 'sloped-roof crossover' to you and me. The facelift will introduce styling tweaks and technology upgrades, plus a petrol-electric&nbsp;plug-in hybrid powertrain is set to feature.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/bmw-x2-facelift-bring-styling-tweaks-and-tech-upgrades\"><strong>BMW X2 facelift to bring styling tweaks and tech upgrades</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-citroen-c5-aircross-suv-hybrid-prices-and-specs-revealed\">Citroën C5 Aircross PHEV</a></h3> \n <p>A significant car for the French brand: it’s&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/vehicles/citroen\">Citroën’s</a>&nbsp;first ever plug-in hybrid, and part of a much broader electrification offensive for the PSA Group. Sharing its petrol-electric powertrain with the plug-in&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/vauxhall/grandland-x\">Vauxhall Grandland X</a>&nbsp;and Peugeot 3008 (albeit in a lower-powered form than top models), it makes 222bhp, promises an all-electric range of 31 miles and emits just 39g/km of CO2 officially. UK pricing starts from £35,340.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/citroen/c5-aircross\">Citroën C5 Aircross review</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/cupra-leon-ehybrid-plug-hot-hatch-launched-242bhp\">Cupra Leon and Leon eHybrid</a></h3> \n <p>Newly independent performance brand Cupra has revealed its version of the new Seat Leon – with the option of a plug-in hybrid powertrain. The so-called eHybrid combines a 1.4-litre turbo petrol engine with an electric motor and a 13.1kWh battery, giving it a 37-mile electric-only range. The regular petrol version, available as a hatchback or an estate, comes with 242bhp or 298bhp.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/cupra-leon-ehybrid-plug-hot-hatch-launched-242bhp\"><strong>Cupra Leon eHybrid plug-in hot hatch launched with 242bhp</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/jeep-renegade-plug-hybrid-technical-details-revealed\">Jeep Renegade PHEV</a></h3> \n <p>Jeep’s first plug-in hybrid has a 1.3-litre petrol engine, an electric motor and the promise of 31 miles of electric range. This will use the same twin-turbocharged 4.0-litre V8 engine but match it with an electric motor on the front axle, resulting in four-wheel drive and a 0-62mph time below 3.0sec. Oh, plus super-low official CO2 emissions, and thus BIK tax, thanks to a 31-mile electric-only range. Madness.</span></p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-amg-gt-73-plug-hybrid-teased-new-video\">Mercedes-AMG GT 73 plug-in hybrid teased in new video</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-amg-gt-black-series-sale-%C2%A3335000\">Mercedes-AMG GT Black Series</a></h3> \n <p>Go up through GT, GT C, GT S, GT R, GT R Pro and you finally arrive at the mental GT Black Series. Its twin-turbocharged V8 makes an incredible 720bhp, while its chassis and body gain proper hardcore racing gear. It costs £335,000.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-amg-gt-black-series-sale-%C2%A3335000\">Mercedes-AMG GT Black Series on sale at £335,000</a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-mercedes-e-class-uk-prices-and-specs-announced\">Mercedes-Benz E-Class facelift</a></h3> \n <p>Mercedes has thoroughly updated its executive saloon, estate, coupé and convertible family, with new engines and upgraded technology, plus interiro revisions.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-mercedes-e-class-uk-prices-and-specs-announced\"><strong>New Mercedes-Benz E-Class: UK prices and specs announced</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-maybach-gls-600-arrives-rival-bentley-bentayga\">Mercedes-Maybach GLS</a></h3> \n <p>The German car firm’s luxury brand has reworked the GLS large SUV into an ultra-luxury model designed to compete with the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bentley/bentayga-hybrid/first-drives/bentley-bentayga-hybrid-2020-uk-review\">Bentley Bentayga</a>. Featuring bespoke styling elements and standard 22in wheels, the GLS is powered by a turbocharged 4.0-litre V8 mated to a 48V electrical system, making it a mild hybrid. There’s a major focus on interior luxury, including nappa leather upholstery and – in four-seat guise – even the option of an in-car fridge.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-maybach-gls-600-arrives-rival-bentley-bentayga\">Mercedes-Maybach GLS 600 arrives to rival Bentley Bentayga</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-mg-5-electric-estate-headed-uk-214-mile-range\">MG 5</a></h3> \n <h3><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/gallery_slide/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/mg-5-estate-side.jpg?itok=U6nt5Avs\" /></h3> \n <p>MG plans to import from China a rebadged Roewe model to become the first electric family estate car offered in the UK. It has an official range of 214 miles and will cost around £25,000.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-mg-5-electric-estate-headed-uk-214-mile-range\"><strong>New MG 5 electric estate headed to UK with 214-mile range</strong>&nbsp;</a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/pininfarina-battista-1900bhp-ev-hits-road-new-images\">Pininfarina Battista</a></h3> \n <p>The first offering from&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/pininfarina-battista-how-formula-e-readying-buyers-1900bhp-ev\">Automobili Pininfarina&nbsp;</a>is a 1900bhp ‘halo’ model for a line-up that will stretch from electric hypercars to upmarket performance-themed SUVs. Much of the technology has been developed by the increasingly influential&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mate-rimac-ctwo-progress-and-opening-british-rd-centre\">Rimac</a>, and fine-tuned with input from&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motorsport/formula-e-2019-2020-season-preview\">Formula E</a>&nbsp;racer Nick Heidfeld. It’s said to be the most powerful Italian road car yet, with its makers claiming a 0-62mph time of less than&nbsp;two seconds and a top speed of 217mph.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/pininfarina-battista-1900bhp-ev-hits-road-new-images\">Pininfarina Battista: 1900bhp EV hits the road in new images</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/seat/ateca\">Seat Ateca facelift</a></h3> \n <p>The hugely popular SUV that transformed Seat’s fortunes is set to get its own transformation with a mid-life facelift, which will see the model brought into line with the newer&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/seat/tarraco\">Tarraco</a>&nbsp;and soon-to-launch Leon with mild styling tweaks, greater levels of interior equipment and technology upgrades. The GTAm, meanwhile, gets harnessed carbonfibre front seats and ditches its rears, while adding a massive rear wing.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"http://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/new-alfa-romeo-giulia-gta-firms-most-powerful-model-yet?page=1\">New Alfa Romeo Giulia GTA is firm's most powerful model yet</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/aston-martin-valkyrie-specs-details-pricing\">Aston Martin Valkyrie</a></h3> \n <p>Created with input from Formula 1 design ace Adrian Newey and claimed by&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/aston-martin\">Aston</a>&nbsp;boss Andy Palmer to be capable of lapping Silverstone “as fast as an F1 car”. Power comes from a 6.5-litre&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/slideshow/remembering-icon-ford-sierra-rs-cosworth\">Cosworth</a>-developed V12 engine and a&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mate-rimac-ctwo-progress-and-opening-british-rd-centre\">Rimac</a>-derived electric motor. Sources have suggested the Valkyrie will generate up to 4000lb (1816kg) of downforce at top speed.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/aston-martin-valkyrie-specs-details-pricing\"><strong>Aston Martin Valkyrie: V12 engine sound heard in new video</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/bmw-ix3-electric-suv-spotted-near-production-guise\">BMW iX3</a></h3> \n <p>New electric model will add a zero-emissions option to BMW’s mainstream SUV line-up. Barely disguised prototypes show off a strong resemblance to the conventionally fuelled X3, with visual differences limited primarily to a blanked-off front grille and absent exhaust pipe. Previously revealed technical details indicate that a 70kWh battery pack will offer a range of nearly 250 miles - slightly more than the Audi E-tron - and permanent four-wheel drive is likely to be carried over from the <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/bmw-ix3-electric-suv-spotted-near-production-guise\">2017 iX3 concept</a>.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/bmw-ix3-electric-suv-spotted-near-production-guise\">BMW iX3 electric SUV spotted in near-production guise</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-2020-citroen-c4-cactus-feature-electric-powertrain\">Citroën C4 and ë-C4</a></h3> \n <p>The quirkiest model in Citroën’s current line-up will offer&nbsp;an electric variant in its next generation, as well as petrol and diesel engines. It sits&nbsp;on the same platform as the Corsa of PSA Group sibling Vauxhall, meaning&nbsp;the EV's&nbsp;50kWh battery pack will send power to a 134bhp front-mounted electric motor, giving it a range of 217 miles.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-citroen-c4-electric-e-c4-offer-217-mile-range\"><strong>New 2020 Citroën C4 Cactus: electric ë-C4 to offer 217-mile range</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/new-ds-large-saloon-seen-disguise-first-time\">DS 9&nbsp;</a></h3> \n <p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/ds_3.jpg\" /></p> \n <p>The French luxury brand’s flagship saloon will arrive on the PSA Group’s EMP2 platform, which also underpins the Peugeot 508. The Audi A4 rival&nbsp;shares many design cues with the DS 7 Crossback SUV and offers a 222bhp&nbsp;petrol engine and&nbsp;a range of petrol-electrci plug-in hybrid powertrains with up to 335bhp. These have an electric-only range of up to 31 miles.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-geneva-motor-show/new-ds-9-saloon-takes-aim-audi-a4\">New DS 9 saloon takes aim at Audi A4</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2020-ford-puma-st-hot-crossover-laps-ring-speed\">Ford Puma ST</a></h3> \n <p>It’s not hybrid or pure electric, but Ford’s next ST will rewrite the hot hatchback rulebook by bringing the raw excitement of the celebrated Fiesta ST to the small crossover class. It was always a natural fit for the return of the Puma name that once graced a low-cost but entertaining coupé. Expect a drivetrain similar in execution to the Fiesta’s, with a 197bhp 1.5-litre three-pot engine and, we hope, some of that car’s handling nous.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-ford-puma-sporty-small-suv-revealed-wednesday\">New Ford Puma: sporty small SUV revealed</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jaguar/e-pace\">Jaguar E-Pace facelift</a></h3> \n <p>An early refresh for Jaguar’s smallest&nbsp;SUV, which only arrived in 2018. Expanded safety and driver assistance systems will be the main focus, while the BMW X2 rival will receive a streamlined selection of engines and sharper styling based on the new XE and F-Type. The E-Pace’s interior layout and technology, however, are both still fresh, so we don’t expect to see any radical changes inside.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/jaguar-e-pace-follow-xf-and-f-pace-2020-overhaul\">Jaguar E-Pace to follow XF and F-Pace with 2020 overhaul</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jaguar/f-pace\">Jaguar F-Pace facelift</a></h3> \n <p>Perceived quality and technology upgrades will be the focus of the F-Pace’s 2020 redesign. The SUV is set to benefit from systems first seen in the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jaguar/i-pace\">I-Pace</a>&nbsp;and new mild hybrid engines will be introduced, but don’t expect any radical styling changes. While disguised prototypes clearly show the design influence of the updated&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2020-jaguar-f-type-revealed-revised-looks-no-v6-engine\">F-Type</a>&nbsp;- with slimmer headlights and brakelights - we can see that the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/x5\">BMW X5</a>&nbsp;rival retains key characteristics such as its rising beltline and rakish roofline.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jaguar/f-pace/first-drives/jaguar-f-pace-300-sport-2019-uk-review\"><strong>Jaguar F-Pace 300 Sport 2019 UK review</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jaguar/xf\">Jaguar XF facelift</a></h3> \n <p>Expect changes as significant as the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/jaguar/xe\">XE’s</a>&nbsp;recent mid-life refresh, with cabin upgrades, expanded technology, an evolved exterior appearance and engines that are more efficient, as Jaguar gears up for a renewed attack on the German heavyweights. Instead, the Elva uses an active air management system built into the bonnet that deflects air above the occupants above certain speeds. According to the company, it should reach 62mph in “under three seconds” and can manage 0-124mph in 6.7sec, making it faster than the track-focused <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mclaren/senna\">Senna</a>. The Elva will be limited to just 399 examples and cost from £1.4m.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mclaren-elva-revealed-804bhp-ultimate-series-roadster\">McLaren Elva revealed as 804bhp Ultimate Series roadster</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-eqa-2020-electric-crossover-previewed-new-image\">Mercedes-Benz EQA</a></h3> \n <p>Mercedes’ entry-level EQ model will eschew the hatchback stylings of the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/a-class\">A-Class</a>&nbsp;and instead mimic the popularity and practicality of the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-mercedes-gla-receives-more-tech-space-and-comfort\">GLA</a>&nbsp;crossover. This bodystyle leaves more space under the seats for battery cells without impacting on interior room, thanks to a higher roofline. Little is known about the electric powertrain it will use, other than a predicted range of around 249 miles. It should be priced to compete directly with the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/bmw/i3\">BMW i3</a>, with styling that borrows heavily from the EQC electric SUV.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-eqa-2020-electric-crossover-previewed-new-image\"><strong>Mercedes EQA: 2020 electric crossover previewed in new image</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-frankfurt-motor-show/mercedes-benz-eqv-electric-mpv-makes-debut-frankfurt\">Mercedes-Benz EQV</a></h3> \n <p>With the electric revolution in full swing, it’s unsurprising that Mercedes-Benz, king of filling niches before others, is one of the first to market with an electric luxury (albeit largely van-based) MPV. Based on the well-established&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/mercedes-benz/v-class\">V-Class</a>, the EQV will deliver 252 miles of range and a choice of seating configurations.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-frankfurt-motor-show/mercedes-benz-eqv-electric-mpv-makes-debut-frankfurt\"><strong>Mercedes-Benz EQV: electric MPV makes debut at Frankfurt</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/porsche/911-gt3\">Porsche 911 GT3</a></h3> \n <p>The first 992-generation Porsche to come through the brand’s Motorsport operation&nbsp;at Weissach, the new GT3 is set to use the same naturally aspirated 4.0-litre flat six engine as the limited-run 991-series <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/2019-porsche-911\">911 Speedster</a>. Performance should therefore match or exceed the 503bhp Speedster, with a track-focused suspension setup, large rear wing for increased downforce and an optional manual gearbox on the cards as well.</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/next-gen-porsche-911-gt3-tipped-use-40-litre-flat-six\"><strong>Next-gen Porsche 911 GT3 tipped to use 4.0-litre flat six</strong></a></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-rolls-royce-ghost-firms-most-advanced-model\">Rolls-Royce Ghost</a></h3> \n <p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/gallery_slide/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/rg_00168_3_011-final.jpg?itok=yhYu3fdl\" /></p> \n <p>Rolls-Royce's smaller saloon and best-selling model has entered its second generation, gaining a 'post-opulent' design theme to sit alongside its new Rolls-bespoke aluminium architecture and 6.75-litre V12. Engineers have gone to great efforts to make it even more refined than before – as if it wasn't already near-silent.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-rolls-royce-ghost-firms-most-advanced-model\">New Rolls-Royce Ghost is firm's most advanced model</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/tesla-%E2%80%98plaid%E2%80%99-3-motor-system-coming-model-s-2020%E2%80%99\">Tesla Model S Plaid</a></h3> \n <p>The dual-motor <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/tesla/model-s/performance\">Model S Performance</a> is already capable of 0-60mph in 2.4sec&nbsp;and has a top speed of 162mph, but the recent arrival of Porshce’s Taycan has seen the electric car pioneer head to the Nürburgring in an effort to best its German rival’s lap times. The Model S Plaid (named in reference to classic Mel Brooks comedy Spaceballs) will gain an extra motor, allowing for torque vectoring, and battery capacity will be increased to deliver more performance without sacrificing range. Prototype cars have been spotted with dramatic rear wings, a wider rear track, bigger wheels and&nbsp;lowered suspension, but it is unknown how much will make it through to production.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/tesla-%E2%80%98plaid%E2%80%99-3-motor-system-coming-model-s-2020%E2%80%99\">Tesla ‘Plaid’ three-motor system coming to Model S 'in 2020’</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/industry/analysis-tesla-making-progress-still-faces-challenges\">Tesla Model X Plaid</a></h3> \n <p>Any improvements Tesla makes to the Model S saloon in its goal to best the Porsche Taycan will then be carried across to what is already the fastest-accelerating seven-seater on sale. A range-topping Golf R Plus could then have that output boosted to 350bhp - less than the 400bhp previously rumoured that would have seen it go head to head with&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/mercedes-amg-a45-s-uk-prices-mega-hatch-revealed\">Mercedes-AMG’s A45</a>.</p> \n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-vw-golf-gti-one-four-hot-golfs-launching-2020\">New VW Golf GTI is one of four hot Golfs launching in 2020</a></strong></p> \n <h3><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/volvo-reveals-xc40-recharge-first-full-electric-model\">Volvo XC40 P8 Recharge</a></h3> \n <p>The Swedish brand’s first EV takes the immensely popular XC40 and swaps the conventional powertrain for a 201bhp electric motor mounted to each axle. 16:50:43","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:43","title":"New Volkswagen ID 3: first examples of EV hit British shores","link":"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-volkswagen-id-3-first-examples-ev-hit-british-shores","description":"<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/new-volkswagen-id-3-first-examples-ev-hit-british-shores\"><img src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/car_review_image_190/public/images/car-reviews/first-drives/legacy/the_first_id.3_drives_off_the_ship.jpg?itok=BFmVG5CH\" width=\"190\" height=\"125\" alt=\"Volkswagen ID 3 lands at UK port\" title=\"Volkswagen ID 3 lands at UK port\" /></a> First batch of First Edition ID 3 models land in Grimsby port ahead of customer deliveries of electric hatchback \n<div> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-reviews/volkswagen\">Volkswagen's</a> pivotal EV, the <a href=\"http://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/id-3/first-drives/volkswagen-id-3-2020-review\">ID 3</a>, has finally reached British shores as the first customer examples roll off the ship at Grimsby port.&nbsp;</p> \n <p>Earmarked for customers that pre-booked First Edition examples earlier this year, the fully-loaded models will be delivered over the next month. Volkswagen claims that the entire production and delivery process is carbon neutral, even including the shipping.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/id-3/first-drives/volkswagen-id-3-2020-review\"><strong>Autocar's Volkswagen ID 3 2020 review</strong></a></p> \n <p>The limited-run First Edition models are priced&nbsp;from £38,880&nbsp;and were&nbsp;offered only to people who&nbsp;previously placed a £750 deposit. First Edition versions of the ID 3 will feature the mid-size 'Pro' battery offering a claimed range of 260 miles, and will feature special badges and extra kit. Buyers will also be offered 2000kWh of charging via We Charge, which Volkswagen claims is enough for 34 rapid charges and worth around £500.</p> \n <p>General sales of the ID 3&nbsp;are due to begin in the UK in the coming weeks, and the model will eventually be offered in seven main variants, with three different battery capacities and two power outputs.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"600\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/the_first_truck_leaves_port_with_customer_id.3_1st_editions.jpg?itok=R2WoOvJX\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The late stages of the ID 3's development has been hit by&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/volkswagen-id-3-delays-continue-software-problems-pile\">well-publicised&nbsp;software issues</a>, and the early cars delivered to customers in September will be without a number of software features, including the&nbsp;augmented-reality functions for the car's head-up display (although these won't be&nbsp;offered on initial UK models)&nbsp;and some of&nbsp;the App Connect features.</p> \n <p>The first machines that have arrived in Britain will be without some of the App Connect, but those who take delivery of them will be given membership of a 'First Movers' club, which will include an eventual software update to install the software. Those leasing cars also won't pay any rates for the first three months.</p> \n <p>Speaking about the decision to launch the car before the full software system is available, Silke Bagschik, Volkswagen's e-mobility sales chief, said: \"The software is&nbsp;not yet up to Volkswagen standards that we want to give to customers, but we wanted to give them the option of having the car and enjoying the driving experience of it as much as we are. And we will upgrade all the software when it's ready.\"</p> \n <p>The electric hatchback will eventually be offered with three&nbsp;battery&nbsp;capacities and two power outputs. The First Edition model&nbsp;will use the mid-size 'Pro' 58kWh battery for&nbsp;a claimed range of 260 miles.&nbsp;It <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-review/volkswagen/id-3/first-drives/volkswagen-id-3-2020-review\">will offer 201bhp driven through the rear wheels</a>, 229lb ft of torque and a top speed of 99mph. The car can be charged through a 100kW DC connection or a 11kW AC system.</p> \n <p><span>The mid-size Pro battery will eventually be offered with two power outputs, with a lower 143bhp version that will be aorund two seconds slower to reach 0-62mph.&nbsp;</span></p> \n <p><span>The 45kWh Pure battery will be offered with outputs of 125bhp and 148bhp, while the largest 77kWh Pro S battery will use the 201bhp motor. Because of the extra weight of the battery, the&nbsp;Pro S model will only be offered with a four-seat layout.</span></p> \n <p>In Germany, the ID 3 First will be offered in three trim levels –&nbsp;basic, Plus and Max - although only the mid-level version will intially be offered in the UK.</p> \n <p>The ID 3 First cars offered in the UK will feature 19in alloy wheels, 30-colour ambient lighting, heated seat and steering wheel, and matrix LED front and LED rear lights. The First models will feature&nbsp;an Exterior Style Silver pack featuring a silver roofline and grey sills and bumpers. Buyers can choose from four exterior colours and three interior schemes.</p> \n <p><img alt=\"\" class=\"image-body-image\" height=\"601\" src=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/sites/autocar.co.uk/files/styles/body-image/public/id.3_1st_editions_being_unloaded_at_port_4.jpg?itok=eoRhpCR6\" width=\"900\" /></p> \n <p>The UK-bound models also come with a rear-view camera as standard, along with automatic cruise control, rear privacy glass and an anti-theft alarm. Notably, the mid-level ID 3 First models that will be offered in the UK at launch don't&nbsp;come with the top-level cockpit infotainment system that includes the head-up display. That means the only software upgrade UK buyers will require will be for&nbsp;the full App Connect features.</p> \n <p>General ordering for the ID 3 for those who haven't pre-booked will open four weeks after the car first goes on sale. Volkswagen has yet to outline trim levels and pricing for those models, or when various power levels and battery sizes will be introduced.</p> \n <p>Volkswagen offered a pre-ordering service for the ID 3 First, with more than 35,000 customers worldwide <a href=\"https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/motor-shows-frankfurt-motor-show/volkswagen-id-3-electric-nissan-leaf-rival-be-revealed\">placing a refundable deposit</a>. Those who placed a deposit in continental Europe were able to buy their cars from 17 June onwards. The delay in the UK was due to the&nbsp;extra time required to gain type approval for right-hand-drive versions.</p> \n <p><span>Volkswagen sales boss Jürgen Stackmann</span>&nbsp;claimed&nbsp;that Volkswagen was still aiming to meet its target of building 100,000 ID 3s this year&nbsp;but that it might be unable to fully recover from the extended shutdown in the second half of the year.</p> \n <p>Prices for the ID 3 in the UK will eventually start from around £27,500 before the government grant&nbsp;for the entry-level 45kWh Pure version.&nbsp;</p> \n <p><strong>READ MORE</strong></p> \n electric vehicle (such as the Zoe) further down the line.They all make use of the same normally aspirated 1.6-litre four-cylinder petrol engine, which is paired with a smaller electric motor and an integrated starter-generator.
